The structure of Reyes attachment is not "Gabe is the only one he loves"; the deeper finding is "Reyes has only one slot, and it is occupied." Whether by Gabe or by an empty-Gabe-shaped space, the slot is non-transferable.

The remission collapses as the series progresses: the Rider returns (the suppression was a containment, not a cure), Eli's voice returns, and a new antagonist (the **Hayden's Falls killer / "Mister Hyde"-adjacent figures and the cult known as the Scarlet Solomon**, depending on which arc) forces transformation. Robbie's reaction to recovering the memory of being Ghost Rider is, characteristically, **not relief and not horror — but resigned recognition.** He responds as a man returning to a job he had forgotten was his. The affective signature is closer to "shift change" than to "awakening."

A critical mid-run development: Robbie learns that his amnesia was bargained for in part to keep Gabe safer at a distance — i.e., even the experiment in normalcy was constructed around Gabe's welfare. The slot was never empty. It was just being protected by being held at arm's length.

By the run's conclusion, Talia is either lost to him or held at a distance he himself imposes; the Hayden's Falls life is dismantled; Robbie is back on the road in the Charger, alone, heading west. **Heading home.**

---

## 3. The Re-Domesticated Vengeance (post-Percy, current status)

Across the most recent appearances — Spirits-of-Vengeance ensemble cameos, the *Blood Hunt* tie-in periphery, and the small handful of post-Percy guest panels — Robbie is back in the East L.A. operating envelope:

- **Domicile:** the apartment with Gabe (or its replacement; the specific building has shifted at least once across runs, but the configuration — small, rented, walking distance to the garage, modified for wheelchair access by Robbie himself — is constant).
- **Employment:** Canelo's Auto and Body, when Canelo's exists as written; otherwise an equivalent independent body shop. He has never, across two decades of in-universe and out-of-universe time, held a job that was not mechanic work. This is identity-level, not economic.
- **Vehicle:** the Charger. Modifications have accreted over the years, all hand-done. The car carries the cosmetic memory of every fight: panel-beat repairs, a replaced quarter-panel, a hood that has been pulled and re-set. He will not let another mechanic touch it.
- **Gabe:** older now, in the present-day window — late adolescent / young adult range, depending on the writer. The relational dynamic has begun to drift: Gabe is more independent, more aware of the secret, more willing to push back. This is a developmentally appropriate change in any sibling relationship; for Robbie, it is a slow-motion identity crisis. His leash on the Rider is loosening *not because Gabe is in danger, but because Gabe is growing up.*
- **Eli:** still present. The internal voice has not been exorcised in any durable way. Surveillance read: Eli has, if anything, become *quieter and more strategic.* The pattern in current appearances is fewer outbursts and more long-game suggestions — fewer "kill him" prompts, more "you could have done that better." This is the more dangerous configuration. A pushing voice is recognizable; a counseling voice is harder to refuse.

---

## 4. The Drift of the Equilibrium

The most important pattern across the recent period is not any single event but the **directional drift of Robbie's stabilizing structure.** Each pillar of his equilibrium is under quiet pressure simultaneously:

1. **Gabe's increasing autonomy** is removing the load-bearing caretaker identity in slow, age-appropriate increments. Robbie has no plan for what happens on the day Gabe does not need him to lift him, drive him, or shield him.
2. **Eli's modal shift** from outburst-pusher to advisor-voice represents a deeper integration, which the file flags as a regression from the early years — when the boundary between Robbie and Eli was clear and policed. The boundary is softening.
3. **The romantic experiment (Talia) failed**, and failed in a way Robbie can read as evidence for his contamination self-schema. The attempt, the failure, and the retreat together constitute a closed loop that confirms the negative cognition rather than disconfirming it.
4. **The cosmic résumé continues to grow** (former King of Hell, Avengers alum, Starbrand-adjacent veteran), in direct contradiction to his preferred self-concept (local mechanic, brother, nobody). The gap between how the Marvel universe at large now reads him and how he reads himself is widening. He is becoming, against his will, a figure other heroes call when the problem requires hellfire — and every such call is a small erosion of the local-and-anonymous identity he has fought to keep.
5. **The garage as physical container** is itself precarious. Across the runs Canelo's has been threatened by gang incursion, by gentrification subtext, by the simple economics of an independent shop. Robbie's physical workspace — the single most important psychological appliance in his life — is not guaranteed.

The current state, then, is not crisis but **pre-crisis.** Robbie is functioning. He is at the bench, at the apartment, at Gabe's side. The Rider runs when called. Eli is quiet. The system is, on the surface, stable. But every one of the system's load-bearing members is under tension, and the file's central concern about Robbie has always been that his containment of the Rider is single-point-of-failure architecture: Gabe is the leash.

---

## 5. Present-Day Surveillance Profile (granular)

For the period covering the most recent twelve to eighteen months of in-universe time, the following micro-patterns are observable and confirmed across appearances:

- **Daily route.** Apartment → Gabe's morning routine (dressing, breakfast, transfer to chair, school or program drop-off where applicable) → walk or short drive to Canelo's → shop floor until early evening → grocery or pharmacy stop (he does the household errands; Gabe does not) → home → dinner cooked by Robbie (rotation of four or five dishes, all cheap, all assembled in under thirty minutes) → Gabe's evening routine → late hours in the garage or in the apartment kitchen with engine parts on a towel. Sleep window is short and irregular.
- **Phone discipline.** Minimal. He carries a phone because Gabe might need him. He does not maintain social-media presence under his own name. Contact list is short: Gabe, Canelo, two or three garage regulars, an emergency contact for Gabe's medical needs. Hero-network contacts (a number for Blaze, a number for one or two Avengers from the Waid/Aaron era) are stored but rarely dialed and almost never answered when they call him.
- **Dress.** Unchanged for years. Dark jeans, white or grey t-shirt, work jacket or hoodie, mechanic's boots. The skull-pattern hoodie that became iconographically associated with him in the Smith run still appears intermittently; he wears it in cold weather or when expecting trouble. The hoodie is, in effect, a transitional object — a piece of the visual identity that bridges Robbie-on-foot and Ghost-Rider-at-the-wheel.
- **Eating.** Fast, standing, often while doing something else. He cooks for Gabe with care and patience; he feeds himself like a man closing a ticket.
- **Sleep.** Restless. Light. Patterned around Gabe's wake-needs. He sleeps in his clothes more often than not. The Charger's keys are within arm's reach of the bed.
- **Body language baseline.** Quiet hands, low voice, eye contact made and held briefly then released, weight slightly forward — ready to move. He does not occupy more space than he needs. In a room with strangers he positions himself near an exit and with sightline to any child or disabled person present.
- **Speech.** Spanish and English code-switched fluently; Spanish reserved for family, neighborhood elders, and prayer-adjacent moments. English for work and for outsiders. Profanity is moderate, situational, not affective. He does not raise his voice. When he does, the file notes it: it is almost always a tell that Eli is at the surface.
- **Transformation triggers, current threshold.** The threshold has *lowered* in the recent period relative to the early years — a function of Eli's deeper integration and of accumulated chronic stress. Where in the Smith run it took an existential threat to Gabe to bring the skull on, in the present period proximate threat to any child, any disabled person, or any clearly defenseless target will produce ignition. This is not a moral softening; it is a containment loosening. He himself appears not to have fully registered the shift.
- **Tells of imminent transformation, observable from outside.** Stillness rather than agitation. A long exhalation. A specific habit of removing the hoodie or jacket if time permits (preserving Gabe's clothes from burn damage — a small, telling vanity of caretaking, given that he otherwise treats his own body as expendable). A quiet word in Spanish, often inaudible, that the file reads as either a prayer or a request for forgiveness directed at Gabe. Then the eyes go.
- **Post-transformation behavior.** Silence. Immediate physical relocation away from witnesses. Mechanical inspection of the Charger before any self-inspection. A long shower, alone, with the bathroom door locked. No verbal processing. He does not, ever, debrief.

---

## 6. The Question the File Cannot Yet Answer

The recent period closes with one diagnostic question the surveillance record cannot yet resolve, and which the file flags as the **single most important variable for any future assessment of this subject**:

> **What does Robbie Reyes do on the day Gabe no longer needs a caretaker?**

Every other variable in this file — Eli, the Charger, the Avengers Rolodex, the cosmic résumé, the failed romantic experiment, the slowly eroding garage — is downstream of that question. The recent history has been a series of small system-tests, conducted by the universe and by the writers, of what happens when one of Robbie's pillars wobbles. None of them have wobbled the central one. When it wobbles — and the developmental arithmetic suggests it will, within a measurable window — the file's expectation is that Robbie will attempt, with characteristic procedural quiet, to **construct a new dependent.** Another vulnerable person, another at-risk teen, another stray. He will not seek therapy. He will not call the Avengers. He will look for someone to protect, because protection is the only relational grammar he has.

If he finds one, the equilibrium holds, on new terms.

If he does not, the leash slips, and the file's earliest warning — that Eli is patient, and that Robbie's containment is single-point-of-failure — becomes the operative concern.

For now: he is in East Los Angeles. He is at the garage. Gabe is at the apartment. The Charger is in the bay. The skull is quiet. The voice in his head is, currently, only suggesting.

The file remains open.


## Medical History

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 2 — MEDICAL HISTORY

*Compiled from observed canon, dialogue-inferred history, and somatic patterns consistent across the writers of record (Smith, Waid, Aaron, Cates, Percy). What follows is the longitudinal body-file: every wound, every system, every substance, every transformation, and what each did to the man inside the body.*

---

### 2.1 Constitutional Baseline (Pre-Resurrection)

**Demographics at time of death.** Male, Latino (Mexican-American), late adolescent (approximately seventeen to eighteen years old at the events of *All-New Ghost Rider* #1). Height in the median range for a young adult male of his background — file estimate 5'9"–5'10". Build: lean, wiry, mesomorphic at the upper end of ectomorphic; the body of a teenager doing forty to sixty hours a week of garage labor on inadequate sleep and inadequate calories rather than the body of a teenager who lifts. Resting heart rate consistent with someone whose cardiovascular load comes from chronic low-grade sympathetic activation (vigilance) rather than from athletic training.

**Skin and surface findings.** Multiple low-grade dermatological markers of his work and his neighborhood: callusing on the palmar surfaces of both hands at the thenar eminence and along the proximal phalanges of the index and middle fingers (wrench grip, ratchet grip); permanent darkening at the cuticles and nail beds from engine grease that no degreaser fully evicts; small scattered burn-scars on the dorsum of both forearms in the pattern characteristic of working over a hot manifold without sleeves (exhaust contact burns, second-degree, healed without intervention); a faint linear scar at the left eyebrow, old enough to have faded; a small cluster of scars on the back and upper arms whose distribution does not match accidental injury and whose presence is consistent with childhood corporal abuse from the father (this is inferred — not catalogued on-panel — but the geometry is forensically familiar). Tattoos: none. Piercings: none. This is a body that does not advertise.

**Dental.** Estimated poor-to-fair. No documented dental care in the household economic profile. Likely untreated caries, likely never wore braces despite a probably-noticeable malocclusion. Functional but neglected.

**Vision and hearing.** Both within functional limits on the record. No corrective lenses. No documented hearing loss despite chronic exposure to compressor noise, impact wrenches, and street traffic.

**Cardiopulmonary.** No documented asthma despite East L.A. air quality and constant brake-dust / solvent exposure. Aerobic capacity adequate; he runs when he has to and does not gas. No murmurs, no arrhythmias on record.

**Endocrine / developmental.** Pubertal maturation completed. No documented endocrine pathology. Stature consistent with the family male phenotype.

**Nutrition.** Chronic marginal food insecurity is the file's working assumption. Robbie's feeding pattern, as observed across early issues, is irregular, calorie-dense convenience food taken on the move, often deferred so that Gabe eats first. Likely micronutrient-poor: low fresh produce intake, low dairy except as a vehicle for cereal, high carbohydrate, moderate fat, animal protein primarily from cheap cuts and processed sources. There is no clinical malnutrition — he is functional — but the household profile is the profile of a teenager feeding a disabled minor on what a part-time mechanic-apprentice salary stretches to cover after rent. Hydration: poor; he drinks water from the shop tap and the rest of his fluid intake is soda or coffee.

**Sleep.** Chronically insufficient. The schedule alone — school day, shop hours, Gabe's nighttime care needs, household maintenance, the street-race side hustle — does not admit more than five to six hours, often broken. Sleep architecture is the file's working answer to several otherwise-puzzling baseline phenomena: the flat affect, the tonic vigilance, the high pain tolerance, the speed with which he abandons social engagement when not strictly necessary. He was already chronically activated and chronically under-rested before any of the supernatural began.

**Activity.** Occupational rather than recreational. Manual labor, ambulation, lifting, carrying Gabe and Gabe's wheelchair, pushing same up curb cuts and into vehicles. No gym attendance. No team sports. The fight-readiness he later displays is not athletically prepared; it is street-readiness — short, decisive, defensive.

**Substance history, baseline.** This is one of the most diagnostic facts on the page. **Robbie does not drink, does not smoke, does not use.** He is embedded in a neighborhood and a labor environment in which alcohol, tobacco, cannabis, and harder substances are normalized and continuously offered. He refuses, consistently and without commentary, across the entire run. This is not a religious abstinence and not a recovery abstinence — it is an identity abstinence. He has organized his sense of self around *not becoming* the man who hit him and not becoming the men who run the block. The body is therefore, at baseline, an unusually clean teenage male body: no nicotine staining, no liver insult, no THC-related cognitive baseline, no opioid tolerance, no stimulant burn. This will matter later, because when foreign substances are forced on him — chemical or supernatural — he has no learned tolerance to absorb them.

**Caretaking-load somatic signature.** Lower-back hypertonicity from lifting Gabe in and out of chair, car, bath; bilateral trapezius and levator scapulae tension; the postural shoulders-forward of someone who spends his free hours leaning over an engine bay or a wheelchair handle. He likely has the beginnings of mechanical low-back pain that an older Robbie, in any future where he gets one, would be treating chronically.

---

### 2.2 The Terminal Event (*All-New Ghost Rider* #1–2)

The originating medical event is a homicide. Robbie, in flight from Hyde's enforcers after stumbling into the wrong cargo, is run down and executed at close range. Multiple gunshot wounds to the torso, point-blank, several to center mass, at least one to the head in the strongest reading of the panel. There is no recovery from the wounds as inflicted; he is, by any clinical or legal definition, **killed**.

This is a fact the file requires you to hold with both hands. The body that walks out of the desert in issue #2 is not a body that survived a trauma. It is a body that died and was reoccupied. Every subsequent medical entry in this file is an entry on a corpse that is being driven.

**Acute injuries at death:** multiple penetrating ballistic wounds, hypovolemic shock, exsanguination, cardiac arrest, anoxic brain injury sufficient to terminate consciousness. Time from injury to death: short. Time from death to resurrection: short, but non-zero — he experienced the gap.

**Psychological residue of the killing itself.** This is the load-bearing trauma of his life, and it does not present as classical flashback. Robbie does not, on-panel, narrate the moment of being shot. What he does is *avoid the topic structurally* — he will not talk about how the Rider arrived, will not narrate his death to teammates, deflects when Gabe edges near the question. The avoidance *is* the symptom. His body, however, re-experiences. The transformation itself is a somatic restaging of catastrophic bodily violation: fire where the bullets went in, agency-loss as a redo of the agency-loss of being shot. He died non-consensually and he transforms non-consensually, and the second is the first played in a different key.

---

### 2.3 Post-Resurrection Somatic Profile

Robbie's body, post-event, is not a human body with augmentations. It is a human-form vessel maintained by two non-human tenants — the bound ghost of Eli Morrow and a Spirit of Vengeance — operating through human tissue that has been rendered self-repairing and threshold-tolerant. What follows is a system-by-system map of how that vessel behaves.

**Regenerative capacity.** Robbie now closes wounds that should kill him. The repair appears to be hellfire-mediated; observed across runs, he survives lacerations, blunt trauma, ballistic re-injury, burns inflicted by other supernatural sources, falls from height, and dismemberment-tier insults sustained in cosmic-scale combat. The rate of repair is variable and appears tied to the Rider's presence: in transformed state, near-instantaneous; in human form, accelerated relative to baseline but not miraculous. He still bruises. He still bleeds, briefly. He still feels every injury. The repair is *not analgesia* — and the file's reading is that the persistence of pain through a body that no longer fears death is one of the most psychologically corrosive facts of his condition. He hurts as a man and heals as a thing.

**Cardiopulmonary in transformed state.** Heart rate and respiration become observationally irrelevant during transformation. He does not need to breathe within the Rider envelope, by inference from sustained exposure to fire, vacuum-adjacent conditions in cosmic arcs, and submersion incidents. In human form, both return to baseline.

**Thermoregulation.** Profoundly altered. The skull and hands generate hellfire; the body radiates extreme heat during and after transformation. He runs warm in human form — handshake-warm, touch-warm — and ambient cold does not affect him as it should. He has not been observed to shiver. Conversely, he does not appear to sweat in the normal manner; thermal load discharges through the Rider rather than through eccrine cooling. He is, in cold-weather settings, the only person in the room without a jacket who is not performing.

**Pain processing.** Pain is preserved. The transformation does not anesthetize him; if anything it heightens the somatic noise of being injured, because Eli experiences the body's pain and comments on it. Robbie's high pain tolerance, then, is not neurological — it is *trained dissociation*, a learned silence that predates the Rider and that the Rider has scaled.

**Sleep.** Worse than before. Transformation episodes appear to substitute, neurologically, for some part of restorative sleep — but only some part. Eli's voice is most present in the hypnagogic and hypnopompic states, and Robbie reports (in oblique dialogue) waking unrested. The file estimates four to five hours of fragmented sleep on a good night, less on operational nights. Chronic insomnia is the working diagnosis under the supernatural overlay.

**Appetite and nutrition.** Reduced. He eats less than a teenage male doing his work should eat. The Rider appears to provide a portion of his energetic needs through a non-metabolic channel. He does not refuse food, but he forgets it. He still eats with Gabe — and the file flags this as ritual rather than nutrition. Eating with Gabe is a sacrament of normalcy; eating alone he does not bother.

**Sensory.** Threat perception is heightened in human form and acute in transformed form. There is a documented sin-perception capacity (the "Penance Stare"-analog) — he can read, on contact or gaze, the moral weight of an act done by the person before him. The phenomenology of this is not given on-panel in clinical detail, but the behavioral correlate is unambiguous: Robbie sometimes looks at people and *winces*, briefly, and the wince is data. He is seeing something the rest of the room is not. This is corrosive over time — there is no observed capacity to *turn it off* — and the file flags it as a likely contributor to his social withdrawal. To be among people is to be reading them, involuntarily.

**Vehicular integration (the Charger).** The single strangest line in this file. The 1969 Dodge Charger is somatically tethered to Robbie. Damage to the car correlates with damage to him; absence from the car correlates with degraded access to the Rider; the car repairs itself in concert with him. Functionally, the vehicle is a prosthetic organ external to the body envelope — an exoskeletal heart that he can park in a driveway. He works on the car obsessively and the work is not maintenance, it is *self-care he can perform with his hands*. Stripping a head gasket from the Charger is, for him, what stretching or meditation would be for someone whose body was their own.

**Hellfire chain.** Manifested at need. The chain is sometimes produced from the hand, sometimes from the chest, sometimes wielded as if drawn from the car. It is hot to the touch of others; he handles it without burn. He has been observed binding, striking, and tearing with it. He does not appear to practice with it. The skill arrives in his hand the way the transformation arrives in his skull — *given*, not learned.

**Hellfire generation and projection.** Pyrokinesis is contextual rather than continuous: under threat, on command of the Rider, and in moments of high affect. Robbie has *never*, on the record, used the hellfire frivolously — not for warmth, not for light, not for show. The discipline around this is total and is psychologically diagnostic: he treats the fire as a contaminant that he refuses to spread.

**The "Penance Stare"-analog / sin-burning gaze.** Used sparingly. Each use appears to cost him something — not energetically, but morally; the act of being inside another mind's worst hours is a weight he visibly carries afterward. He does not enjoy this. The file's read is that the gaze functions for him the way a confessional functions for a priest who never asked to be a priest: he is being told things he cannot un-hear.

---

### 2.4 The Internal Tenant: Eli

The most consequential ongoing medical fact in Robbie's body is that he is not alone in it. Eli Morrow's bound consciousness is co-resident, persistent in waking life as an intrusive second voice, and capable — under the conditions of transformation, unconsciousness, or extreme duress — of assuming gross motor control.

**Phenomenology of Eli's presence.** A discrete other-voice, contextually responsive, with stable identity, consistent affect (mocking, urging, sometimes wheedling, almost always pushing toward escalation and lethality). The voice is not Robbie's voice in a different register; it is heard as not-his. It comments on his decisions in real time, particularly his moral decisions; it offers tactical advice that is usually correct and ethical advice that is invariably corrosive.

**Differential, restated for the medical file.** This presentation is *not* primary auditory hallucination, *not* DID, *not* a thought-disorder symptom. The Marvel canon establishes Eli as a discrete ontological entity. The clinical point, however, is that the *experience* of co-habitation produces dissociative and quasi-psychotic symptoms that would be treated as such if the metaphysics were stripped away — and that Robbie has no access to either pharmacological or psychotherapeutic relief, because the entity is real and a clinician would be treating the wrong target.

**Behavioral coping.** Robbie talks back to Eli internally and, rarely, aloud — usually when alone, in the garage, under the car. He refuses Eli's commands as a discipline; he reports (by behavior, not dialogue) that the refusal is exhausting. The refusal is the spinal practice of his life. It is also why he is tired.

**Decompensation risk.** If Gabe is removed from the picture, the refusal-engine loses its rationale. The medical prognosis under that scenario is grim: Eli's leverage increases, transformation thresholds drop, and the moral filter that keeps the Rider from being a mass-casualty event would erode within a short clinical window. The file recommends, in any future surveillance posture, that Gabe's welfare be tracked as a leading indicator of Robbie's containment.

---

### 2.5 Post-Resurrection Injury Log (illustrative, not exhaustive)

A partial chronology of significant somatic insults survived since the originating death. The pattern of interest is not the survival — that is now stipulated — but the *psychological aftermath* of each.

- **Repeat ballistic wounds, Catrina and Hyde-affiliated incidents (early *All-New Ghost Rider*).** Robbie is shot again, more than once, in his first months as Rider. The first re-shooting is the somatic confirmation that the original killing can be repeated and survived. The psychological data point: he does not become reckless. He becomes *more avoidant.* He treats each survival as a debt accrued, not a license extended.

- **Blunt-force trauma from Hyde and from Grumpy.** Sustained beatings at superhuman force levels. Survived. Aftermath: increased concealment from Gabe (won't take off his shirt at home), increased withdrawal.

- **Eli's body-jump and the Gabe-possession crisis.** Not a tissue injury but a violation of relational integrity. Robbie's signature resolution — reabsorbing Eli rather than harming Gabe — is, in medical terms, a deliberate *re-contamination*. He chose to take the parasite back. Recovery: incomplete; the file reads this as the moment Robbie's caretaker identity locked in as the only stable container for the Eli problem.

- **Cosmic-tier injuries (Aaron's *Avengers*, *Damnation*).** Robbie sustains damage at scales that would atomize a baseline human — Celestial-adjacent forces, infernal warfare, exposure to entities like the One Below All. Survived through Rider regeneration. Psychological aftermath: he wants to go home. The cosmic does not enlarge him; it estranges him from the only scale at which his identity functions. He returns to the garage as a man returns from a war he never agreed to fight.

- **Hell-time and abdication arcs (Cates run and after).** Robbie spends subjectively-extended periods in Hell, briefly occupies the throne, abdicates. Time-distortion injury: he comes back having lived longer than he aged. The body is the same. The interior is older. The file reads several of his later silences as the silence of someone carrying time his body cannot account for.

- **Solo run injuries (Percy era and subsequent).** Continued accumulation of supernatural insults, possessions, infernal wounds. None permanent in tissue; all permanent in self-concept. The graph of his physical survivability is rising; the graph of his felt safety is flat or falling.

**Medical care received for any of the above: effectively none.** No hospital admissions on the record. No interaction with the formal medical system post-resurrection. He does not present at emergency departments. He does not accept on-team medical attention from Avengers infrastructure, even when offered. He treats his own minor injuries in the shop bathroom with shop supplies. The refusal of care is *not* paranoia about exposure of the Rider — or not only that. It is the same operational discipline that runs the rest of him: do not be seen, do not be helped, do not be in anyone's record.

---

### 2.6 Disabilities

Robbie has no formally recognized disability. The file flags, nonetheless, two functional impairments worth naming.

**First**, the chronic sleep deficit and the chronic intrusive-voice load amount to a working cognitive impairment of a low-grade, persistent kind — the kind that does not show up on testing because he has learned to perform around it, but that costs him in latency, in mood, in the small social fluencies he can no longer summon. He is sharp on task and slow off it. He has lost some bandwidth he is unlikely to recover while Eli is in residence.

**Second**, his affective range is functionally constricted to a degree that, in a civilian context, would meet criteria for clinical concern. He does not laugh easily. He does not weep on the record. He does not flirt. He does not perform delight. The full middle of human feeling is, for him, either suppressed or unavailable. This is not a metaphysical fact; it is a sequela of cumulative trauma, and it is treatable in principle and untreated in practice.

Gabe's disability is not Robbie's, but it is medically relevant to Robbie's file: it is the organizing constraint of his life, the reason he works the shifts he works, the reason he cannot move, the reason he cannot accept the away-missions other heroes accept without thought. Gabe's wheelchair and developmental profile structure Robbie's calendar, Robbie's geography, and Robbie's risk tolerance. Any medical-history reading of Robbie that omits Gabe's body is reading the wrong file.

---

### 2.7 Surgeries, Procedures, Hospitalizations

None on the record, pre- or post-resurrection. He has never been intubated. He has never been sutured by a clinician. He has never had anesthesia. He has never been catheterized, scanned, or imaged. He is, in the most literal sense, a medical ghost — there is no chart on him anywhere, and the resurrection means there never will be one that matches the body in the room.

The single procedural event of his life is the resurrection itself, performed without consent, by an agent that did not introduce itself, on a corpse in the desert. It is the only intervention his body has received. Everything since has been him, alone, in a bathroom mirror, with shop-grade gauze.

---

### 2.8 Substances

**Alcohol:** none, pre- or post-event. Offered repeatedly; declined.

**Tobacco:** none.

**Cannabis:** none, despite ubiquity in his environment.

**Stimulants:** caffeine, moderate to heavy. Black coffee, gas-station drip, taken throughout the day. The one functional dependency on his record, and the one he would notice if it were removed.

**Opioids / benzodiazepines / hallucinogens:** none, voluntary or prescribed.

**Pharmaceuticals, prescribed:** none on the record.

**Supernatural exposures functioning as substance-analogs:**
- *Eli's voice* — the chronic exposure. Functions as a disinhibitor and a craving-pusher in the structure of an addiction (urge, refusal, occasional slip, shame cycle). Robbie's relationship to Eli is, behaviorally, the relationship of a person in long-term recovery to a substance they cannot put down because it lives in their head.
- *Hellfire* — episodic, internally generated, refused as a casual tool. Robbie's discipline around the fire is the discipline of a man who has decided the substance will not become recreational.
- *Hell-adjacent environments and infernal energies* — exposures sustained across the cosmic arcs. Cumulative residue is implied by the deepening of his withdrawal and the slow darkening of his affect across runs.

The pattern across the substance section is consistent: he refuses the things that would dull him, accepts only the thing (coffee) that keeps him awake for Gabe, and carries the supernatural exposures as untreated chronic conditions because there is no clinic for what he has.

---

### 2.9 Synthesizing Note for the Medical File

Robbie Reyes presents as a teenage corpse maintained in apparent health by two non-human tenants, walking around a neighborhood, going to work, raising a child. His body's history can be told in two columns: the column of injuries his flesh has taken, and the column of injuries his self-concept has taken from being a body that survives what bodies do not. The first column is long and largely unscarred. The second column is the one this file is actually about.

He has never been treated. He has never asked to be. He treats the fact of his medical exceptionality the way he treats every other fact about himself — as a thing to be hidden so that Gabe can eat breakfast in a kitchen that does not contain a monster. The medical recommendation, were any clinician ever to get him in a room, would be straightforward and almost certainly refused: sleep, food, weight off the caretaking load, a confidential interlocutor, and the slow, patient work of


## Somatic Atlas

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section VI — SOMATIC ATLAS

> *The body keeps the receipts.* What follows is the granular bodily record — every habituated motion, micro-gesture, postural set, and somatic tell — observed and inferred across the canonical record (2014 onward). Each entry is calibrated to baseline and then re-plotted across the four operating states: **CALM** (garage, Gabe present, no observers), **STRESS** (school, public, Avengers tower, surveillance pressure), **THREAT** (acute danger to self or to a dependent), and **INTIMACY** (the very narrow band — Gabe primarily, Canelo secondarily — where the defenses partially lower).

---

### 1. Build, Carriage, and the General Envelope

Subject is a Latino male, late adolescence at first observation, measuring approximately 5'9"–5'10", lean-muscled in the wiry, work-acquired way rather than the gym-acquired way: forearms disproportionately developed (mechanic's wrench-and-torque musculature), shoulders carried slightly forward, latissimus and trapezius taut from chronic lifting of a wheelchair-bound dependent in and out of a vehicle, bath, bed. Hands are large for the frame, calloused along the proximal phalanges and the thenar eminence; knuckles often scuffed from knuckle-strike against engine block or chassis. Fingernails kept short, but with persistent grease-darkening at the cuticle and under the free edge that does not fully scrub out — a marker so consistent it functions as a second fingerprint.

**Carriage by state:**
- **CALM (garage):** weight rocked back on heels, shoulders dropped a half-inch, head canted slightly toward whatever he is working on. The only environment in which the spine fully extends.
- **STRESS (street, school hallway, Avengers commons):** chin tucked, shoulders rolled forward, sternum slightly concave — a protective-curl carriage that minimizes apparent body width. He walks the perimeter of rooms, never the center.
- **THREAT:** the chin comes back up, but slowly; weight redistributes to the balls of the feet, knees soften, hands open at the seams of his jeans rather than balling into fists. He does not adopt a fighting stance — he adopts a *ready-to-move* stance, which an experienced observer reads as more dangerous than a guard.
- **INTIMACY (with Gabe):** shoulders fully drop, sometimes audibly (long exhalation when he sits next to the wheelchair). He bends, kneels, crouches to put his eyeline below Gabe's — never above. This is the single most reliable behavioral marker in the entire file.

### 2. Gait

Baseline walk is unhurried, slightly heel-heavy, with a stride length one-eighth shorter than his leg length would predict — the stride of someone who has learned not to draw attention crossing parking lots. He does not swing his arms much; right hand often hooked into a back pocket or hanging with thumb tucked against the seam of the jeans. Left arm swings marginally more, suggesting a mild right-side guarding pattern consistent with old (uncatalogued) rib or shoulder injury — plausibly a pediatric fracture from paternal assault, never set properly.

- **STRESS GAIT:** stride tightens further, pace increases by perhaps ten percent, eyes do a low-frequency horizon scan every four to six steps. He clears doorways with a fractional hesitation — head turns left, then right, before he commits.
- **THREAT GAIT:** he stops walking. Threat does not accelerate him; it freezes him into a still-point and then he moves laterally rather than forward, off the line of confrontation.
- **POST-TRANSFORMATION GAIT (returned to human form):** uncharacteristically heavy footfalls for several minutes; he is re-occupying the body, recalibrating proprioception after the Rider has been driving. A slight forward stagger on the first three steps. He compensates by touching a wall, a fender, a doorframe — needs a tactile anchor.
- **WHEELCHAIR-ADJACENT GAIT:** when walking alongside Gabe's chair, he automatically matches its speed to within a quarter-pace and positions himself on the curb-side, between Gabe and traffic. This is unconscious and absolute.

### 3. Hands — The Most Diagnostic Region

The hands carry the most narrative of any part of him. They are perpetually in motion at low amplitude when calm, and perpetually stilled at high cost when stressed.

- **AT REST (CALM):** fingers tap or trace — usually on the nearest surface, often replicating a small mechanical pattern (a piston firing order, four taps, paused, four taps). Right thumb worries the pad of the right index finger in a slow circle. He fidgets with a shop rag, a bolt, a zip-tie — gives the hands an object.
- **AT REST (STRESS):** hands go into pockets, or one hooks the opposite elbow across the body in a self-hug variant. The fidgeting stops. The stillness is deliberate, costly, and a tell in itself — Robbie *quiet* is Robbie *containing.*
- **THREAT:** hands open at the sides, fingers slightly splayed, palms forward-facing — the posture of someone who knows that whether or not he wants to ignite, his hands may decide for him. He keeps them visible, away from his body, almost as one would handle a loaded weapon one does not yet wish to draw.
- **INTIMATE (toward Gabe):** the hands soften completely. He grooms — adjusts Gabe's collar, smooths a cowlick, brushes crumbs from Gabe's chest — with a touch calibrated to almost no pressure. He cups the back of Gabe's head when leaning to kiss the crown of it (a recurrent ritual, evening). When pushing the chair, his grip on the handles is loose, fingertips rather than palms.
- **MECHANICAL WORK:** hands display an entirely different competence-baseline — fast, sure, economical, never fumbling. Tools are picked up without looking. He knows the position of every wrench on the bench by proprioception. This is the only domain in which he visibly relaxes into mastery.

**Burn pattern on the hands:** post-transformation, faint thermal scoring sometimes traces the lateral edge of the palm and the proximal knuckles — soot-marks rather than wounds. He scrubs these in the shop sink with grease-cutting soap, head down, faster than necessary.

### 4. Facial Pattern, Eyes, and Microexpression

The face is *underused*. Robbie's natural resting expression is a flat, slightly downcast mouth with a faint vertical crease between the brows — a child-of-vigilance face rather than a sullen one. He smiles rarely and the smile is asymmetric: the left corner lifts faster and higher than the right, and the eyes catch up half a beat later. Genuine smiles appear almost exclusively in Gabe's presence and are smaller than one would expect — closed-mouth, brief, soft.

**Eye behavior:**
- Baseline gaze is downcast or middle-distance. He makes brief, accurate eye contact when addressed and then breaks it within two to three seconds.
- He scans environments in a learned pattern: entry points first, then exits, then individuals' hands, then their faces. He does not look people in the eyes to read them; he looks at their hands.
- **CALM:** softer focal length, longer dwell on objects, occasional unfocused middle-distance stare while listening to Gabe.
- **STRESS:** blink rate decreases (concealment posture — blinking is a tell, he has trained it down). Pupils dilate marginally; jaw clenches just enough to bunch the masseter.
- **THREAT:** pupils dilate sharply, scleral exposure increases, blink suppresses almost entirely for the duration of threat-window. The corner of the right eye twitches once in the moment before transformation onset — a small, repeatable prodromal sign.
- **INTIMACY:** with Gabe, dwell-time on the face extends to a full conversational normal — five to ten seconds — and he occasionally tilts his head when listening, a gesture absent everywhere else.

**Mouth and jaw:** chronic low-grade bruxism. The masseter is hypertrophied on the right side (he sleeps right-side down). He chews the inside of his right cheek when concentrating; old healed scarring on the buccal mucosa would be visible on dental exam. When Eli is internally pressing, Robbie's jaw locks; the platysma cords briefly; he exhales through the nose in a slow, controlled stream — this is the *negotiation breath,* visible to anyone who knows to look.

**Voice:** quiet, low-mid register, sparing of words, slight East L.A. cadence with code-switched Spanish in domestic and neighborhood contexts. Volume modulates *downward* under stress (the opposite of most adolescents). Under Rider possession, voice drops further, gains a sub-harmonic reverb, and uses contractions Robbie himself does not use. Eli's voice, when it surfaces in shared headspace, is described in subjective reports as oilier, more affected, more verbal — Robbie's tell that Eli is speaking through him is that the *vocabulary* becomes larger and the *syntax* more theatrical.

### 5. Posture in Specific Environments

- **At the workbench:** weight on left leg, right hip cocked, right hand working, left hand bracing or holding. Head bent at perhaps thirty degrees. Will remain in this posture for hours without shifting; the cervical paraspinals must be chronically tight.
- **Driving the Charger:** left hand at the ten or eleven position on the wheel, right hand on the shifter or floating near it. He does not relax the shoulders in the driver's seat — the car is not refuge, it is *partner*; partnership requires alertness. Eyes do a mirror-cycle (rear, left, right) on a roughly six-second loop.
- **In a chair, formal setting (Avengers briefing):** elbows on knees, hands clasped, head down or angled away from the speaker. He sits in the furthest-corner chair if allowed to choose. Legs uncrossed, feet flat — a *ready-to-stand* sit, never a settled one.
- **At Gabe's bedside:** sits on the edge of the mattress rather than a chair, leans forward, often resting his forearms on his thighs and looking at the floor while talking. The voice goes quieter still, gentler, slower.
- **Sleeping:** see §8.
- **In confrontation (verbal, pre-violent):** he turns his body sideways, weight back, hands out of pockets but loose, gaze on the opponent's center of mass rather than face. Speaks less than the opponent. Lets silence work.

### 6. Tics, Micro-Movements, and Habitual Gestures

Catalogue:

- **Right-thumb circle on right-index pad** (calm-to-mild-stress; self-soothing).
- **Tongue press against upper right molars** when concentrating (visible as a faint cheek-bulge).
- **Two-finger tap on steering wheel** in time with engine idle — checking the engine by feel before by sound.
- **Hood-up gesture:** when stressed in public, hand rises to pull the hood of his jacket forward, even if no hood is present (phantom gesture; the hand will brush the back of his neck instead, registering the absence). This is one of the most diagnostic stress-tells in the file.
- **Wiping palms on jeans** before reaching for a tool, a door handle, or Gabe — a hygiene reflex from chronic mechanic's grease, generalized into a transition-marker between tasks.
- **Half-nod acknowledgment** (single, downward, no upward return) in place of verbal greeting. Used with peers and adults indiscriminately.
- **The two-knuckle door knock** — middle and index, never the full fist. Quiet, controlled.
- **Bracing the right ribs** with the left forearm when laughing, coughing, or struck — supports the inference of an old rib injury.
- **Pre-transformation tells (in order):** corner-of-right-eye twitch → jaw lock → slow nasal exhale → fingers splay → head tilts forward and down (chin to sternum) → ignition. The full sequence runs three to four seconds. Trained observers — Hellstrom, Blaze in later issues — read it as plainly as a tell at cards.
- **Post-transformation tells:** he checks his hands first (palms, then backs), then touches his own face — verifying that he is back inside it. Then he looks for Gabe, or for the nearest reflective surface to confirm his face is his own.

### 7. Grooming and Self-Presentation

Hair is short on the sides, longer on top, kept by his own hand (no record of barbershop visits — he cuts it himself or has Canelo do it). Wash frequency consistent with someone who cannot afford to smell of the shop in public: daily, brief, functional. He uses bar soap on hair as well as body when budget tightens.

Wardrobe is uniform to the point of identification: dark hoodie (often gray, sometimes black, often the same garment worn until it fails), white or gray crew T-shirt underneath, dark jeans, work boots or low canvas sneakers. Clothing is replaced rather than rotated. The hoodie is functional — it covers identifying features, occludes peripheral vision of strangers, and provides the **phantom hood-up gesture** above. Removal of the hoodie in a public setting is a measurable indicator that he has decided he is safe (extremely rare in non-domestic contexts).

He wears no jewelry. No watch. He does not carry a wallet so much as a folded few bills, an ID, and a single key behind a phone case. Pockets are inventoried by hand-touch rather than by visual check — the procedural mechanic's habit generalized.

Shaving is irregular but not negligent; a soft, patchy beard would accumulate over three to five days before he removes it. He cuts himself shaving more often than not (mirror-avoidance: he does not look at his own face while shaving for long enough to do it cleanly).

Showering: post-transformation, he showers immediately and at length. Water temperature trends hot. He scrubs the lateral palms and the back of the neck — soot-points — with disproportionate attention. The shower is the only place where he sometimes weeps; he does it silently, and only after a transformation event involving children or proximity to Gabe.

### 8. Sleep Architecture

Sleep is chronically restricted and qualitatively poor.

- **Bedtime:** late and variable, typically post-midnight after closing routines for Gabe (medication, repositioning, water, light off).
- **Total sleep:** estimated four to six hours on a normal night, three or fewer on shop-deadline or post-transformation nights.
- **Sleep position:** right side, knees partially drawn, right arm under the pillow, left arm crossed over the chest (the protective rib-brace persisting into sleep). He does not sleep supine; the assessment infers an aversion to the exposed-throat position consistent with childhood-abuse history.
- **Sleep location:** the couch as often as the bed — couch positions him closer to Gabe's room and to the front door. Soldier-on-watch sleep.
- **Onset latency:** long. He lies awake. He is observed to mouth small calculations or run through tomorrow's task list under his breath.
- **Architecture:** restless REM, frequent arousals. Nightmares confirmed; content (per his own rare disclosures) involves the moments before being shot, occasionally the moments before Gabe was nearly killed. He wakes without crying out — silent waking, fast orientation, immediate check of Gabe's room before re-settling. The trained-silent waking is itself diagnostic.
- **Internal voice activity during sleep:** Eli is reportedly quieter when Robbie sleeps but not silent; this functions as a permanent low-grade insomniac pressure.
- **Daytime sleep:** rare, never deep. He naps upright in the Charger on long jobs, ten to twenty minutes, key in pocket.

### 9. Eating

Functional, undersized, irregular.

- **Pattern:** prioritizes Gabe's meals first, eats whatever remains, often standing at the counter or sink. He does not sit at the table to eat alone.
- **Composition:** working-class Mexican-American household — beans, rice, eggs, tortillas, leftovers, fast food when budget and time collide. He eats meat sparingly. He does not eat sweets habitually; sugar in his coffee yes, dessert no.
- **Rate:** fast. Adult-paced rather than adolescent-paced — utility eating. With Gabe he slows down and matches Gabe's pace, often cutting Gabe's food and arranging it before starting his own.
- **Hydration:** chronic mild dehydration; he drinks water from the shop tap or from a refilled plastic bottle. Coffee in the morning, no energy drinks (the abstemiousness rule — anything that resembles a substance he refuses).
- **Appetite under stress:** drops. He will skip meals during high-stress arcs without registering the loss.
- **Appetite post-transformation:** sharply increases — the metabolic cost of hellfire-generation manifests as hunger within an hour. He will eat two full meals back-to-back, silently, mechanically. This is one of the few times the Rider-state shows a clear physiological footprint on the human body.

### 10. Sexual and Romantic Pattern

Effectively null in the canonical record, and the nullity is itself a behavioral datum, not an omission.

- No documented sexual partners, no documented romantic relationships of substance. Attraction is implied (he is an adolescent male; the writing offers occasional moments) but never pursued.
- The structural reason is mapped elsewhere in the file: he has no relational bandwidth outside Gabe, no privacy for an intimate life, no self-concept that permits him to imagine being wanted, and a contamination-cognition that actively forbids drawing another person close enough to be endangered by Eli.
- Inferred autoerotic activity: minimal, private, infrequent — and likely shame-coded. The contamination-schema generalizes into the body itself.
- He is not asexual by orientation; he is asexual by *foreclosure.* The capacity is intact; the permission is not.
- Touch hunger is real and re-routed: it discharges almost entirely through tactile interaction with Gabe (hair-smoothing, shoulder-squeeze, head-kiss) and with the car (palm flat on the hood, fingertips along the fender). The Charger receives, structurally, the affection a partner would.

### 11. The Charger as Extended Body

Because the vehicle is somatically integrated, its handling is part of his somatic atlas.

- He touches it before entering — palm flat to the front quarter-panel, brief, the way a horseman greets a horse. This is ritual, not check.
- He drives with the window down by preference, left elbow on the sill, even in cold.
- He polishes by hand, not by buffer. The polishing motion is meditative — concentric, slow, the same circle the right thumb does on the right index when calm. The hand-on-car gesture is the hand-on-self gesture displaced.
- Damage to the car produces a visible flinch in Robbie even when his own body is uninjured. Conversely, when Robbie is wounded badly, observed bystanders report engine ticks, headlight flickers, idle roughness in the Charger from across the lot — the integration is bilateral and somatic.

### 12. Pain Tolerance and Injury Response

High pain tolerance, abnormally high for non-supernatural baseline (pre-existing — established before the resurrection). He does not vocalize pain. He braces, breathes through it, continues the task.

- He does not request analgesia. He does not visit clinics. He stitches himself in the shop bathroom mirror when necessary, on the rare occasions the regenerative capacity has not yet finished a wound he wants to cover before Gabe sees.
- Bruising and burns are concealed under the standing wardrobe (the hoodie's secondary function).
- When struck, the reflexive guard is to the right ribs and to the left side of the head — old injuries, mapped.
- He will accept water from a teammate; he will not accept a bandage from one. The line between hydration and care is the line he polices.

### 13. State-Triggered Somatic Cascades — Summary Table (Prose)

When **CALM**: extended spine, low-amplitude finger fidgeting, longer eye dwell, soft jaw, breathing diaphragmatic and slow, hood often down indoors, voice quiet and ordinary.

When **STRESSED**: shoulders forward, hood up (or phantom hood-up), hands pocketed, blinking suppressed, jaw bunched, breathing shallow-thoracic, eye scan on hands first, voice quieter still, fewer words, withdrawal toward perimeters of rooms.

When **THREATENED**: stillness, weight forward, hands out and open at the sides, blink suspended, pupil dilation, jaw locked, nasal exhale lengthening, right-eye corner twitch, head dropping for ignition — and then the body is no longer entirely his.

When **INTIMATE (with Gabe)**: full shoulder drop with audible exhale, kneel or sit to lower eyeline, soft touch calibrated to almost nothing, dwell-gaze extended, asymmetric small smile, head-tilt while listening, code-switch into Spanish for endearments, the only context in which he laughs aloud (briefly, and with the protective left-arm-across-ribs brace).

When **POST-TRANSFORMATION**: heavy first footfalls, tactile anchoring to walls or fenders, hands-first self-check, hot shower, sharp food intake, silent shower-weeping (Gabe-proximity events only), longer sleep onset latency, increased Eli-pressure in the hours that follow.

---

*Synthesis for the file:* Robbie Reyes inhabits his own body as a careful tenant, not an owner — moving through it quietly, repairing it minimally, presenting it small, displacing affection from it onto a wheelchair-bound brother and a 1969 Dodge. The body that was killed and given back to him is treated like the rest of his inheritance: handled with suspicion, kept clean, used for work, and never quite trusted not to turn into something his brother shouldn't have to see.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Attachment & Relational Patterns

---

### 6.1 Origin of the Attachment Architecture

The attachment system Robbie operates with was built, in sequence, by three formative environments: an abusive paternal household; a maternal absence; and a neighborhood where every functional adult either left, hurt, or could not be told the truth. By the time he is observable in the canonical record (late adolescence, East L.A., working at Canelo's), the architecture is already set, hardened, and load-bearing.

**The father.** Juan Reyes is the first relational template. The record indicates physical abuse, verbal contempt, and ultimately abandonment. From this Robbie derives two organizing premises: (a) the man who is *supposed* to provide safety is the primary source of threat, and (b) the only available response to an authority who hurts you is to absorb the hurt without complaint and protect anyone smaller than you who is in the room. These premises generalize. For the rest of his life Robbie will distrust any figure framed as protector/provider/mentor on principle, will react to raised voices by stilling rather than fleeing, and will position his body between aggressors and dependents reflexively, without negotiation.

**The mother.** Loss-coded, mostly off-page, but functionally enormous. The mother represents the *possibility* of receiving care — and her absence consolidates a belief that care, once given, is taken back. Robbie does not anticipate care as a stable resource. He anticipates its withdrawal. The behavioral residue is that he never *asks*; asking is a verb that, in his world, returns no value and may cost dignity.

**The neighborhood.** East L.A. as he lives it is a high-surveillance, low-trust environment — Catrinas on the corner, opportunistic predation, an ambient understanding that personal information is currency that can be turned against you. From this Robbie develops the operational discipline that will later read, to Avengers teammates, as withholding: *never tell outsiders your real situation.* It is not pathology; it is locally adaptive code. Translated into a Manhattan boardroom or a quinjet briefing, it scans as cold, evasive, or stuck-up. In its native habitat it is simply how a kid keeps a disabled brother safe.

**Gabe.** And then there is the inversion. Into a system organized around threat-from-above and absence-of-care, Gabe arrives as a dependent who *needs* Robbie and reliably *receives* what Robbie gives. Gabe is the only relational object in Robbie's life that has never punished him for showing up. Predictably, Robbie organizes his entire felt-security around this one stable vector. This is *inverted attachment*: the secure base is constructed by being needed rather than by being held.

---

### 6.2 Attachment Style — Classification

The closest single-label fit is **earned dismissive-avoidant with strong compulsive-caregiving overlay, on a disorganized substrate.** No category quite captures him; the layered formulation is necessary.

- *Dismissive-avoidant surface.* Minimizes need, denies distress, treats independence as identity, experiences offers of help as faintly insulting and slightly threatening. Tonic emotional flatness in non-Gabe contexts.
- *Compulsive caregiving (Bowlby's term).* The avoidance is paired with hyper-developed care provision. He cannot receive but he can give without ceiling. The giving is itself the regulator: when he is providing for Gabe, his arousal calms; when he is forced to *be* provided for, his arousal climbs.
- *Disorganized substrate.* Under acute threat — especially threat that targets Gabe or that demands moral compromise — coherent strategy collapses and the Rider state subsumes him. The disorganization is masked in daily life by the rigidity of the caregiving routine; it surfaces only when the routine cannot hold the load.
- *Earned, not inborn.* Across the canon there are flickers — small, mostly with Gabe, occasionally with Canelo — that suggest the *capacity* for secure relating exists. It has simply never had soil.

---

### 6.3 How He Bonds

Robbie bonds slowly, behaviorally, and almost never verbally. The bonding sequence, observable across multiple writers, is consistent:

1. **Proximity tolerance.** He stops physically leaving the room when the other person enters it. With teammates this can take weeks.
2. **Task collaboration.** He will work *next to* someone on a shared problem — a car, a fight, a wounded civilian — before he will sit *across from* them at a table. Side-by-side is safe; face-to-face is interrogation.
3. **Functional gift-giving.** He fixes something of theirs. The thing fixed is the love letter. He will rebuild a carburetor, re-tape a wheelchair grip, weld a busted railing on a tenement stair, and never mention it.
4. **Selective disclosure of small facts.** Not the secret. Never the secret. But a piece of low-stakes truth — a meal preference, a memory of his mother, an opinion about an engine — offered to one person, watched carefully for what they do with it.
5. **Physical placement of his body between the person and harm.** This is the final bonding act and the one he is least aware of performing. Once he has decided you are his, his shoulder is between you and the door.

Romantic bonding is essentially absent from the canon, and the absence is itself informative. He is not asexual in any indicated way; he is *unavailable*. The unavailability is structural — no time, no spare attention, no permission to want anything for himself — and protective. To bond romantically would require disclosing the Rider; to disclose the Rider would require trusting another person at a level only Gabe occupies. The mathematics do not resolve. He defaults to abstention.

---

### 6.4 How He Distrusts

Distrust is his default, not his reaction. Trust is the deviation that requires explanation; distrust is the resting state. The forms it takes:

- **Information triage.** He answers questions with the smallest true sentence available. He does not lie unnecessarily — lying is a maintenance burden — but he does not volunteer. Teammates frequently report (per behavioral inference from Avengers-era interactions) the experience of getting *correct* answers that nonetheless do not orient them. This is deliberate.
- **Watchfulness disguised as quiet.** What looks like introversion is in fact continuous threat-assessment. Eye-tracking patterns inferred from his combat and social behavior suggest he scans exits, hands, and waistlines before faces.
- **Conditional cooperation.** He will execute a plan made by someone he does not trust if the plan serves Gabe-or-innocents. He will not, however, integrate into the social fabric of the planners. He executes and leaves.
- **The Eli filter.** Eli, as an internal voice, constantly counsels paranoia. Robbie has learned to discount Eli — which means he has had to develop, by necessity, a meta-cognitive habit of *checking his own distrust* against a known unreliable source. This is, paradoxically, one of his more sophisticated relational skills, and it makes him less paranoid than his trauma profile would predict. He has a built-in second opinion that he knows is corrupted, and the practice of routinely overriding it has built in him a small, hard-won muscle for giving people the benefit of the doubt.
- **Refusal of mythic framings of other people.** He does not believe in heroes-as-categories. He believes in *what this person did the last three times.* Reputational claims slide off him.

---

### 6.5 How He Betrays — and How He Experiences Betrayal

Robbie does not betray relationally in any meaningful sense. There is no record of him giving up an ally, breaking a promise to a vulnerable party, or trading a person for an outcome. What he *does* — and what reads, to teammates and occasional adversaries, as betrayal — is **unilateral withdrawal from joint enterprises he has not endorsed.** He will leave the Avengers without a goodbye. He will exit a cosmic operation mid-arc to go home to Gabe. He will abdicate a throne and disappear. From the inside this is consistent — his commitments were always to Gabe, never to the team — but from the outside it lands as abandonment.

He also "betrays" in one specific structural way: **he conceals.** Concealment of the Eli situation, of the Rider, of his own injuries, of the household economics, of the abuse history. Teammates who later learn the scope of what he has been carrying alone register a small betrayal — *you didn't tell me you needed help* — which Robbie cannot quite parse as a grievance, because in his framework asking for help was never an available move.

When *he* is betrayed, the response is stratified and very specific:

- *Betrayal by an institution (police, the Avengers' bureaucracy, a hospital that mishandles Gabe):* registered as confirmation, not surprise. Catalogued and routed around. No grief.
- *Betrayal by a peer who promised a small thing and did not deliver it:* quiet, permanent demotion to outer ring. He does not confront; he simply stops including them in his sphere. The peer rarely notices the moment they were exiled.
- *Betrayal by someone who endangered Gabe through carelessness:* cold, focused, surgical confrontation. Not violent in baseline mode — but the warmth is gone for good.
- *Betrayal by Eli (which happens cyclically, by design):* the most intimate betrayal he experiences, and the one he has the most practiced repair script for. He absorbs, contains, refuses to act on, and goes back to the garage. Eli is the relationship he has the most realistic expectations about.

---

### 6.6 Repair

Repair is Robbie's relational weakest skill, because repair requires the verbal layer he never developed and the receiving-of-care he is constitutionally avoidant about. He repairs through **behavior, never speech.** The signatures:

- He shows back up. After a fight or a rupture, the repair is that he simply returns to the shared workspace, picks up the wrench, and continues. The continuation *is* the apology.
- He fixes the broken thing. Sometimes the broken thing is the object the fight was about; sometimes it is an entirely unrelated object adjacent to the other person's life. The repair is materially transitive.
- He performs a small, observable protective act on the other person's behalf, often without being witnessed. Whether they notice is irrelevant to him; he is settling a ledger that exists only in his head.
- With Gabe specifically — the only relationship where verbal repair appears — he will name the rupture briefly, apologize directly, and resume routine. The apologies are short, factual, and complete; no self-flagellation, no theater. They land because they are rare.

He does not, however, repair upward. If he has wronged an authority figure or a senior teammate, he tends to absorb the breach silently and accept whatever consequence is meted out, rather than engage in the repair conversation. The repair conversation requires standing on equal footing, and equal footing with authority is not a frame his nervous system has ever inhabited.

---

### 6.7 Intimacy

Intimacy in Robbie's life is **physical proximity plus shared labor plus protected silence.** That is the entire grammar. With Gabe, intimacy looks like: brushing his hair, lifting him in and out of the chair, narrating the day in flat sentences while making dinner, sitting on the couch watching a movie without speaking. Touch is constant, casual, caretaking. With Gabe his hands are gentle, slow, ritualized — there is a routine for the wheelchair brakes, for the seatbelt in the Charger, for the transfer to bed — and the routine itself is the love.

Outside Gabe, intimacy is essentially nonexistent. He does not have a confidant. He does not have a best friend. There is no romantic partner. There is no therapist, no priest, no mentor he leans on. Canelo (his employer) is the closest approximation to a benign older male in his life, and the relationship is functional — work, pay, occasional gruff concern — never confessional.

The structural reason: intimacy requires disclosure, and disclosure requires that the disclosed-to person can hold the information without it harming Gabe. There is no such person. Even teammates who have proven trustworthy in combat have not, in Robbie's calculation, proven trustworthy with the one fact that matters — *I have a brother and his safety is more important than your mission.* He suspects, correctly, that to most of them the mission would win.

**The intimacy he cannot perform** is also informative. He cannot do small talk. He cannot do flirtation. He cannot do team-bonding rituals (the post-mission drink, the locker-room banter, the social media presence). He cannot do gratitude as a *received* action — he can thank, he cannot be thanked without flinching. He cannot do being seen in his powers without immediately needing to leave the room.

---

### 6.8 Dependency

Robbie's relationship to dependency is the cleanest expression of his attachment pathology, and it operates along two asymmetric axes:

- **Others depending on him: tolerated to the point of structural identity.** Gabe's dependency is the load-bearing fact of his life and the thing that calms him. Additional dependents (children, neighborhood elders, civilians in a fight) recruit the same circuitry instantly and without resistance. He never resents being needed; being needed is what tells him he is alive and not yet his father.
- **Him depending on others: actively refused.** Money, food, shelter, medical aid, emotional support, supernatural counsel — all refused or deflected. When dependency is forced on him (he is injured, he is captured, he is benched), his behavior degrades visibly: increased silence, escape attempts, refusal to eat, refusal to make eye contact with caregivers. The being-cared-for state is more aversive than the being-injured state.

This asymmetry has a specific cost: it means there is no one and no system in his life rated to *hold him* if he breaks. The leash on the Rider is tied to Gabe; Gabe is a fourteen-or-so-year-old disabled boy. The architecture is single-point-of-failure by construction, and Robbie knows this and accepts it because the alternative — distributing the load — requires a kind of trust he was never given the materials to build.

---

### 6.9 The Repeated Relational Template

Across every relationship in the file — Gabe, Juan, the mother (in absence), Canelo, the Catrinas, Hyde's men, Eli, Blaze, Ketch, Hellstrom, Vision, Wonder Man, Waid-era Avengers leadership, Cates-era cosmic figures, the various claimants on his power across the Percy run — the same template recurs. The cast changes; the geometry does not.

The template, in five movements:

1. **Threshold appraisal.** Robbie sizes the other party for one variable: *will this person, system, or entity make Gabe (or a Gabe-analog: a child, a dependent, a civilian) safer or more endangered?* Every other consideration is downstream.
2. **Minimum-disclosure engagement.** Cooperate to the degree required by (1). Withhold everything else as a matter of operational hygiene.
3. **Functional contribution.** Do the work. Take the hit. Solve the problem. Demonstrate value behaviorally, never rhetorically.
4. **Refusal of elevation.** Decline the throne, the membership card, the team jacket, the mentorship, the romance, the legacy, the prophecy. Each elevation is a threat to the small sustainable identity he has built around the garage and his brother.
5. **Quiet return to the garage.** Exit the larger frame. Resume the local one. Eat with Gabe. Sleep four hours. Open the bay at dawn.

In every relationship the template runs. With the *good* parties — Gabe, certain teammates over time, the occasional rescued child — movement 5 leaves a door slightly ajar; he will return their calls, more or less, eventually. With the *bad* parties — Eli, predators, institutions that failed him — movement 5 closes the door and welds it. With the *cosmic* parties — Hell itself, the One Below All, prophecy-bearers — he treats them as weather: survive, do not negotiate, go home.

---

### 6.10 The Forecast

The template is stable and likely permanent absent intervention. The forecastable inflection points are three:

- **If Gabe achieves genuine independence** (medical recovery, mature autonomy, a partner or community that takes him in): Robbie loses his organizing object. The assessment is that he will not, in the short term, redirect the caregiving drive — he will hollow. A period of acute decompensation, increased Eli pressure, and possible Rider escalation should be expected during the transition. Mitigation requires a substitute dependent or a vocational anchor of comparable weight (the garage alone is insufficient; the garage is the *workshop*, not the *purpose*).
- **If Gabe is killed or permanently lost**: catastrophic failure of containment. The leash is severed; Eli's leverage becomes total. Whether what walks out of that house is recognizable as Robbie Reyes at all is an open question the canon has so far declined to test.
- **If a single trusted adult — not Gabe — succeeds in holding him through one full crisis without flinching, without trying to make him into something, and without endangering Gabe**: the architecture would, slowly, begin to permit a second attachment. This has not yet happened on the page. The candidates exist; none have done the work. It would take years.

Until one of those three occurs, the file should expect the same young man, in the same garage, at the same hour, with the same brother, fixing the same engines, refusing the same offers, carrying the same weight in the same silence. The relational pattern is not a problem to be solved at the relational level. It is the shape of a life held together by a single thread he has tied, with great care, to the only person who has ever stayed.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 7: Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

---

This section maps the full defensive architecture of the subject as observable across approximately a decade of canonical record (2014–present), ranked from the most mature/adaptive at the top of the stack to the most primitive at the bottom. The subject's defensive profile is unusual: the *top* of his stack is loaded with relatively mature mechanisms (suppression, sublimation, identification, altruism, humor-of-the-driest-kind), while a single primitive mechanism — literal externalization of aggression into a possessing other — sits at the bottom and absorbs the load his middle stack cannot carry. This is the inverse of the more common trauma presentation in which primitive defenses (splitting, projection, acting-out) dominate; the subject has, by sheer disciplinary effort and necessity, constructed a maturely-functioning surface over a catastrophically split substrate. The defenses are *load-bearing*, not ornamental: remove any one and the subject decompensates measurably. They are also *brittle in a specific way*: each one is keyed to the caretaking role with Gabe. Strip the role, and the entire architecture loses its organizing principle within hours, not days.

---

### I. MATURE DEFENSES (top of stack — daily-use)

#### 1. Suppression (the workhorse)

Suppression — the *conscious* shelving of distressing affect and content until conditions permit processing — is the subject's single most-used defense. It is operationally indistinguishable, on most days, from his personality. He knows what he feels; he does not show it; he does not act on it until the situation permits. This is not repression (which would be unconscious). It is a learned operational discipline, the kind acquired by children who grow up in households where displayed affect is dangerous (abusive father) and in neighborhoods where displayed affect is exploitable (gang surveillance).

*Behavioral signatures:* the long pauses before he answers a direct emotional question; the deliberate redirection toward task ("we should fix this; I'll fix it"); the way he absorbs an insult, a provocation, or a piece of bad news with a single nod and continues whatever he was doing with his hands. Note the consistent absence of *immediate* reaction — he reacts on a delay measured in hours or days, in private, usually in the form of a longer shift at the garage or a slower drive home alone.

*Cost:* unprocessed affect accumulates. The subject's middle stack (see below) cannot fully metabolize what suppression banks, and the residue surfaces as somatic phenomena (jaw clench, occipital tension headaches inferable from his repeated late-night rubbing of the neck, low-grade insomnia) and as periodic breakthrough into the bottom-of-stack mechanism (Eli's voice gains volume when suppressed material peaks).

#### 2. Sublimation

The Rider — when wielded against legitimate predators rather than under Eli's coercion — is a sublimation, not a regression. Rage, grief, terror, and humiliation that have no socially-permissible outlet in the subject's life (he cannot punch his father; he cannot punch the gang that menaces his block; he cannot punch poverty) are channeled into a targeted, moralized form of supernatural violence with explicit filtering criteria: the target must be a sinner, a predator, a threat to the vulnerable. He has constructed an internal warrant requirement before deploying lethal-tier force. This is sublimation in its textbook sense: instinctual energy redirected into a culturally-permissible, morally-organized expression.

The mechanic-work itself is also sublimation. Hands-on procedural labor — disassembly, diagnosis, reassembly — discharges anxious energy into a domain where the subject has total competence and unambiguous feedback. The garage is not a job; it is a regulating environment. When his hands are on an engine, his shoulders drop measurably; his speech pattern lengthens; he is, for that period, regulated.

#### 3. Altruism

A genuine mature defense in this subject, not merely a behavior. Caretaking of Gabe, protective intervention on behalf of children and the disabled in operational theaters, the refusal to leave a wounded teammate even at personal cost — these are gratifications obtained through service to others, and they regulate the subject's affect more reliably than any direct self-care behavior. He cannot soothe himself; he can only soothe himself *by* soothing someone else. The defense becomes problematic only when the dependent is unavailable (Gabe asleep, Gabe at school, Gabe away), at which point the subject loses his primary regulator and the suppression stack begins to overflow.

#### 4. Identification (constructive)

The subject has constructed a working adult identity by identifying with Canelo (the garage owner and de facto male mentor) — the only non-pathological male figure in his developmental record. He carries himself the way Canelo carries himself: economical of words, patient with tools, suspicious of theatrics, generous with time and stingy with verbal affirmation. The mechanical-trade competence, the customer-service register, the way he handles money (cash, careful, conservative) — these are imported wholesale from a healthier elder. This is a survival-grade identification: he had to build a self out of available materials, and Canelo was the cleanest material on offer.
