A secondary, partial identification with Gabe's *resilience* — Gabe's humor, Gabe's refusal to be pitied — provides the subject with the small repertoire of warmth and gentle teasing he displays only in the apartment.

#### 5. Anticipation

Moderately developed. The subject runs scenarios — he plans Gabe's transport routes, anticipates which neighborhood corners are dangerous at which hours, prepositions cash, keeps the Charger fueled and oriented for rapid exit. He is, in the operational-security sense, a planner. The defense fails him only in cosmic-scale contexts (Hell, the One Below All, throne-of-damnation events) where the threat exceeds his scenario-modeling vocabulary, at which point he reverts to immediate-task focus (see Concrete Operational Reversion, below).

#### 6. Humor (dry, sparse, defensive)

The subject's humor register is narrow but functional. It appears almost exclusively as dry understatement, usually directed at the absurdity of his own situation, and almost exclusively with Gabe or in solo internal monologue. With teammates it is virtually absent. The function is tension-release at the lowest possible social cost; he uses it as a thermostat in the apartment to keep Gabe's mood up and his own dread off the surface.

---

### II. NEUROTIC DEFENSES (middle stack — situational, identity-defining)

#### 7. Reaction Formation (against the paternal model and against Eli)

This is one of the most behaviorally visible defenses in the file. The subject's abstemiousness — no alcohol, no drugs, no tobacco, no casual sex, no gambling, no joining the gang despite repeated overture-pressure — is not the product of preference. It is the product of a sustained, *active* inversion of his father, and later of Eli. Where his father was violent, the subject suppresses violence; where his father was absent, the subject is grimly present; where his father drank, the subject does not; where Eli kills, the subject refuses.

*Tell:* the rigidity. Reaction formation is detectable by its over-correction. The subject does not merely decline a drink; he declines with a measured, slightly disproportionate firmness. He does not merely refrain from killing; he refrains with an absolutism that survives torture, coercion, and Eli's psychic pressure. A simply principled person would negotiate edge cases. The subject does not negotiate, because negotiation would mean entertaining the possibility that he is, at base, the thing he is refusing to be. The defense is doing identity work, not just ethical work.

*Cost:* the rigidity precludes nuance. Situations in which a kill would arguably be defensible (Hyde, Eli-in-Gabe, certain cosmic predators) generate excess agony in the subject because he cannot make the utilitarian calculation — to him, killing once is becoming the thing.

#### 8. Isolation of Affect

The subject habitually separates the cognitive content of an event from its emotional charge. He can describe his own death — execution by gunfire — in flat, procedural language. He can describe the abuse he experienced as a child in the register of weather reports. The events are intact in memory; the feelings are walled off. This is not amnesia; it is amputation. The walled-off affect leaks, periodically, into the somatic channel (transformation, jaw, sleep) rather than into language.

*Behavioral signature:* the disjunct between what he is reporting and his vocal tone and facial expression. Teammates have noted (Vision, Wonder Man) that he reports catastrophic things calmly. This is not stoicism. This is isolation of affect.

#### 9. Intellectualization (partial, vocationally expressed)

Mild. The subject does not theorize about his condition the way a more verbally-organized character would, but he *does* convert emotional problems into mechanical or procedural problems whenever possible. "I am haunted by a murderer" becomes "how do I keep Eli from surfacing during work hours." "I am dying inside" becomes "the Charger needs new plugs." The translation is itself a defense: the procedural domain is one in which the subject has competence and agency; the emotional domain is one in which he has neither. He moves problems from the second domain to the first as a matter of habit.

#### 10. Displacement (low-grade, well-disciplined)

When suppression and sublimation cannot fully absorb the day's accumulated affect, the subject displaces — but the displacement is unusually well-contained. He does not displace onto people. He displaces onto objects: a stuck bolt receives a disproportionate yank; a recalcitrant engine gets the wrench-tap that should have gone to the customer who underpaid him. He has trained himself to keep the displacement vector pointed away from Gabe, away from coworkers, and away from civilians. The discipline is admirable and exhausting.

#### 11. Undoing

Present in subtle form. After incidents in which the Rider has done damage — particularly property damage in his neighborhood, or harm to peripheral persons — the subject engages in restorative micro-behaviors: returning to fix a damaged structure, leaving cash anonymously, taking a longer route past a previous scene to verify the area has recovered. The undoing is small and private. It does not erase the act; it pays a kind of attention-tax against the guilt.

#### 12. Identification with the Aggressor (failed / refused)

Worth noting because of its *absence*. The classic developmental trajectory for a parentified, abused boy with an internalized predator (Eli) would be identification with the aggressor — adopting the bully's posture as defense against the bully's return. The subject explicitly refuses this. The refusal is so consistent and so effortful that it constitutes its own defensive operation: a continuous active negation of a developmental path his history would otherwise predict. He is, in effect, defending against a defense — refusing to become a perpetrator-identified survivor because he has identified perpetration itself as the contamination Gabe must be protected from.

#### 13. Counterphobic Behavior (selective)

The subject does not seek danger generally. He does, however, drive toward threats to Gabe or to children with no hesitation whatsoever, even when the threat exceeds his power class. This is not bravery in the recreational sense; it is counterphobic in a narrow domain — the domain in which fear, if obeyed, would force him to abandon a dependent. He has so completely identified abandonment with his father that any flight response toward a dependent is intolerable; he overrides it by moving forward, every time, regardless of the calculus.

---

### III. IMMATURE DEFENSES (lower-middle stack — episodic, problematic)

#### 14. Concealment / Operational Secrecy (not pathological splitting, but functionally splitting in effect)

The subject's concealment of the Rider — from Gabe, from Canelo, from teammates, from anyone whose regard he values — is the single most resource-intensive activity in his life. It is closer to operational tradecraft than to repression: cover stories, alibis for missing hours, careful explanations for burned clothes, accounts of injuries that match plausible garage accidents, separation of the Charger from witnesses, careful management of who sees which version of him.

This is partly mature (learned, conscious, environment-appropriate in a gang neighborhood) and partly immature (it isolates him from help, prevents integration of the Rider experience into a coherent self-narrative, and reinforces the contamination self-schema by reinforcing the felt necessity of hiding). The defense bridges the mature and immature stack: it operates with mature discipline in service of an immature shame.

*Cost:* the subject has no one to whom he tells the whole truth. Not one. Even Gabe, post-discovery, receives partial accounts. This is a structural loneliness no amount of competence can offset.

#### 15. Somatization

The body absorbs what language cannot. Jaw clench (visible in the consistent rendering of the lower face), neck and trapezius tension, low-grade insomnia, periodic appetite suppression around acute stressors, and — most significantly — the transformation itself as a somatic *event* that discharges accumulated dysregulation. The Rider state is, among other things, the body performing what the affect system has not been permitted to perform in language. This is somatization at supernatural amplification.

#### 16. Passive Aggression (minimal, but present in team contexts)

In the Avengers and similar team contexts, the subject's noncompliance with the social demands of membership — failing to attend briefings, leaving early, declining post-mission gatherings, providing minimal verbal contribution in strategy sessions — has a faint passive-aggressive edge. He will not refuse the role directly; he will simply not perform the relational components of it. This is consistent with someone who cannot say "no" to authority (working-class deference, parentified obedience to the system that provides) but who reserves a private vocabulary of refusal expressed through absence and silence.

#### 17. Regression to Concrete Operational Function

Under cosmic-scale stress — King of Hell prophecies, mythic narratives, throne-offers, end-of-universe stakes — the subject regresses to concrete, present-task focus. "Get Gabe somewhere safe; find the exit; fix what is in front of me." This is regression in the technical sense (a return to an earlier developmental cognitive style under stress), but it is functional: it keeps him operational where mythic framing would paralyze him. The regression is a defense against being overwhelmed by symbolic content.

---

### IV. PRIMITIVE DEFENSES (bottom of stack — single, catastrophic, structural)

#### 18. Externalization of Aggression into a Possessing Other (the load-bearing primitive)

This is the foundation of the entire defensive structure. The subject's aggressive drive — magnified by trauma, by chronic threat, by inherited paternal violence — is not metabolized internally. It is *outsourced* to a literal, externalized agent: Eli, the Spirit of Vengeance, the Rider state. When violence is required, it is not the subject who performs it; it is *the thing the subject contains.* When the violence is excessive, it is *Eli's* excess. When the kill almost happens, it was *almost Eli* who did it.

In a non-supernatural patient this defense would be classified as a severe dissociative organization with externalizing features — the structural equivalent of "it wasn't me, it was the rage that has its own name." What makes the subject's case clinically unusual rather than simply pathological is that *the externalized agent is, in canon, an actual discrete entity.* The defense is therefore *vindicated by metaphysics* — Eli really is a separate murderer's ghost — while still functioning psychologically as a defense. The subject is *also* using Eli's reality as cover for his own aggression. The two are not separable in practice. Some of what Eli "makes" him do is what he, in unbearable moments, wants to do; the defense permits him to do it while disowning it.

*Behavioral signatures:* the consistent linguistic separation in the subject's monologue ("Eli wants me to," "Eli's pushing," "*I* won't, but he wants me to"); the post-incident shame after Rider violence that exceeds what would be felt for one's own actions (he grieves Eli's kills as if they were his and disowns them as if they were not, both simultaneously); the way he refers to the Charger and the chain as *its* tools rather than his.

*Cost:* this defense is the single most expensive item in the architecture. It produces a permanent identity-rupture: the subject cannot be one self because half of his force-deployment is attributed elsewhere. It also produces the shame-cycle that drives the entire negative self-schema: every Eli-act is evidence that the subject contains something monstrous, which reinforces concealment, which prevents integration, which guarantees the next Eli-act.

*Why the defense persists despite its cost:* because the alternative — owning the aggression as fully his own — would, in his cognition, make him his father. The defense is the only thing standing between his self-concept and the perpetrator-identity he refuses absolutely. He would rather be possessed than be guilty.

---

### V. POSITIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS (strengths developed in response to deficit)

- **Extraordinary work ethic.** Compensates for economic precarity, for the absent father, for the cosmic shame. As long as he is working, he is, in his own ledger, paying down some portion of what he owes the universe for being what he is. The work is also his most reliable self-soothing modality.
- **Manual and mechanical mastery.** A domain of total competence and unambiguous feedback. The garage gives him what no relationship can: a place where he knows exactly what to do and whether he did it right.
- **Fierce protective loyalty.** Once attached, he does not detach. This compensates for the disorganized attachment substrate by creating, in adult life, a single attachment so absolute it cannot be disorganized — a one-channel love.
- **Integrity under coercion.** The refusal to kill on Eli's order, repeated across years and across writers, is the central moral fact. The defensive function is identity-protection; the resulting compensation is a moral spine of remarkable tensile strength.
- **Capacity to refuse power.** Thrones offered, abdicated. Cosmic significance offered, declined. This compensates for the grandiosity that the trauma history would otherwise predict (omnipotence-fantasy as defense against childhood helplessness); the subject has, instead, developed a counter-grandiose orientation toward smallness, locality, and adequacy.
- **Procedural calm under acute threat.** When others panic, he gets quieter and moves with greater economy. Compensation, again, for a childhood in which dysregulated adults made calm a survival skill.
- **Sin-detection moral filter on violence.** A self-imposed warrant requirement before lethal-tier force. Compensates for the absence of institutional moral authority in his developmental environment by internalizing one of his own — and applying it with more rigor than most institutions ever achieve.

---

### VI. NEGATIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS (costs that the architecture pays)

- **Relational impoverishment.** No peer friendships of substance. No romantic life. No accepted mentor (Canelo is the closest, and even Canelo gets less than he gives). No therapist, no priest, no sponsor. The defenses preclude the kind of disclosure that would permit intimacy.
- **Chronic concealment that prevents help-seeking.** The architecture is built around not telling, which means that even when help is available (Avengers, Daimon Hellstrom, Blaze, Ketch, all canonically positioned to assist), he cannot reach for it. The defense forecloses the rescue.
- **Identity that cannot survive Gabe's independence or loss.** The caretaker role is the organizing principle; remove it and the whole architecture collapses. Gabe growing up, Gabe being killed, Gabe simply needing him less — each of these is a latent existential threat the architecture is not prepared for.
- **Outsourcing of aggression that must then be reabsorbed.** Every Eli-incident requires a reabsorption — a psychological undoing in which the subject takes the disowned act back into himself enough to feel guilty about it without taking it back enough to integrate it. This is metabolically expensive and never finishes.
- **Anhedonia outside the caretaking role.** Pleasure is rare. The subject does not enjoy food, music, leisure, or rest as ends in themselves. He enjoys Gabe enjoying them. The defensive architecture has narrowed the pleasure aperture to a single source.
- **Sleep restriction as identity-armor.** Long hours function defensively (suppression-by-exhaustion, displacement-into-task), but at predictable cognitive cost. The architecture trades sleep for control.
- **Inability to be a peer.** In any team context, he cannot occupy the role of equal-among-equals. He is either the protector (Gabe) or the silent contractor (Avengers). The middle register of collegial intimacy is unavailable to him.
- **Catastrophic vulnerability of the leash.** The entire architecture's restraint of the bottom-stack primitive (Eli-externalization) depends on the integrity of the top-stack altruism (Gabe-caretaking). The system has a single point of failure. Lose Gabe and the leash fails and the primitive defense becomes the dominant operating mode. This is the architecture's terminal vulnerability and any party modeling the subject should mark it accordingly.

---

### VII. SYNTHESIS

The subject's defensive architecture is a tall, narrow, well-disciplined tower built on a single load-bearing primitive defense (externalization into a possessing other) and stabilized at the top by a single load-bearing relationship (Gabe). The middle stack — reaction formation, isolation of affect, concealment, undoing — is operating at high efficiency and visible cost. The mature defenses — suppression, sublimation, altruism, identification with Canelo, anticipation, sparse humor — are real and functional, not performed.

The architecture works. It has held for years, through resurrection, through cosmic war, through offers of thrones and damnation. It will continue to hold as long as Gabe is alive, Eli is recognizable as other, and the garage remains open. Threaten any of those three pillars and the assessment is that the tower comes down quickly, in that order of speed: Eli's recognition as other is the most fragile (one good piece of evidence that Eli's wants and the subject's wants overlap and the disownment cracks); the garage is moderately fragile (economic precarity, neighborhood instability); Gabe is the least fragile in a normal-life sense and the most catastrophic in a worst-case sense.

The subject is, in defensive terms, a young man holding a great deal more than a young man should be required to hold, holding it with discipline that exceeds his years, and holding it through mechanisms that — examined coldly — are working harder than they should have to, for longer than they should be expected to, with no relief mechanism built in.

He is, in short, sustainable for now and not sustainable forever. The file should note the timeline.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section: Longitudinal Psychological Profile

---

A note on chronology before the clinical detail: Robbie is a young man. The "decades" available to a longitudinal reading are not the four or five available for a Blaze or a Strange. The honest temporal frame is **phase-based** — early childhood under the father; middle childhood after the father's exit and the mother's loss; adolescence as parentified caretaker; the acute resurrection year; the post-Avengers integration period; and the cosmic / King-of-Hell phase. Each phase is short in calendar terms and seismic in psychological terms. I have organized this profile along that phase grid, mapping affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept at each layer, and tracking what *evolved*, what *ossified*, and what *broke*.

---

### Phase I — Early Childhood (under Juan Reyes, the father)

**Affect regulation.** The earliest organizing fact in the record is paternal violence. The behavioral residue visible decades later — the flinch-discipline, the watching of doors, the way Robbie's shoulders drop a half-inch when a man raises his voice and rise a full inch when a man raises a hand — indicates a child who learned arousal-modulation as a survival skill before he learned it as a developmental skill. The likely childhood pattern: **freeze-dominant**, with secondary fawning toward the father, and a slowly-built reservoir of suppressed protest. There is no indication in the canon of tantrum, acting-out, or externalizing pathology in childhood; the energy went inward and became watchfulness. This is the foundational dysregulation: not too much affect leaking out, but too much affect compressed and held still.

**Cognitive style.** Already concrete, already vigilant, already organized around prediction of the adult's mood. Children in physically abusive homes develop precocious environmental scanning at the expense of symbolic and imaginative play; Robbie shows the adult signature of this in his striking absence of fantasy life. He does not daydream on-panel. He plans. The earliest cognitive operation he refined was almost certainly *threat anticipation in a domestic context.*

**Self-concept.** Inchoate but already negatively-tinged. The abused child's primary attributional error — *something about me is making this happen* — is the seed from which the adult contamination-self-schema will later grow. At this phase it is pre-verbal; later it will be elaborated.

---

### Phase II — Middle Childhood (father's exit, mother's loss, Gabe's emergence as the central object)

**Affect regulation.** This is the phase in which the parentification consolidates. With the father gone (or going) and the mother absent or dying, Robbie — still a child himself — is conscripted into the caretaker role for a younger, disabled sibling. The relevant clinical frame is Minuchin's *parental child* and Jurkovic's work on destructive parentification: a child who absorbs an adult function without the developmental scaffolding for it. The affect-regulation evolution here is critical and lifelong: Robbie learns that *his own feelings are operationally inconvenient.* If he panics, Gabe panics. If he grieves loudly, Gabe is destabilized. So he develops what looks, by adolescence, like a near-pathological tonic suppression — but originated as a functional adaptation to keep a disabled sibling regulated.

**Cognitive style.** Procedural mastery begins here. Caretaking a child with developmental and mobility needs is procedural work: feeding routines, mobility transfers, medication timing, communication patience. Robbie's adult cognitive signature — concrete, sequential, task-decomposing, allergic to abstraction — is forged in the daily ritual of *getting Gabe through the day.* He learns to think in *next actions*, not in narratives.

**Self-concept.** The pivot. The negatively-valenced self-schema from Phase I is rescued from pure shame by the emergence of a *usefulness identity.* Robbie cannot believe he is good, but he can demonstrate he is *needed.* This is the bargain his self-concept makes and never renegotiates: worth is not intrinsic, worth is what you do for the person who cannot do it themselves. Note that this is not low self-esteem in the simple sense — it is a *contingent* self-esteem locked to a single relational object. Functional, but fragile in exactly one direction (loss of Gabe).

---

### Phase III — Adolescence at Canelo's Auto and Body (the pre-resurrection plateau)

**Affect regulation.** By the time we meet him in *All-New Ghost Rider* #1, the regulation strategy is mature and rigid. **Suppression is tonic; expression is binary.** Baseline is quiet, low-arousal, watchful, with micro-expressions kept small enough to be read only by Gabe. Anger appears as a controlled, narrowed thing — jaw, eyes, shoulder-set — almost never as outburst. Tenderness is reserved entirely for Gabe and appears in a softened voice, slower pacing, physical proximity, and a willingness to be playful that is invisible to all other observers. The middle of the affective range — ordinary social pleasure, ordinary irritation, ordinary embarrassment — is essentially flattened. This is not anhedonia in the depressive sense; it is *strategic affective minimalism.* Feelings cost time and attention he has allocated elsewhere.

The abstinence pattern is also locked in by this phase. No alcohol, no drugs, no tobacco, despite saturation exposure in the neighborhood. Read clinically: this is **counter-identification** to the father (whose abusive presentation likely involved intoxication) operationalized as a near-total prohibition on chemical disinhibition. He will not let his guard down by ingestion. The behavior is so consistent it should be treated as identity-defining rather than as a lifestyle choice.

**Cognitive style.** Now visibly *engineered*. He thinks in **systems and parts.** The garage isn't a job; it's the cognitive idiom his mind has settled into. Engines decompose into subsystems; subsystems decompose into parts; parts have known failure modes; problems are diagnosable. He extends this style to people (read threat signature, identify intent, map escape route) and to his own circumstances (rent, food, gas, Gabe's needs — a flat ledger of immediate variables). What is conspicuously absent: long-horizon planning beyond the *win-the-race-and-move-Gabe* fantasy, which is the one symbolic / imaginative cognition he allows himself, and even that is operationalized into a concrete plan (a race, a prize, a relocation).

**Self-concept.** Stable, functional, narrow, and quietly bleak. He is *Gabe's brother* and *a mechanic.* He is not *a student*, not *a friend*, not *a son* in any felt sense, not *a young man with a future of his own.* Note the absence — across the entire pre-resurrection record — of any romantic interest, peer friendship sustained outside transactional contact, or articulated personal aspiration unattached to Gabe. The self has been pruned to fit the role.

---

### Phase IV — Acute Resurrection and Containment Year (the *All-New Ghost Rider* arc and immediate aftermath)

This is the phase of **rupture**. Everything before this set the architecture; this is the earthquake.

**Affect regulation.** Decompensation, then re-stabilization at a new and worse baseline. In the first days post-resurrection, the tonic-suppression strategy is overwhelmed: he has been murdered, his body now belongs partly to a malevolent other, his hands light on fire, his voice deepens, he loses temporal continuity during Rider states. The old defenses cannot scale to the new symptom load. What we observe across issues #2–6 is a young man **reaching for his existing tools and finding them too small** — he tries to suppress the Rider as he suppressed grief, and it does not stay suppressed; he tries to compartmentalize as he compartmentalized the father, and Eli speaks anyway.

The adaptation he arrives at by mid-volume is the one he will carry forward indefinitely: **outsource dysregulation to the Rider, then bear shame about the outsourcing.** This is the new equilibrium. It is technically functional and clinically maladaptive. He has effectively built a *second-order* suppression: the Rider absorbs the rage and somatic re-experiencing that his ordinary tonic suppression can no longer hold; Robbie then suppresses his feelings *about* the Rider. The defense stack got taller, not better.

**Cognitive style.** Adaptive — and this is genuinely impressive. He extends the systems-and-parts framing to the supernatural. The Rider becomes another engine to diagnose: triggers (Gabe threat, child threat, mortal injury); inhibitors (consciousness, moral concentration, Gabe's voice); failure modes (loss of consciousness, Eli leverage). He learns his own possession the way he learned a transmission. This is the cognitive thread that lets him survive the year. Where a more abstract or symbolic mind would spiral into existential interpretation ("am I damned, am I a monster, what does this *mean*"), Robbie performs *mechanical phenomenology*: what does it do, when does it do it, how do I keep it from doing it around Gabe.

**Self-concept.** This is the phase in which the **contamination schema** crystallizes. Before resurrection, he believed he was *useful and contingent.* After, he believes he is *useful, contingent, and dangerous.* The third term is new and load-bearing. He begins to relate to his own body as a quarantined object: covers burns, hides transformation, refuses to be touched casually, sleeps apart from Gabe when possible. The acute event Gabe's discovery of the secret functions in his self-concept as the dreaded validation — *the person whose gaze defines me has now seen the contamination.* That he survives that exposure without total collapse is evidence both of Gabe's love (Gabe does not recoil) and of the durability of the caretaker identity (the role survives the exposure because Gabe still needs him). The Eli-possessing-Gabe sequence at the end of the arc is the *signature event* of this phase and arguably of the entire psychological record: faced with the choice of killing Gabe to kill Eli, or absorbing Eli back into himself, he absorbs. This becomes the **template move** of his adult psychology — *take the poison back into yourself to protect the dependent* — and once a person discovers their template move under maximal stress, they tend to run it forever after.

---

### Phase V — Post-Standoff / Avengers Integration Period

**Affect regulation.** Stable, suppressed, and increasingly isolated. The Avengers tenure shows him operating *in a peer-rich environment for the first time in his life* and being unable to use it. The relevant frame is attachment-theoretic: a young man whose secure base was constructed through caretaking cannot easily occupy the role of *cared-for peer*, even when the offer is genuine. Vision's and Wonder Man's read of him as withholding is correct at the descriptive level; the etiology is that he literally does not have a motor for casual disclosure. He has never developed it.

There is a subtle evolution here worth flagging: Robbie's affect during this phase is not just suppressed but **homesick.** A new feeling enters the record — a quiet, persistent want to be elsewhere, specifically the garage and Gabe. This is, paradoxically, evidence of *expanded* emotional capacity. The pre-resurrection Robbie did not have the luxury of homesickness; he was always already home, exhausted. To feel the pull of home from a Quinjet implies he has internalized home as an object he can miss. Small thing; real thing.

**Cognitive style.** Tactical competence shines, mythic framing slides off. He learns combat protocols quickly, executes plans with discipline, and refuses to engage in the team's larger ideological / cosmological discourse. When the conversation moves to *what the Avengers stand for*, he goes quiet. When it moves to *which entrance has the structural weakness*, he speaks. This is not anti-intellectualism — it is the consistent extension of his procedural cognitive style. Abstraction continues to feel, to him, like a place where lies live.

**Self-concept.** Marginal evolution. The Avengers exposure offers him a potential *expansion* of self-concept (you are also a hero, a peer, a member) and he refuses the expansion. The refusal is principled rather than petulant: accepting the expansion would require dropping the contamination schema, which he is not willing to do because the contamination schema is partly true (Eli is in him) and partly load-bearing (it justifies the concealment that protects Gabe). He cannot afford to feel like an Avenger because feeling like an Avenger would loosen the disciplines that keep Gabe safe from what he is.

---

### Phase VI — Cosmic / Damnation / King-of-Hell Phase

**Affect regulation.** Tested at scales his architecture was never built for and *holding*, with cost. The cosmic arcs (Aaron's Avengers, *Damnation*, the Cates and Percy runs) place him in proximity to events — King of Hell rites, Starbrand catastrophes, the One Below All — that would induce either grandiosity or psychotic-spectrum decompensation in less anchored psyches. Robbie does neither. He performs, he survives, he goes home. The cost shows in the steady increase across these arcs of a *flatter, more clipped, more taciturn* presentation — the affective minimalism deepens under load rather than breaking. He is conserving.

A clinically important development in this phase: the **brief acceptance and prompt abdication of the throne of Hell.** Read this carefully. He does not refuse the throne out of humility, ideology, or fear of corruption (the usual hero-genre refusal). He refuses it because *a throne is not a workbench, and Gabe is not in Hell.* The refusal is *concrete and relational*, not abstract and moral. This is enormously revealing about the stability of his self-concept under the most extreme inflation pressure he will ever face: offered literal sovereignty, he asks where his brother is and how to get back to him. The self-concept did not even briefly entertain expansion. That is rigidity in the strict clinical sense — and in this case, rigidity is the source of his resilience.

**Cognitive style.** Unchanged in kind, expanded in domain. He now applies *systems-and-parts* thinking to infernal hierarchies, cosmic entities, and metaphysical contracts. He learns Hell the way he learned the Charger. He continues to refuse mythic framing of *himself* while becoming functionally fluent in the mythic *systems* around him. This is a real cognitive achievement — most people offered cosmic literacy then accept cosmic identity. He partitions them.

**Self-concept.** The most stable it has ever been, in the sense that it has now survived maximum testing — death, possession, peer recognition, cosmic offers, sovereign offers — without restructuring. The pre-existing schema (*useful to Gabe, contaminated by Eli, dangerous, local*) has metabolized every disconfirming experience without updating. Clinically, this is double-edged. It is *protective* in the short and middle run (Robbie does not get inflated, corrupted, or shattered). It is *concerning* in the long run because a self-concept this rigid will not survive its anchor's removal. The Phase VI Robbie is the most consolidated version of him we have on record, and he is consolidated around a single relational object whose dependency is the load-bearing wall.

---

### Cross-Phase Synthesis

**Affect regulation, longitudinally.** A monotonic curve of *increasing tonic suppression, increasing binary expression, increasing reliance on outsourced dysregulation (the Rider) for breakthrough affect.* What looks like stoicism is a multi-layered compression: childhood threat-suppression beneath caretaking suppression beneath post-resurrection contamination-suppression. He has not learned new regulation skills across phases so much as he has *added layers* to the existing suppression. He has no developed practice of articulating feelings to another person, no developed practice of titrated emotional expression, no developed practice of receiving comfort. The regulation works; the repertoire is dangerously narrow.

**Cognitive style, longitudinally.** Remarkably stable. Concrete, procedural, present-focused, systems-and-parts from middle childhood onward. The *domains* to which the style is applied expand enormously (engines → people → his own possession → infernal cosmology), but the *operations* are the same. This is the great cognitive strength: he is portable across crises because his thinking tools work everywhere. It is also a limit: he cannot easily occupy symbolic, ideological, or identity-narrative space, which means he cannot easily participate in the meaning-making activities that other people use to integrate trauma.

**Self-concept, longitudinally.** A short, hard arc: *abused child → useful brother → useful and contaminated brother → useful and contaminated brother who has now refused every offered alternative.* The schema has not evolved so much as it has been *tested and confirmed* in his own internal court. Each refused expansion (Avenger identity, King-of-Hell identity, Chosen-Rider identity) deepens his commitment to the original schema. The clinical concern is precise: a self-concept this stable, this narrow, and this anchored to a single relational object is structurally a **single-point-of-failure psychology**. The point of failure is Gabe.

**The evolutionary headline.** What changed across phases: the *scale* of what he carries (a brother, then a brother and a ghost, then a brother and a ghost and a cosmic Rider, then all of that plus knowledge of Hell). What did not change: the architecture used to carry it. He is still the parentified eleven-year-old whose body learned that feelings are inconvenient and whose hands learned that problems are solvable. The supernatural did not transform his psychology; it loaded his psychology. The psychology has held. It has held by *not adapting,* which is a feat and a vulnerability simultaneously.

The longitudinal picture, then, is of a young man who arrived at his adult defensive architecture early, under pressure, in a configuration optimal for a very specific life (caring for Gabe in East L.A.), and who has subsequently been asked to bear vastly disproportionate weights with that same architecture. He has done it. He is doing it. The architecture is now bearing more than it was designed for, and it is bearing it through rigidity rather than growth. Should the anchor — Gabe — be removed, the entire structure goes; the assessment of the prior section stands and is, if anything, understated. Until then, expect: more of the same, quieter each year, the garage still open, the brother still fed, the Rider still leashed, the young man still refusing to become what has happened to him.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 4 — Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

---

### 4.0 Framing Caveat (Methodological Note)

Any psychiatric formulation of this subject must explicitly hold two facts in tension. First: Robbie Reyes presents with a clinically coherent post-traumatic and dissociative symptom profile that would be diagnosable, and treatable, in a secular clinic if every supernatural element were stripped away. Second: the supernatural elements are not metaphor — they are *literal*. There is a discrete second consciousness in his skull. The voice he hears is veridical, not pathological. The "loss of agency" during transformation is a real possessing entity exerting real motor control, not a dissociated self-state.

The methodological discipline this requires is the following: **diagnose the symptoms, not the metaphysics.** A possessed person can still have PTSD about being possessed. A man who literally died and came back can still meet Criterion A for the death. The supernatural is not an exclusion criterion; it is an additional stressor stacked on a pre-existing trauma architecture. We separate, throughout, what is *phenomenally* dissociative (and would be coded as such) from what is *etiologically* dissociative (originating in psychic splitting) versus *etiologically* supernatural (originating in a discrete external entity). The clinical experience for the subject is the same regardless; the treatment implications diverge sharply.

This section proceeds: (4.1) Axis-level formulation; (4.2) Primary diagnosis — PTSD with dissociative features; (4.3) Secondary — Complex/Developmental Trauma; (4.4) Tertiary — Persistent Depressive coloration; (4.5) Subthreshold and feature-level findings (OCPD traits, schizoid-spectrum traits, suicidality assessment); (4.6) Full differential (what he is NOT, and why); (4.7) Etiology and developmental cascade; (4.8) Symptom-to-behavior mapping at granular resolution; (4.9) Comorbidity load and course over time; (4.10) Risk and decompensation forecast; (4.11) Treatment notes for a hypothetical clinician with clearance.

---

### 4.1 Multiaxial Formulation (DSM-IV-style retained for clarity)

- **Clinical disorders:** PTSD, chronic, with dissociative subtype (primary). Complex PTSD features (ICD-11). Persistent Depressive Disorder, mild, secondary. Other Specified Dissociative Disorder (possession-form) — provisional, qualified by metaphysical confound (see 4.2.6).
- **Personality:** No diagnosable personality disorder. Strong subclinical traits: obsessive-compulsive (rigid morality, perfectionistic caretaking, work-as-regulation), schizoid-spectrum (constricted affect range, social anhedonia, preference for solitude), and avoidant (concealment, withdrawal under interpersonal exposure). These are best understood as *trauma-shaped character* rather than independent Axis II pathology — they remit conceptually if the trauma history is bracketed, which is the standard test.
- **Medical:** Resurrection-altered physiology; chronic possession-state; somatic integration with vehicle prosthesis; regenerative capacity masking baseline injury accumulation. Pre-trauma: chronic sleep restriction, probable chronic undernutrition, history of corporal abuse with no documented sequelae.
- **Psychosocial stressors:** Sole caregiver to a disabled minor sibling; absent/abusive father; deceased mother; gang-saturated environment; economic precarity; episodic supernatural threat at planetary and cosmic scales; secondary stressor of secrecy management.
- **GAF analog:** Functionally high (60–65) in baseline daily life — holds employment, sustains caregiving, completes school, manages finances. Functionally compromised (40–50) in domains of intimacy, peer relationships, identity coherence, and future-orientation for self. The split is diagnostically meaningful: he is *functional in role*, *impaired in self*.

---

### 4.2 Primary Diagnosis: Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder, Chronic, with Dissociative Features

#### 4.2.1 Criterion A — Stressor

Threshold met, redundantly. The qualifying index event is the execution in the parking lot: multiple gunshot wounds, point-blank, with conscious awareness of impending death. Death is, in this case, not a hypothetical — it occurred. Resurrection does not retroactively desensitize the dying. Additional Criterion A events: witnessing threat of grievous harm to Gabe on multiple occasions; being possessed (a form of bodily violation analogous, in clinical phenomenology, to assault); witnessing repeated instances of lethal violence as a participant; the experience of dying and returning under coercive supernatural circumstances.

Critically, the *non-consensual resurrection* is itself a Criterion A event under any reasonable reading. He did not ask to be brought back, and he did not ask to be brought back *with a passenger*. The phenomenology is closer to waking up post-assault with the perpetrator still in the room — and the room is his own body.

#### 4.2.2 Criterion B — Intrusion

Atypical presentation. Classical visual flashbacks of the shooting are not foregrounded in the canonical record. Instead, intrusion is *somatic and ego-state-mediated*:

- **Somatic re-experiencing via transformation.** Each ignition of the skull is, structurally, a re-enactment of the rupture: body violated, identity displaced, voice altered, agency hijacked. The transformation *is* the flashback — only it manifests as power rather than as paralysis, which both rewards the symptom and prevents its resolution.
- **Intrusive auditory content.** Eli's voice — present in waking consciousness, contextually responsive, escalating under stress. Phenomenologically intrusive even where ontologically external. The subject experiences thoughts-not-his-own; the fact that those thoughts are literally not his does not reduce the symptom load.
- **Triggered hyperreactivity to gunfire, to threat-on-the-defenseless, to scenes resembling the original ambush.** Behavioral evidence: rapid mobilization, narrowed attention, autonomic activation.
- **Nightmare content** is sparsely documented on-panel (a function of medium more than absence); inferentially likely given the rest of the cluster.

#### 4.2.3 Criterion C — Avoidance

Conspicuously elevated and structurally organized.

- Avoids discussing the resurrection with anyone — Gabe especially, Canelo, teammates.
- Avoids the *site* of the killing across multiple issues except when operationally compelled.
- Avoids initiating transformation when alternatives exist; uses the Rider as last resort despite tactical inefficiency.
- Avoids interpersonal contexts that might require disclosure (Avengers social settings, mentoring offers from Blaze/Ketch, sustained co-presence with anyone he cannot quickly disengage from).
- Avoids forming any new attachment beyond Gabe — a totalizing avoidance that masquerades as introversion.

#### 4.2.4 Criterion D — Negative Alterations in Cognition and Mood

- **Persistent negative beliefs about self:** "I am contaminated," "I am dangerous to those I love," "I am the thing Gabe needs protection from." These are textbook trauma-cognitions, near-verbatim in clinical literature.
- **Distorted blame:** self-blame for the theft of the Charger, for the original event, for Eli's presence, for everything Eli does through him. Blame is not realistically apportioned; the gunmen, the abusive father, and Eli himself receive less internal blame than the subject assigns to himself.
- **Persistent negative emotional state:** dysphoria, shame, low-grade dread.
- **Markedly diminished interest** in age-typical adolescent activities — no documented romantic life, no peer friendships, no hobby-pursuit unrelated to the garage or Gabe. (Pre-morbid level here is genuinely unknown; he may have always been this way. But the *constriction* is conspicuous.)
- **Detachment / estrangement:** he is in rooms with people and not in the rooms with them. Avengers issues consistently render him in the visual margins.
- **Inability to experience positive emotion** except in the Gabe-dyad. Affective range is bimodal: tenderness toward Gabe; flatness toward everything else.

#### 4.2.5 Criterion E — Alterations in Arousal and Reactivity

- **Irritability / anger outbursts:** modulated. Self-directed insult: tolerated. Threat-to-the-vulnerable: explosive, with the Rider as the discharge channel. This is a *bifurcated arousal threshold* — high for self, low for dependents — diagnostically consistent with parentified C-PTSD presentations.
- **Reckless / self-destructive behavior:** present in muted form. Willingness to accept lethal damage to himself, to take on possessing entities personally, to absorb damnation rather than displace it. Reads as self-sacrifice in narrative register; reads as passive suicidality in clinical register. Distinguishing the two is non-trivial and is treated in 4.5.
- **Hypervigilance:** continuous, oriented to threats to Gabe. Scans environments. Tracks exits. Knows the neighborhood's threat-actors by sight and gait.
- **Exaggerated startle response:** documented in flinch-pattern around sudden movement, raised voices, particular men whose body language echoes his father's.
- **Sleep disturbance:** inferable from work hours and caregiving load; canonically supported by repeated panel-evidence of fatigue and night-work.
- **Concentration:** preserved on tasks; degraded in unstructured contexts. He focuses superbly on an engine and poorly on a conversation about his feelings.

#### 4.2.6 Dissociative Subtype Specifier

Meets criteria for *depersonalization* (the experience of being outside one's own body during transformation; the experience of one's voice not being one's voice) and arguably for *derealization* (the experience of the surrounding world as strange or unreal during Rider-state, particularly when operating in cosmic-tier theaters).

The crucial nuance: in standard PTSD-with-dissociation, these symptoms arise from *psychic* mechanisms. In this subject, they arise from a *literal* supernatural possession that produces phenomenologically identical experiences. We code the symptoms on Axis I because they are real, distressing, and impair function — but we annotate that their etiology is *external-entity-driven* rather than purely intrapsychic. Treatment implications: standard grounding and reconsolidation interventions will partially help (because the trauma layer is genuine), but the symptom will not fully remit while the entity remains. This is, clinically, a novel case structure — analogous to how one would treat a torture survivor whose torturer is still legally living in the basement.

#### 4.2.7 Course Specifier

Chronic. Onset acute (the killing). No remission documented across approximately a decade of published continuity. Episodic intensification correlates with (a) direct threats to Gabe, (b) Eli gaining leverage, (c) forced social exposure, (d) cosmic-scale framings of the subject's significance.

---

### 4.3 Secondary: Complex Trauma Features (ICD-11 Complex PTSD analog)

The acute PTSD sits atop a complex-trauma substrate that predates the homicide by years. The ICD-11 C-PTSD triad — **affect dysregulation, negative self-concept, interpersonal disturbance** — is satisfied independent of the resurrection event:

- **Affect dysregulation:** bifurcated threshold profile, outsourcing of anger to dissociated agent, inability to access middle-range affect (joy, curiosity, playfulness).
- **Negative self-concept:** present before the Charger, deepened after. Subject's pre-resurrection self-talk and Gabe-organized identity already showed the "I am only worth what I do for Gabe" structure that C-PTSD survivors describe.
- **Interpersonal disturbance:** difficulty trusting, difficulty receiving care, difficulty in non-instrumental relationships. He has *transactions* and he has *Gabe*; he does not have *friendships*.

Etiology of the C-PTSD layer: paternal physical abuse (referenced in dialogue and flinch-pattern); maternal loss; parentification at developmentally inappropriate age (sole caregiver for a disabled sibling before reaching legal majority); chronic environmental threat (gang-saturated neighborhood); economic precarity producing chronic low-grade survival stress. Any one of these alone is sufficient for trauma-shaping in the literature; their compounding is sufficient for the rigid defensive architecture observed.

The clinical importance of distinguishing the C-PTSD layer from the acute PTSD layer is prognostic. The acute layer is, in principle, addressable through standard trauma protocols (and, where supernaturally possible, through separation from Eli). The complex layer is character-deep and requires long-form relational repair — exactly the kind of work this subject is least equipped to accept.

---

### 4.4 Tertiary: Persistent Depressive Coloration

Does not meet full MDD criteria; episodes of acute depressive symptomatology are not clearly documented. What is present is a *chronic dysthymic tone*: low-grade anhedonia, foreshortened sense of future *for himself* (he plans futures for Gabe; he does not plan a future for himself, and direct questioning would likely reveal he does not expect to have one), flattened affect outside the caretaking dyad, and a subtle hopelessness that organizes itself as "stoicism" but reads, on clinical inspection, as *learned acceptance that good outcomes are not for him*.

This is best coded as **Persistent Depressive Disorder, mild, with early onset, secondary to chronic trauma exposure** — or, equivalently, as the depressive coloration of C-PTSD without coding it separately. The choice is largely bookkeeping; the clinical picture is the same.

---

### 4.5 Subthreshold and Feature-Level Findings

#### 4.5.1 Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Traits (subclinical)

- Rigid moral code, particularly around killing.
- Perfectionism in the caretaking role to a degree that precludes flexibility (will not delegate Gabe's care; will not accept help that would relieve load).
- Work-as-regulation: the garage is not only employment but ritual.
- Restricted expression of warmth outside the sanctioned dyad.

Does not meet OCPD threshold because the rigidity is *function-preserving* under his actual circumstances rather than ego-syntonic compulsivity. Strip the circumstances and the rigidity may relax. This is trait, not disorder.

#### 4.5.2 Schizoid-Spectrum Traits (subclinical)

- Constricted affect range.
- Preference for solitary activity.
- Few close relationships outside first-degree family.
- Indifference to praise or criticism *as social currency* (though acute sensitivity to praise/criticism that bears on Gabe's safety or his own monster-status).

Does not meet Schizoid PD threshold because (a) the constriction is trauma-explained and *not* preferred; (b) he is capable of intense affective engagement in the Gabe-dyad, which a true schizoid presentation would not show; (c) social withdrawal is *protective*, not *intrinsic*. He is not a man who doesn't want connection; he is a man who has been taught connection is dangerous and concealment is survival.

#### 4.5.3 Avoidant Traits (subclinical)

Concealment behaviors map cleanly to avoidant logic — fear of exposure, fear of judgment (especially Gabe's), preference for restricted social contexts. Again subclinical; situationally rational given his actual secret.

#### 4.5.4 Suicidality Assessment

This requires careful parsing because the subject's self-sacrificial pattern reads, in heroic register, as virtue, and in clinical register, as risk.

- **Active suicidal ideation:** not documented. The subject does not articulate desire to die. He has died, and the experience does not appear to have made him want to repeat it.
- **Passive suicidal ideation:** *present, low-grade, chronic.* The structural belief "if it saves Gabe, I'll take it" — extended over time — operates as an indifference-to-survival posture that, in clinical literature, is the precursor stratum to passive SI. He does not seek death. He does not avoid it where the trade is favorable for the dependent.
- **Self-sacrificial behavior pattern:** absorbs damnation, possession, lethal damage, in preference to displacing harm onto Gabe or innocents. Heroic on the page; in clinical terms, indicative of a self-concept that valuates the self lower than the dependent — a known C-PTSD presentation.
- **Risk modifier:** the caretaking role itself is anti-suicidal. So long as Gabe exists and needs him, the leash holds. Remove Gabe and the picture changes catastrophically (see 4.10).

Net assessment: **chronic low-grade indifference-to-survival with role-protective inhibition.** Not acutely at risk. Structurally at risk under specific predictable conditions.

---

### 4.6 Differential Diagnosis — What He Is NOT, and Why

The differential matters more here than in most cases because the surface phenomena (two voices, transformation, supernatural agency) invite incorrect categorization.

#### 4.6.1 NOT Dissociative Identity Disorder

The surface case for DID is the apparent alternation between Robbie-state and Rider-state with altered voice, altered behavior, altered capacity. The case fails on multiple specific grounds:

- **Eli is canonically a discrete entity**, not an endogenous fragment of self. In DID, alters arise from the patient's own psyche as protective dissociated self-states. Eli has an independent biography (life, crimes, death predating Robbie), independent loyalties, independent goals (often opposed to Robbie's), and independent metaphysical existence.
- **Continuous autobiographical memory** is preserved across transformations. DID's hallmark is amnesia between alter states. Robbie remembers what the Rider did. He may experience reduced agency, but he does not experience time-loss.
- **Co-consciousness, not switching.** Robbie hears Eli; Eli hears Robbie; both are *simultaneously present*, with one or the other dominant. DID alters typically exhibit sequential, not simultaneous, presentation.
- **Stable core identity.** "Robbie Reyes" is a continuous self across transformations, with consistent values, memory, and relational orientation. DID typically presents fragmented identity with no clear host or a host whose stability is itself compromised.
- **The Rider state has external visible markers** (flame, morphology). DID does not produce somatic transformation.

Correct frame: **coerced possession with partial co-consciousness.** DSM-5's *Other Specified Dissociative Disorder* with possession-form specifier is the closest available code, with the explicit annotation that the "possession" is not culturally-framed metaphor but literal external-entity occupancy. Treatment for DID (parts work, integration) would be actively *wrong* here — one does not integrate an entity that is not part of the self.

#### 4.6.2 NOT Antisocial Personality Disorder

Despite the Rider's lethal capacity, the subject categorically fails ASPD criteria:

- No childhood Conduct Disorder. Pre-resurrection record shows a kid working a job, caring for a sibling, avoiding gang involvement.
- Sustained employment, sustained caregiving, sustained financial responsibility.
- Guilt is acute, not absent — overactive, in fact.
- Refuses to kill, repeatedly, under coercion that would break most subjects.
- Empathic responses to children, the disabled, the powerless are spontaneous and unfaked.
- Cruelty is alien; his defining gesture is *refusing* cruelty, even when Eli demands it and the tactical case favors it.

The Rider's violence is wielded by a person whose defining moral content is the *refusal* of antisocial logic. Eli has ASPD-coded features (canonically a serial killer); Robbie does not. The two share a skull and nothing else.

#### 4.6.3 NOT a Primary Psychotic Disorder

The auditory experience of Eli's voice is the surface trigger for considering schizophrenia or related disorder. The differential fails on:

- **Voice is single, coherent, contextually-responsive, with stable identity.** Schizophrenic auditory hallucinations are typically multiple, fragmented, commenting/commanding without coherent agency, and lack stable identity.
- **No formal thought disorder.** Speech is concrete, linear, goal-directed.
- **No negative symptoms** beyond what trauma fully explains. Affective flattening is mood-congruent and trauma-shaped, not the schizophrenic blunting.
- **No disorganization.** Behavior is highly organized — arguably *over*-organized.
- **Insight is preserved and accurate.** He knows what Eli is. He is correct about it.
- **No prodrome, no functional decline of the schizophrenic pattern, no first-degree family history of psychosis** in available record.
- **Reality testing intact.** His apparently extraordinary perceptions correspond to extraordinary realities.

#### 4.6.4 NOT Narcissistic or Histrionic Personality Disorder

Categorically inverted profile: minimizes self, refuses recognition, declines power offers (including a literal throne), withdraws from spotlight, conceals capacities. The published record shows a young man who actively resists every inflationary opportunity offered him — kingship, mentorship, Avengers prestige, mythic destiny. NPD/HPD presentations would seek precisely these things. He flees them.

#### 4.6.5 NOT Bipolar Spectrum

No manic or hypomanic episodes documented. No decreased need for sleep coupled with elevated mood. No grandiosity (the inverse, in fact). No pressured speech (the inverse). No goal-directed expansion outside trauma-triggered task-mobilization. The "activation states" are *threat-triggered, circumscribed, and dysphoric* — not euphoric, not autonomous, not cyclical.

#### 4.6.6 NOT Borderline Personality Disorder

Despite trauma history, BPD criteria are unmet:

- *Stable* self-image (negatively-valenced but stable; not the BPD identity diffusion).
- *Stable* relationships in the one domain where he has them (Gabe dyad is decade-stable, with no idealization/devaluation oscillation).
- No frantic efforts to avoid abandonment (he expects abandonment and prepares for it stoically rather than reactively).
- No impulsivity in the BPD-spec domains (sex, spending, substances, binge eating). The opposite — abstemiousness across the board.
- No chronic emptiness in the BPD sense, though there is a depressive low-grade dysphoria (different phenomenology).
- Affective lability absent; the profile is *constricted*, not labile.

The trauma maps; the personality structure does not.

#### 4.6.7 NOT Autism Spectrum

The constricted social engagement and procedural cognitive


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Behavioral Atlas

A longitudinal catalog of observable tells, micro-routines, and decision-defaults across every documented affective state. Compiled from canonical appearances (Smith, Waid, Aaron, Cates, Percy runs; team-book guest appearances) and from inferred granularity consistent with the established trauma architecture. Surveillance-grade: assume any of these would appear in a sustained observational record over a multi-year file.

---

### 6.1 BASELINE / CALM STATE

The "calm" baseline is itself diagnostic — it is not relaxation. It is *low-arousal vigilance*, the resting posture of someone whose nervous system has never been off duty.

**Postural signature.** Slight forward lean from the hips when standing, weight distributed evenly across both feet (never hip-cocked, never lounging) — the stance of a mechanic who expects to suddenly need to move a heavy object, and of a boy who grew up expecting to need to interpose his body. Shoulders carried low and slightly forward; not the rolled-in shoulder of depression, but the contracted shoulder of someone who learned not to take up space in a small apartment with an angry man in it. Hands almost never in pockets — pockets cost a quarter-second of reaction time. Hands are either occupied (tool, wrench, Gabe's chair handles, steering wheel) or hanging loose with fingers slightly curled.

**Gaze pattern.** Scans on entry to any room: exits first, then high-threat vectors (door, window, anyone standing), then low (Gabe's eye-line height, child height). The scan takes under two seconds and is not consciously performed; he does it walking into a 7-Eleven the same way he does it walking into Avengers Tower. Sustained eye contact is short — three to four seconds maximum with strangers, longer only with Gabe and with adversaries he has decided to confront. He looks at people's hands more than their faces.

**Verbal baseline.** Spare. Sentences average under eight words in calm conversation; he answers questions, he does not elaborate. Affirmatives are "yeah," "sure," "got it" — not "yes" (too formal) and not "uh-huh" (he does not perform engagement). He does not narrate his own actions. He does not editorialize. When asked how he is, the default answer is "fine," delivered without inflection, treated as a closure phrase rather than an opening.

**Code-switching.** Spanish at home with Gabe (terms of endearment, household chatter, the half-joking older-brother register); English-with-occasional-Spanish-loanwords at the garage; clipped, almost monosyllabic English with teammates and authority figures. The third register is the most stripped, and the most defensive — it carries the least of him.

**Micro-rituals (calm).**
- Wipes his hands on a shop rag before touching Gabe's wheelchair, even when his hands are clean.
- Tucks the laces of his work boots into the tops of the boots rather than tying them long; a small efficiency, learned, never thought about.
- Always parks the Charger nose-out, facing exit. Always.
- Checks the apartment lock twice on the way out — turns the knob after locking.
- Eats standing up at the counter more often than sitting at the table, unless Gabe is also eating. With Gabe, he sits.
- Counts cash on receipt of pay in private; folds bills in a specific order (largest outside, folded once lengthwise) before pocketing.
- Keeps his phone face-down on any surface; turns it face-up only when actively using it.

**Sleep behavior (calm period).** Late to bed, early to rise. Sleeps in a t-shirt and sweats, never bare-chested — readiness to move into the hall if Gabe needs him, modesty also a factor. Wakes at small sounds from Gabe's room and does not return to sleep until verifying. Naps possible only in the Charger's driver seat, never in his own bed during daylight.

---

### 6.2 WORK / TASK-IMMERSION STATE

The garage is the closest thing to homeostasis Robbie has. Behavior here is the cleanest read on what he looks like when the defenses are doing their job well.

**Hands.** When working on an engine, his hands are precise, unhurried, economical. He sets tools down in the order he picked them up so he can reverse the sequence. He cleans a tool before returning it to the box. He talks to engines under his breath — short diagnostic mutters in Spanish, the only context in which he reliably talks to himself. The shop rag is always in the right rear pocket, never the left, never the front.

**Time perception.** He loses time in mechanical work, in the good way — the only flow-state available to him. He will skip meals to finish a job. Canelo has had to physically remove his hands from a wrench more than once to make him eat.

**Music.** Low, almost inaudible, on a battered shop radio — usually whatever the station is playing, no strong preference asserted. He hums but does not sing. He turns the radio off before answering the phone.

**Interruption behavior.** When interrupted mid-task, there is a one-beat pause — he completes the gesture in his hand before looking up. This is not rudeness; it is a learned containment that prevents tool-drop accidents and that, more deeply, prevents him from being yanked out of his one safe place too abruptly.

---

### 6.3 INTIMACY — WITH GABE

The single relational context in which his full affective range is documented. Everything that is suppressed elsewhere appears here, modulated only by Gabe's developmental needs.

**Voice register.** Softer, half a step higher in pitch, slower in tempo. Latency between Gabe's question and Robbie's answer is longer than with anyone else — he is *actually thinking about the answer* rather than discharging it. The slowing-down is the tell. With Gabe, he has time. With everyone else, conversation is a transaction to close.

**Physical contact.** Constant low-grade. Hand on the back of the wheelchair, hand on Gabe's shoulder when passing, ruffles Gabe's hair on the way out the door, kisses the crown of Gabe's head goodnight. Robbie does not initiate physical contact with any other human being on the documented record. With Gabe, contact is reflexive and unhesitating.

**Play behavior.** Reads Gabe's videogame controllers, knows the games well enough to coach. Permits himself to lose. Laughs — actually laughs, a short single exhale of breath through the nose — only at Gabe's jokes. Smiles, full smile with teeth, exclusively at Gabe.

**Caretaking protocols.** Lifts Gabe in and out of the chair with a learned, hip-pivoting motion that protects his own lower back; he learned this on his own, not from anyone. Has memorized Gabe's medication schedule and pre-fills the day's pillbox at the same time every Sunday night. Cuts Gabe's food into manageable bites without asking and without commenting on the fact that he is doing it. Adjusts the apartment temperature for Gabe's comfort, not his own.

**Verbal endearments.** "Hermanito," "Gabito," sometimes just "hey, you." Never uses Gabe's full name except when scared.

**Telling micro-pattern.** When Gabe is upset, Robbie's first instinct is to *fix the environment*, not to verbally soothe. He will reset the room — pick up a toppled toy, lower a too-loud TV, close a blind — before he kneels in front of the chair and addresses the feeling. He learned that words are unreliable. Objects he can move.

**Lying to Gabe.** He does it constantly (about the Rider, about money, about danger) and it costs him visibly — micro-expression: tongue presses briefly against the inside of the upper lip, gaze flicks down-left for an instant. He hates the lying and he keeps doing it. This is the central moral compromise of his daily life, and it is far more agonizing to him than any cosmic-scale dilemma.

---

### 6.4 SOCIAL — NEUTRAL ACQUAINTANCES (CANELO, NEIGHBORHOOD, CLASSMATES)

**Default mode.** Polite, brief, unmemorable on purpose. He does not want to be remembered by people he has not chosen. He nods rather than waves. He says "thanks" and "appreciate it" but does not chat. He turns down invitations with a half-truth ("gotta get back to Gabe") that is always partially true and always functions as a conversation-ending shield.

**Canelo specifically.** The closest thing to an adult mentor in his life. Behavior with Canelo includes mild teasing he permits Canelo to deliver, accepts cash advances with visible discomfort, will work an extra shift in exchange rather than accept a gift. He has never hugged Canelo and would not know how to.

**Neighborhood predators (Catrinas, etc.) — pre-Rider behavior.** Eyes down, pace neither hurried nor slow, route deliberately varied. He knows which corners are watched and which are not. He has memorized the gang's rotation. He does not provoke; he does not flinch visibly either. The flinch is internal.

**Neighborhood predators — post-Rider behavior.** The eyes-down posture persists out of *habit*, not necessity. He has to consciously remember that he is now the apex threat on the block. The body-memory of being prey outlasts the acquisition of fangs by years. Granular tell: he still crosses the street to avoid certain corners even when he is alone in the Charger at 2 a.m. — there is no tactical reason; the route is wired in.

---

### 6.5 SOCIAL — TEAM CONTEXTS (AVENGERS, COSMIC ENSEMBLES)

**Arrival behavior.** Walks in last. Sits at the periphery of any briefing — back to a wall, sight line to the door. Does not take coffee, does not take pastries, does not partake of any provided amenity. Accepting hospitality would be accepting membership.

**Speaking patterns in team settings.** Speaks only when asked a direct question. Answers are operational ("I can take the south side." "Charger's fueled." "Gabe's safe; I can stay an hour."). Does not contribute to strategic debate unless his specific competency is at issue. Does not joke. Does not banter. Does not respond to banter; lets it pass.

**Dress in team contexts.** Wears his own clothes — jeans, t-shirt, the jacket. Has consistently refused costume, codename branding, comms uniform. The refusal is not principled-stated; it is just done. He shows up in what he was wearing at the garage.

**Tells under team scrutiny.** When the Vision or another perceptive teammate looks at him too long, Robbie's jaw tightens once — a single small clench, masseter twitch — and his gaze shifts to a mid-distance object. He has learned not to lock eyes with telepaths.

**Departure behavior.** Leaves without saying goodbye unless directly addressed at the doorway. Provides no estimated return time. Does not provide a contact number more than once.

**Receiving praise.** Visibly uncomfortable. Looks at the floor or at his hands. Says "yeah" or "okay" rather than "thank you." Changes the subject within one exchange. Receiving praise from authority figures registers as *exposure*, not validation.

**Receiving criticism.** Absorbs it without defense, files it, applies the correction silently in the next operation. Does not argue, does not justify. The lack of defensive response sometimes reads to teammates as sullenness; it is actually the trained response of a kid who learned that arguing with an angry adult made things worse.

---

### 6.6 PRE-COMBAT / IMMINENT THREAT

The transition from baseline to threat-engagement is fast, observable, and stereotyped.

**Recognition phase (first 0.5–2 seconds).** Pupils dilate. Breath holds, then resets to a deeper rhythm. Head tilts approximately five degrees toward the threat axis. Weight shifts subtly to the balls of the feet. He does not say anything. He does not announce.

**Threat triage.** First question always answered internally: *where are the non-combatants?* Gabe first if present; children second; bystanders third; teammates fourth; self last. The triage order is invariant across documented incidents.

**Positioning.** Moves to interpose himself between the threat and the dependent. Will physically step in front of Gabe's chair, in front of a child, in front of a smaller teammate. Does this without conferring.

**Verbal warnings.** Short, low, declarative. "Don't." "Back up." "Walk away." He gives them once. He does not negotiate twice.

**Eli's pressure during this window.** Internally, Eli begins talking — louder as threat escalates. Robbie's external tell: a slight, repeated swallow; a brief, almost imperceptible head-shake as if clearing water from one ear. This is the body language of arguing with a voice no one else can hear.

---

### 6.7 COMBAT — UNTRANSFORMED

He fights, when he must fight as a human, like someone who has lost fights before and learned from them. Not stylish. Not trained. Functional.

**Attack patterns.** Low center of gravity. Targets the knees, the throat, the groin — survival-fight repertoire, not sport. Uses environment: tools, car doors, walls. Will pick up a wrench before he will raise a fist. Closes distance fast to negate firearms; understands intuitively that distance favors the armed party.

**Damage tolerance.** Takes hits without sound. Does not vocalize pain. This was a pre-Rider trait — abused children learn that audible pain prolongs the punishment — and the resurrection only reinforced it.

**Disengagement.** Will break contact and flee with a dependent the instant flight is viable. He has no ego investment in winning a fight; he has total investment in extracting the protected party. He will pick Gabe up and run.

---

### 6.8 TRANSFORMATION — THE RIDER ONSET

Documented threshold behaviors immediately before transformation:

- A held inhalation that does not exhale at normal latency.
- Hands open and close once at the sides.
- He looks down at his own hands for a fraction of a second — checking, almost, whether it is happening.
- Verbal: sometimes a single word in Spanish under his breath, untranslated on-panel; sometimes "no" to Eli; sometimes nothing.
- Visible reluctance. He does not summon the Rider triumphantly. He lets it through, the way one might unlatch a gate one wishes were locked.

**During the Rider state.** Voice drops, gains a doubled reverb (Eli speaking through). Movement becomes economical to the point of mechanical — wasted motion drops to zero. Combat decisions are faster and more lethal-capable, but Robbie's moral filter persists: targets are sin-tagged, the innocent are routed around, killing is constrained. The Penance-analog gaze is used selectively — he reserves it. He does not enjoy it.

**Return from the Rider state.** Stagger. One hand to the temple or the back of the neck. A long exhale. Looks immediately for the dependent — Gabe, if present, or whoever he was protecting. Then looks down at himself, inventories his body, checks his hands for blood. The post-transformation hand-check is one of the most reliable tells in the entire file.

---

### 6.9 ACUTE STRESS — NON-COMBAT (BILLS, DEADLINES, EXPOSURE RISK)

**Behavioral changes.** Sleep contracts further. Eating becomes mechanical and fast — standing at the counter, single-item meals. Garage hours extend. Talks to Gabe slightly less because he is rationing his composure. Phone goes face-down and stays face-down. Drives the Charger more — driving is self-soothing.

**Specific tell.** When mentally calculating money under stress, his lips move very slightly. He does not realize he does this. Gabe has noticed.

**Avoidance tell.** When he cannot face a thing, he picks up a tool he does not need and starts cleaning it. Cleaning the same socket wrench twice in twenty minutes means something has gone wrong inside.

---

### 6.10 GRIEF

Limited documented grief events (mother, his own death-and-return, near-losses of Gabe, casualties around him). The pattern is consistent.

**External presentation.** Almost no change. The same flat affect, the same task-orientation. To an untrained observer, Robbie appears unaffected. To a trained one, the tells are: longer pauses before speech, reduced micro-expressions entirely (the face goes still rather than sad), increased physical proximity to Gabe (sleeps on Gabe's floor, parks the Charger where he can see the bedroom window).

**Private grief behaviors.** Drives alone, late, long routes through East L.A. and the freeways. Sits in the Charger in parking lots without getting out. Does not cry on camera; the assessment is that he does cry, alone, briefly, in the car, and that he treats it as something to be done and finished, not lingered in.

**Anniversary behavior.** The assessment infers — based on the rigidity of his routines and the centrality of dates in trauma — that he marks the anniversary of his death silently. Likely behavior: takes the route of the original race, parks, sits, leaves. Does not tell Gabe. Does not tell anyone.

**Grief and Eli.** Grief is the state in which Eli has the most leverage, because Robbie's defenses thin. Granular tell: in grief states, Robbie's argument with Eli becomes audible as occasional muttered fragments, brief head-shakes, a hand pressed briefly to the side of the skull.

---

### 6.11 VICTORY

He does not celebrate. The category essentially does not exist in his behavioral repertoire.

**Post-mission behavior after a clean win.** Confirms the dependent is safe. Walks away from the scene before anyone can clap him on the back. Does not stay for debrief if he can avoid it. Goes home. Showers. Checks on Gabe. Eats. Sleeps if he can.

**Verbal response to "we won."** Usually a nod. Sometimes "good." Once or twice, documented: a small, tired half-smile that lasts under a second and is directed at the ground, not at any person.

**Self-reward.** There is none. The reward *is* the absence of the next problem for a few hours. He does not buy himself anything. He does not drink to it. He does not take a day off.

---

### 6.12 DEFEAT / FAILURE

**Immediate response.** Silence. He does not curse, does not externalize, does not blame. He absorbs the outcome and begins planning the next action within seconds.

**Self-attribution pattern.** Defaults to blaming himself, regardless of actual causal share. If a teammate failed, Robbie blames himself for not covering. If circumstances failed, Robbie blames himself for not anticipating. This is consistent with the parentified self-schema: everything is, ultimately, his to have prevented.

**Tell.** After a failure, he cleans the Charger. Inside and out. Methodically. The cleaning is the rumination.

**Apology behavior.** Apologizes to Gabe for things that were not Robbie's fault and were not even known to Gabe. "I'm sorry, hermanito" said in passing, unprompted, sometimes for an injury or scare from days prior. Does not apologize to teammates as easily — those apologies, when forced, are clipped and unembellished.

---

### 6.13 INTIMACY — ROMANTIC / SEXUAL

Functionally absent on the documented record. The assessment infers that this is not orientation-driven but architecture-driven: a young man this parentified, this concealment-disciplined, this temporally consumed, has no bandwidth and no template for partner intimacy. He has also, post-resurrection, classified his body as contaminated; the somatic-shame profile predicts active avoidance of romantic exposure.

**Predicted behavior in a hypothetical romantic approach.** Polite deflection, half-truth about being too busy, retreat to the garage. Capable of attraction; structurally unable to act on it without first dismantling the contamination self-schema. If reciprocation were ever pursued, he would conceal the Rider longer than is wise and the relationship would rupture on that concealment.

---

### 6.14 RESPONSE TO AUTHORITY
