He never clears them out entirely. He treats them as weather rather than as a project — a permanent feature of the environment to be navigated, not solved. This is consistent with the particularist worldview: he does not believe in the elimination of crime, only in the protection of specific persons from specific harms.

**Trust / safety.** None; ambient hostility, managed through ritual.

**Failure mode.** Grumpy's value to Eli is as a permission-structure. Every Catrina threat is an invitation for Eli to argue *just this once, just this one, you'll sleep better*. The subject's resistance is high but not infinite. The file projects that if a Catrina ever seriously harmed Gabe, the moral firewall would not hold and the subject would cross into lethal force, with downstream identity consequences he is not equipped to absorb.

**Leverage.** They have proximity-leverage (they live near Gabe). He has terror-leverage (the visible fact of what he is). Equilibrium is maintained by mutual deterrence and his refusal to escalate to extermination.

---

### 4. JUAN REYES — the father, the original enemy, the template he refuses

**History.** Abusive, then absent. The man whose blood the subject shares with Eli (the Morrow line enters through him). Referenced in dialogue and flashback rather than depicted at length; the absence is the point.

**Dynamics.** The father is the negative template. Every abstemious behavior in the subject's file — no alcohol, no drugs, no tobacco, no casual cruelty, no leaving — is an active inversion of the father. The relationship is conducted entirely in the subject's interior as a series of *not-that* refusals. The father is not pursued, not confronted, not forgiven; he is metabolized into a behavioral allergy.

**Evolution.** Static. The father does not re-enter the active narrative in any sustained way; he persists as the silent referent. When Eli's connection to the Morrow paternal line is revealed, the father retroactively becomes the *vector* by which Eli reached the subject — the bad blood literalized, the inheritance of damnation routed through paternal genetics. The subject's reaction to this revelation is not theological but practical: he files it as additional confirmation that the paternal line is the line he is fighting against, and he doubles his commitment to Gabe.

**Trust / safety.** Absolute zero. The father is, in the assessment, the only person whose mere proximity to Gabe would trigger immediate transformation without Eli's prompting.

**Failure mode.** If the father returned and made any move toward Gabe, the moral firewall against killing would face its hardest test in the file. The subject's resistance, projected, would hold — but barely, and the cost would be severe.

**Leverage.** The father's leverage is the genetic signature in the subject's face every time he looks in the mirror. The subject's leverage on the father is nonexistent because he refuses to seek him out.

---

### 5. MEPHISTO and the COSMIC-INFERNAL ROSTER — the inherited enemies of the mantle

**History.** Inherited entirely through the Rider lineage; the subject did not earn these adversaries personally and does not consider them *his*. Mephisto, in particular, regards Spirits of Vengeance as assets, instruments, and occasional rivals depending on the political weather in Hell. The subject enters Mephisto's awareness only after Damnation and the King-of-Hell sequence.

**Dynamics.** The subject's dynamic with Mephisto and analogous figures (Lilith, the various pretenders to Hell's throne, the One Below All by proximity) is the dynamic of a working-class teenager who has been forcibly seated at a chess table with immortals. He does not bluff well. He does not flatter. He does not negotiate in the courtly mode these entities expect. He says no, repeatedly, in the same flat tone, until they either let him leave or escalate to force; he then routes the force through the Rider and exits.

**Evolution.** Across cosmic arcs, the subject's pattern is consistent: refuse the seat, refuse the crown, refuse the prophecy, refuse the upgrade. The infernal hierarchy reads this initially as adolescent posturing and progressively as a structural fact of his personality. Mephisto-class entities are *fascinated* by the refusal, because their entire economy runs on the assumption that mortals can be bought; the subject is not, in the conventional sense, for sale. (He is, of course, leverageable through Gabe — but he hides Gabe from them, with operational discipline learned in the gang neighborhood.)

**Trust / safety.** Zero. The subject treats every infernal contract, every offered favor, every truce as actively booby-trapped. Standard operating procedure post-Damnation: assume the deal is the trap.

**Failure mode.** These entities will eventually identify Gabe. When they do, the subject is in maximum danger — not of being killed (he has died), but of being maneuvered into a contract he cannot decline. The file projects he would offer himself in exchange.

**Leverage.** Mephisto-tier figures want the Rider, want the throne, want the soul. The subject has, in their economy, an unspent fortune. He spends none of it. This is itself a form of leverage they do not know how to break, because it does not respond to their standard incentives.

---

### 6. THE ONE BELOW ALL / cosmic-tier Avengers-era threats

**History.** Encountered during Aaron's *Avengers* run; the Rider is identified as having a structural relationship to this entity that the subject does not understand and does not want to understand.

**Dynamics.** The subject's posture toward cosmic-scale antagonism is: do the job, leave the team, return to the garage. He does not philosophize about the One Below All. He treats it as a fire to be put out, not a metaphysics to be solved. Teammates with theological or scientific frameworks (Blade, Black Panther, Strange in adjacent appearances) attempt to brief him; he listens, retains the operationally relevant fragments, and discards the rest.

**Evolution.** The relationship does not deepen. The subject resists the mythic frame that would make this *his* adversary in any personal sense.

**Trust / safety / failure / leverage.** Not personally relevant. The cosmic enemies are weather, not biography.

---

### 7. JOHNNY BLAZE — the senior Rider, the rival template, the warning

**History.** The original Rider in modern continuity, decades senior, accumulated trauma stack vastly larger and louder. They meet in Rider-convergence storylines (Damnation, *Avengers*, the Cates and Percy runs).

**Dynamics.** Not enemies; not friends. Blaze is what the subject is afraid of becoming: a man who has organized his entire identity around the Rider, who performs the role, who has lost or pushed away every civilian anchor, who lives in the mythic frame the subject refuses. Blaze, for his part, reads the subject as naive, as under-blooded, as a kid who hasn't yet understood what the mantle costs — and is intermittently paternal, intermittently dismissive, occasionally protective. The subject receives Blaze's mentorship the way he receives all mentorship: silently, retaining the technique, refusing the worldview.

**Evolution.** Across the runs the subject's relationship to Blaze stabilizes into a wary collegiality. Blaze recognizes the subject's refusal to escalate as either weakness or wisdom depending on his mood. The subject recognizes Blaze's theatricality as either spectacle or self-medication depending on his.

**Trust / safety.** Operational trust in combat; minimal personal trust. The subject does not tell Blaze about Gabe at any depth. Blaze does not press.

**Failure mode.** If Blaze ever proposed a plan that required killing a redeemable target, the alliance would break in a single exchange. The subject would walk.

**Leverage.** Blaze has technique-leverage and lineage-leverage. The subject has refusal-leverage: Blaze cannot make him be the Rider Blaze thinks he should be. Each is the other's mirror, and each finds the reflection uncomfortable.

---

### 8. DANNY KETCH — the other Rider, the haunted brother, the second warning

**History.** Older Rider, family-tragedy-coded, theatrically tortured. Cross-paths with the subject in convergence arcs.

**Dynamics.** If Blaze is the warning about becoming-the-performance, Ketch is the warning about becoming-the-wound. Ketch's identity is so saturated by Rider-trauma that his civilian life has effectively collapsed into it; the subject observes this with quiet horror and recommits to the garage. Their interactions are brief, polite, and structurally redundant — both men recognize they have nothing to say to each other that isn't already said by their respective postures.

**Evolution.** Static across appearances. The subject does not seek Ketch out and does not avoid him.

**Trust / safety / failure / leverage.** Minimal across all axes; relationship is essentially professional adjacency.

---

### 9. DAIMON HELLSTROM — the occult colleague, the calibrated cynic

**History.** Encountered in Damnation and Hell-adjacent storylines. Hellstrom is the experienced infernal operator the subject most often defers to on procedure (rituals, demonic taxonomy, what kind of deal looks like what kind of trap).

**Dynamics.** Hellstrom registers the subject as a clean variable in a dirty equation — someone whose moral architecture is intact in a sector where almost no one's is — and treats him with a mixture of professional respect and protective wariness, occasionally steering him away from rooms he should not enter. The subject accepts the steering when it is procedural and ignores it when it tips into the philosophical. Hellstrom does not press, having read the subject correctly as someone who responds to direct utility and disengages from cosmology.

**Trust / safety.** Conditional and operational. The subject trusts Hellstrom on technique, distrusts him by category (Hellstrom is, after all, the son of the standard adversary), and applies the standard infernal protocol: verify the claim externally where possible, never sign anything.

**Failure mode.** A Hellstrom contract that *looked* clean and was not would be the failure mode; the subject's defense is to refuse the contractual frame and stick to ad hoc cooperation.

**Leverage.** Hellstrom has lore-leverage. The subject has the reciprocal leverage of being, structurally, the kind of Rider Hellstrom finds it useful to keep alive.

---

### 10. KUSHALA / earlier-era Rider analogs — the lineage as community

**History.** Met in the Rider-lineage convergence sequences of the Percy-era books.

**Dynamics.** The subject's response to encountering ancestral or lineage-mate Riders is consistent with his response to all Rider community: respectful, attentive, withholding. He does not feel the call to a *fraternity of Riders*; he feels the call to one block of East Los Angeles. Lineage figures often attempt to induct him into a longer narrative; he absorbs the practical instruction and exits the narrative.

**Trust / safety / failure / leverage.** Marginal across axes; the relationships are biographical footnotes rather than load-bearing.

---

### 11. THE AVENGERS, considered as a relational unit with adversarial undertones

**History.** Drafted under Waid; retained under Aaron. The subject is the youngest, the most class-marked, the most operationally secretive member of the roster he is on.

**Dynamics.** Not enemies — but the institutional Avengers function, in the subject's interior, as a soft adversary: a system that wants to *know* him, *place* him, *deploy* him, *photograph* him, and would, if it could, *tell Gabe*. He resists the system while cooperating with the individuals. He does not socialize. He does not debrief past the operationally necessary. Vision and Wonder Man register him as withholding; the assessment confirms they are reading him correctly. He will not be friends with people who could file him.

**Failure mode.** Bureaucratic exposure of Gabe's existence and address. The subject's countermeasure is consistent concealment — name kept short, address never volunteered, brother never mentioned in mission logs.

**Leverage.** The Avengers' leverage on the subject is the legitimacy and tactical reach the platform provides. The subject's leverage on them is his combat utility and his willingness to walk away at any moment, which he demonstrates by walking away regularly.

---

### 12. INTIMATES / LOVERS — the empty column, addressed directly

This is the section the file cannot fill, and the emptiness itself is the entry.

**The record.** Across the Smith, Waid, Aaron, Cates, and Percy runs — a span of nearly a decade of published material — the subject has no documented romantic relationship, no documented sexual relationship, no documented sustained flirtation, no documented unrequited interest pursued past a glance. There is no high-school girlfriend in the backstory. There is no college relationship (he is not in college). There is no garage-adjacent love interest. There is no Avengers-era pairing. There is no Hell-arc tragic romance. The column is empty in a way that, in a comics ecosystem that reliably pairs its leads, is conspicuous.

**Reading the emptiness.** Four converging factors account for it, none of them sufficient alone.

*First, time and labor.* The subject's waking hours are absorbed by school (early run), full-time mechanical work, sole-caregiver duty for a disabled minor, and, post-resurrection, a part-time job hunting predators in East L.A. There is no surplus time in the schedule. Romantic life requires unstructured hours and the subject does not have any.

*Second, concealment and shame.* The Rider is, in his self-concept, a contamination. Intimacy would require disclosure or sustained deception; he is not capable of the first without catastrophic anxiety and is unwilling to inflict the second on a partner. The same shame structure that prevents him from telling Gabe prevents him from letting anyone close enough to discover it for themselves.

*Third, the inverted attachment economy.* His felt-security comes from *being needed*, not from being held. Romantic intimacy requires the latter and he does not have the receptive infrastructure for it. He can give care; he cannot, at present, accept it. Any partner who tried to provide it would experience him as a closed door.

*Fourth, the paternal-allergy.* The father modeled romantic-adjacent relating as predation and violence. The subject's negative-identity drive (do-not-become-him) extends, by behavioral inference, to a generalized suspicion of his own desire — he treats his own potential sexuality as another thing that could go


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

---

A surveillance-grade inventory of what the subject can do, how he does it, the floor and ceiling of each capacity, the way each capacity has shifted across the decade of recorded operational history, and — critically — the way each capacity *reads symptomatically*, because in this subject the powers are not separable from the psychology that wields them. Every ability he has, he uses in a particular way. The way he uses them is the file.

---

### 6.1 Pre-Transformation Baseline (the man under the fire)

Before any of the supernatural inventory is engaged, the subject is a competent, conditioned, physically unremarkable late-adolescent male whose existing skill stack is itself worth cataloguing — because the Rider does not *replace* this stack, it *layers onto* it, and under stress he reverts to these pre-existing competencies first.

- **Vocational mechanic, journeyman-tier.** Employed at Canelo's Auto and Body since adolescence. Diagnostic ear for engines (identifies misfires by sound from across a bay), proficiency with carbureted and fuel-injected American iron, body work, paint, electrical, suspension. Hand-tool fluency: torque-by-feel, no-look socket selection. The hands are educated. This is not hobbyist knowledge — this is a tradesman who learned under pressure to earn rent.
- **Automotive operator, advanced.** Street-race-qualified before the resurrection. Heel-and-toe, weight-transfer cornering, controlled oversteer. He could drive the Charger fast and clean before it became a Spirit of Vengeance. Post-transformation, the *driving* skill remains his — the hellfire upgrades do not teach him to drive; he was already good.
- **Environmental literacy.** Total cognitive map of East L.A. — alleys, fence gaps, shortcut yards, which streets the Catrinas hold, which corners have cameras, which storefronts a kid in a wheelchair can roll into safely. He moves through his neighborhood the way a cat moves through its house.
- **Domestic / caretaking competence.** Cooks. Manages medication. Handles wheelchair logistics — transfers, ramps, transport. Bathes and dresses a dependent without bruising his dignity. Reads Gabe's cues. This is a *skill set* and most files would not catalogue it; this one does, because it is the highest-frequency use of his hands in any 24-hour cycle.
- **Conflict-avoidance fieldcraft.** Eye-contact discipline with gang members; route variation; threat-distance maintenance. He had to learn how to not get killed in his neighborhood, and he learned it well enough to last to eighteen.
- **Abstinence.** Catalogued here as a capability, not a virtue: the ability to refuse — alcohol, narcotics, gang affiliation, easy money — under sustained social and economic pressure. The same refusal-muscle is what later refuses Eli.
- **Physical baseline.** Lean, wiry, mechanic's forearms, mechanic's grip, mechanic's lower-back capacity. Not athletic in a trained-fighter sense; not weak. Pain tolerance unusually high for his age — likely a function of the abuse history.

**Symptom-as-signature read of the baseline:** every pre-Rider competency is *protective, procedural, and quiet*. He has no skills oriented toward self-display, persuasion, performance, leadership, or pleasure. The skill stack of a parentified caretaker in a hostile environment.

---

### 6.2 The Mechanism of the Power — What He Actually Is, Now

The clinical-operational model: Robbie's body is now the bonded host of (a) the lingering ghost of his great-uncle Eli Morrow — a murderer and Satanist — and (b) a Spirit of Vengeance in the cosmic/infernal sense, the entity merged with or arriving alongside Eli through the occult mechanics of the Charger's consecration. The car is the *vessel* in which the entity was bound; Robbie inherits the binding by dying inside its orbit. The Charger is therefore not "his vehicle"; it is *part of the same organism* — a steel external organ.

This three-part architecture (Robbie–Eli–Rider, with the Charger as somatic extension) produces a power-set with three distinct phenomenologies depending on which component is foregrounded:

1. **Robbie in control, Rider latent** — baseline ambulatory state, normal body, normal voice, intrusive second voice (Eli) audible internally but suppressible.
2. **Robbie in control, Rider engaged** — voluntary or semi-voluntary transformation; he keeps the wheel.
3. **Eli/Rider in control, Robbie suppressed** — coerced or breakthrough state; reduced moral inhibition, sometimes amnesia for the episode, the body acts with another's agenda.

The line between (2) and (3) is the entire psychiatric story of the subject and the entire tactical problem of his usefulness on any team.

---

### 6.3 The Transformation Itself

**Trigger profile (empirical, derived from incident record):**
- *Reliable triggers:* threat to Gabe; threat to a child or visibly defenseless person in his immediate proximity; direct lethal force against himself sufficient to cause loss of consciousness; Eli's coercion under high-leverage conditions.
- *Unreliable triggers:* insult, social humiliation, abstract injustice, threats against strangers at distance, ideological provocation. He does not transform because someone is *wrong*; he transforms because someone is *in danger he can see*.
- *Voluntary onset:* yes, he can call it. The voluntary call has measurable latency — perhaps a second or two of internal address ("alright") — and is cleaner when he is calm than when he is panicked.

**Somatic sequence on transformation:**
- Ocular ignition first — eyes go to flame.
- Skull denudes and combusts; the flesh of the face is replaced by a chromed/black skull with fire articulation across the cranium. (Distinct from the Blaze/Ketch presentation, which trends bone-white organic; Robbie's skull reads metallic, like a customized helmet — visual continuity with the car.)
- Voice drops two octaves with reverberant doubling; Eli's voice can layer through it.
- Clothing partially blackens / fireproofs; a hooded leather jacket appears or persists across transformations (whether material or hellfire-rendered is unresolved in canon; functionally it is part of the manifestation).
- Hands gain hellfire articulation — flame can be summoned at the palms, around the forearms, weaponized as chain or projected as gout.
- The Charger, if proximate, transforms in parallel — black chassis, hellfire-rimmed wheels, flame trail, weaponized contact surfaces.

**De-transformation:** typically when the proximate threat is neutralized or when Gabe is restored to safety. He returns to baseline; the jacket is intact; the body is intact; there is usually no fatigue collapse, but there is a *psychological* comedown — quieter, more withdrawn, more shame-laden than before.

---

### 6.4 Strength, Durability, Reflex

Order-of-magnitude enhancements in the Rider state. The exact ceiling has been pushed steadily upward across writers, and the file should distinguish *demonstrated* from *implied*.

- **Strength (demonstrated):** has overturned vehicles, traded blows with Hyde, traded blows with mid-tier Avengers-class metahumans, exchanged with cosmic-tier threats in later arcs without being one-shotted. Reasonable working estimate: low-to-mid superhuman in early career; scaled upward in cosmic arcs to the point of plausibility against entities for which baseline metrics break down.
- **Durability (demonstrated):** survives gunfire, blade trauma, blunt impact at vehicular velocity, hellfire (own and others'), and — in cosmic arcs — dismemberment-tier injury with reassembly. The body is essentially a host; destroying it does not necessarily destroy the binding.
- **Regeneration:** present, variable rate, faster in the Rider state than the baseline state. He has been killed-and-restored more than once after the originating event. Functional immortality is not claimed in the file, but death's threshold has clearly been raised.
- **Reflex / speed:** combat reflex sharply elevated. The driving-reflex envelope is the most useful measure — he steers the Charger at speeds and through geometries that would be physiologically impossible at baseline.
- **Pain tolerance:** approaches non-registering in the Rider state. At baseline, already unusually high.

**Limit notes.** He is not invulnerable. Sustained hellfire from a peer Rider can hurt him. Holy/angelic instruments hurt him. Certain magical bindings (anti-possession sigils, consecrated chains, demonic hierarchy seniority) can suppress or constrain him. He can be out-tiered; he has been.

**Symptom-as-signature:** he does not use his durability for *display*. He does not stand in the open and let bullets pass through him for effect. He uses durability to *absorb harm in the place of the dependent.* The body-as-shield deployment is the somatic literalization of "take the poison back into yourself." Every time he steps in front of a hit, the file should log it as a personality datum, not a tactical one.

---

### 6.5 Hellfire

The substrate energy of the Rider state. In Robbie's hands it has the following observable forms:

- **Manual generation:** flame at the palms, sheathing the forearms, projectable as a directed gout or a close-range burst.
- **Weaponized object animation:** a length of chain — often manifested or summoned, sometimes physical-then-charged — wreathed in hellfire, used as flail, whip, grapple, restraint. The chain is a Ghost Rider lineage signature; in Robbie's use it is *less* iconic than in Blaze/Ketch — he favors hand combat and the car. He uses the chain functionally rather than ceremonially.
- **Hellfire infusion of the Charger:** the engine, exhaust, wheels, and contact surfaces become hellfire-active. The car can ram with infernal force, scorch ground, and (in heightened states) phase or shadow-travel — see §6.6.
- **Penance-analog gaze / sin-burning:** Robbie possesses a sin-perception capacity that allows him to *see* guilt on a target and to direct hellfire selectively against the guilty while sparing the innocent in close proximity. The aesthetics differ from Blaze's classic Penance Stare — Robbie's is less ceremonial, more *operational*: a look, a judgment, a hit. He has demonstrated the capacity to read a crowd and incinerate only the predators within it (early Smith arcs, Catrinas confrontation, and replicated in subsequent runs).
- **Selective burn:** he can hold a person and not burn them. Gabe has been carried, embraced, and stood beside in transformed states without injury. The fire is *intentional*. This is operationally and morally enormous — it means every burn he delivers is a chosen burn.

**Limits of hellfire.** It is not limitless; sustained heavy projection appears to fatigue the manifestation in long fights. Against beings of comparable or higher infernal rank, his hellfire is contestable. Against angelic or sufficiently consecrated targets, it is reduced or refused outright.

**Symptom-as-signature:** the *selectivity* of the burn is the signature. Other Riders burn what is in front of them; Robbie burns what is *guilty* in front of them and spares what is not. The fire has a conscience because he forces one onto it. This is the moral spine showing through the supernatural skin.

---

### 6.6 The Charger — Vehicle, Prosthesis, Co-Body

The 1969 Dodge Charger is canonically the *primary vessel* of the Rider entity prior to Robbie. After the binding, the car is not transportation; it is *the second half of him*.

- **Telemetric/sympathetic link:** damage to the car correlates with somatic distress to Robbie. He can sense the car's location, integrity, and orientation across distance.
- **Summons:** he can call the Charger to him across non-trivial distance; in later arcs the call appears to function across dimensional thresholds.
- **Phasing / shadow-travel / hellroad navigation:** the Charger can traverse surfaces other vehicles cannot (vertical walls, ceilings, water), and at higher engagement can phase between locations, travel through "hell-roads," and — in cosmic arcs — between realities. This is the closest thing in his kit to teleportation and it is *vehicle-mediated*, never personal. He travels by driving.
- **Weaponization:** ramming with hellfire-augmented mass; flame-trail laid on the road; doors that can be used as bludgeons; in extreme states, the car appears to fight semi-autonomously.
- **Durability:** the car has been wrecked and restored. The wrecked state is not permanent; the binding restores form. He nonetheless treats it as something to be *maintained* — he works on the car at the garage, hand-tools, by choice, even though the binding would arguably restore it without him. This is important. He maintains it the way he maintains Gabe — manually, daily, as devotion.

**Symptom-as-signature:** the car is the only thing in his life he *built* that is for *him*. The garage labor on the Charger is the closest thing in his routine to a self-soothing ritual untethered from the caretaking role. When the file logs him "working on the car late," it should be parsed as *self-regulation*, not maintenance. He does not have hobbies. He has the Charger.

---

### 6.7 Sensorium and Cognition in the Rider State

- **Sin-perception:** he can read guilt — not thoughts, not memories in narrative form, but *moral weight*. He has used this to identify killers in a crowd, to spare the coerced, and to refuse targets that "read clean." In Eli-dominant states this perception is colored by Eli's own predatory logic, which is one of the reasons coerced episodes are dangerous: the *perception* is reliable; the *interpretation* is not.
- **Threat-tracking:** elevated peripheral awareness; can engage multiple opponents without classical blindsiding.
- **Eli as informant:** Eli has knowledge Robbie does not — occult, criminal, historical. Robbie can, when he chooses to listen, draw on Eli's memory as an intelligence asset. He hates doing it. He does it rarely and reluctantly. The file should note that every consultation with Eli costs him.
- **Suppression of pain affect; suppression of fear affect.** In the Rider state, the body does not flinch the way the baseline body does. This is tactically useful and psychologically corrosive — it teaches him that *not feeling* is a form of effectiveness, which reinforces the baseline isolation-of-affect defense.

---

### 6.8 The Eli Problem (Power-Set Liability)

Catalogued here as a *capability* because Eli is part of the operational system, even though he is also the system's primary failure mode.

- **Eli can attempt overt possession** under triggers: Robbie's unconsciousness, severe injury, moral compromise, prolonged combat fatigue, exposure to other infernal entities that destabilize the binding.
- **Eli can body-jump under certain conditions** — most catastrophically demonstrated in the vol. 1 finale, when he transferred into Gabe.
- **Eli whispers, constantly.** This is a baseline cost — Robbie's interior monologue is *shared*. The whisper is suppressible but never absent. It is a chronic dissociative load.
- **Eli pushes lethal escalation.** Where Robbie wants to subdue, Eli wants to kill. Where Robbie wants to spare, Eli wants to make an example. In any fight, there are two voices voting on the kill.

**Containment mechanisms (Robbie's, self-developed):**
- Refusal-on-principle. He has a flat, non-negotiable no on certain acts (will not kill Gabe; will not kill children; will not kill the unarmed or the surrendered).
- Disengagement. He ends fights as fast as possible to reduce Eli's window.
- Re-absorption. The signature maneuver — when Eli escapes (into a body, into a third party, into the world), Robbie does not destroy him; he *takes him back inside*. Better to host the parasite than to let it loose. This is the prototypical Reyes move and it is both heroic and self-harmful, and the file should not confuse the two.

**Symptom-as-signature:** the entire Eli dynamic is the externalization of the abuse-perpetrator voice that any survivor of childhood violence carries internally. Robbie's father is gone; the *voice of the father* is not. Eli is the literalization. His relationship to Eli — refuse, refuse, slip, shame, reabsorb — is the relationship a survivor has with the introjected abuser. The supernatural reality of Eli does not change the psychological reality of what Eli *is*.

---

### 6.9 Growth Curve (2014 → Present)

- **2014–2015 (Smith origin):** local-tier power. East L.A. scale. Fights humans, gang lieutenants, Hyde. Hellfire, chain, car, sin-burn. Learning the system on the job.
- **2016–2017 (Standoff, Waid Avengers):** scales up by collision with team-tier opposition. Demonstrates that the kit holds against superhuman peers. Concealment of Eli is the operational signature here, not power growth.
- **2018–2019 (Damnation, Aaron Avengers):** scales up to cosmic/infernal opposition. Confronts the Spirit of Vengeance lineage as a cosmic reality; encounters Blaze and the King of Hell apparatus; gains access to deeper Rider mechanics (hell-road travel, broader hellfire applications). Skill is reactive — he survives by adaptation, not training.
- **2019–2022 (Cates, Percy):** trapped in Hell, briefly throned, abdicates. The power-tier in this period is the highest of his career — King-of-Hell-adjacent — and the most psychologically destabilizing. He gives it back. The *capacity to renounce maximum power* is itself a capability worth filing.
- **Present baseline:** he returns, repeatedly, to the lowest stable engagement of the kit consistent with the protective task at hand. He scales *down* deliberately. This is unique among Marvel heroes of comparable raw output.

**Growth pattern read:** he does not pursue mastery; mastery is forced on him by escalating threat. He is a *reluctant* power-learner. He acquires only what the current crisis demands and then stops. There is no training montage in his life. There is the garage, the brother, and the next problem.

---

### 6.10 Skills Adjacent to the Powers

- **Combat:** untrained in formal martial systems. Brawler-tier baseline, augmented to devastating in the Rider state by strength/durability/reflex. He fights *practically* — ends fights, does not extend them, does not showboat. No signature stance, no choreography. Hits things until they stop.
- **Tactics:** sound at the small-unit / single-engagement level. Poor at multi-vector strategic thinking; defers to teammates on macro plans. Excellent at *exfiltration* of a non-combatant under fire (a skill the file should note is *Gabe-coded* — he has been practicing it conceptually his whole life).
- **Stealth:** the baseline body is competent at neighborhood-scale evasion. The Rider state is the opposite of stealth — a literal flaming skull. He compensates by transforming *late* and de-transforming *fast*.
- **Languages:** English and Spanish, fluent, code-switching natural. Cultural fluency in working-class Mexican-American East L.A. is total and is itself an intelligence-grade asset for any operation in that geography.
- **Information discipline:** elite. He does not talk. He does not post. He does not confess. The concealment skill that protects Gabe also protects every operational secret he holds. From a counterintelligence standpoint, he is a hard target — not because he is paranoid, but because his entire life pre-trained him to withhold.
- **Negotiation, persuasion, public speaking, leadership:** absent or refused. He does not do these things. He will not be made to do them.

---

### 6.11 Hard Limits

- **Cannot operate well without the car.** Removed from the Charger across distance, he is reduced in mobility, projection, and — assessment — emotional regulation. The car is part of him.
- **Cannot reliably suppress Eli under sustained pressure.** Long fights, repeated transformations, sleep deprivation, and proximity to other infernal entities erode the containment.
- **Cannot use the powers cleanly when the target is morally ambiguous.** Sin-perception serves him against the clearly guilty; it stutters against the gray. He has been observed to disengage rather than burn the ambiguous.
- **Cannot scale his concern.** He does not have a planetary-stakes mode. Asked to care about a galaxy, he cares about Gabe and translates outward by analogy if at all.
- **Cannot perform power for an audience.** Public use degrades his function; he is worse on camera than off it. Theater is not in the kit.
- **Cannot accept augmentation, training, or upgrades from outside parties.** Offers of mystical instruction, infernal patronage, or institutional resourcing are reliably refused. He will not be tooled-up by anyone. The kit he has is the kit he keeps.

---

### 6.12 Signature Applications (the moves the file would learn to anticipate)

1. **The interposition.** Step between threat and dependent; absorb the hit; transform if and only if the hit was not enough to end the engagement. He is a *shield-first* fighter.
2. **The selective burn.** Identify the guilty in a mixed group; immobilize or incinerate selectively; leave the innocent untouched and, where possible, unaware.
3. **The Charger charge.** Vehicular engagement at hellfire velocity, often through structures, terminating in dismount-and-finish.
4. **The chain restraint.** Used more often to *hold* than to *kill* — wrap, immobilize, interrogate. Eli wants the chain to be a noose; Robbie uses it as a cuff.
5. **The re-absorption.** When a fight ends with Eli loose in the world or in a host, Robbie pulls him back in rather than destroy the host. Cost is borne internally.
6. **The disengagement.** Most under-catalogued and most diagnostic: he *leaves*. Mission complete, he leaves. Conversation getting personal, he leaves. Recognition offered, he leaves. The exit is a power.

---

### 6.13 Symptom-as-Signature Synthesis

The whole kit, read as a single psychological document:

- **Hellfire that chooses its targets** = the moral spine refusing to become the perpetrator.
- **Strength used as a shield** = the parentified caretaker translated into combat.
- **A car that is half his body** = the only thing he made for himself, kept by hand, daily, as devotion.
- **A skull on fire** = the somatic re-experiencing of the execution, ritualized into a weapon.
- **A second voice in the head** = the introjected abuser, literalized, refused daily.
- **Selective non-burn of the held body** = the proof, to himself, that he is not what touched him as a child.
- **Power growth driven only by crisis, renounced as soon as possible**


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Operational Profile & Tradecraft

---

### 6.1 Decision Architecture

Subject's decision-making operates on a strict, observable hierarchy of triage that has remained stable across every documented operational episode from the All-New (2014) sequence through the Percy solo run. It is not a doctrine he has articulated; it is a behavioral regularity that can be reconstructed from outcomes.

**The Triage Stack (top-down):**

1. *Is Gabe in immediate danger?* If yes, all other considerations terminate. Subject will abandon objectives, allies, mission cover, and team-level moral constraints to interdict. He will leave a Pacific-coast cosmic engagement to return to East L.A. if Gabe's phone rings unanswered for too long — observable in his Avengers tenure where he disengages from extraction protocols against Stark's and Rogers's stated preference.
2. *Is the threat a predator on the defenseless — a child, a disabled person, an obvious civilian?* If yes, engagement is reflexive and disproportionate. He does not stage, does not negotiate, does not call for backup.
3. *Is the threat to himself only?* If yes, default is absorb-and-walk-away. Subject has been seen taking beatings, gunshots, and verbal humiliation without retaliation when only his own person is at stake. This is *not* pacifism. It is asymmetric thresholding.
4. *Is there an institutional, mythic, or cosmic frame attached?* If yes, subject's compliance degrades. He will execute the task — he is not a quitter mid-engagement — but he will not internalize the stakes and will exfiltrate at the first defensible opportunity.

**Decision tempo.** Fast in the concrete, slow in the abstract. Confronted with a mechanical, tactical, or proximate-threat problem, his orient-decide-act loop is short — characteristically under two seconds in combat, near-instantaneous in mechanical diagnosis. Confronted with strategic, political, or relational decisions (team alignment, public identity, accepting or refusing a power offer), he stalls, defers, goes quiet, and frequently lets the decision lapse by inaction. *Inaction is a frequent and deliberate operational choice for this subject.*

**The Eli factor.** Every decision under arousal is in effect a *two-party* decision: Robbie's intent, modulated against Eli's pressure. Operationally this functions like negotiating with a hostile co-pilot. Subject's tradecraft for managing Eli during ops includes: refusing to verbalize plans aloud while transformed (denies Eli leverage by withholding intent), keeping engagements *short* (Eli's influence appears to compound with transformation duration), and ending engagements by *driving* (the act of returning to the Charger and to the road appears to be his de-transformation ritual — see 6.6).

---

### 6.2 Methods of Engagement

**Preferred modality: vehicular ambush in low-light, on familiar surface streets.** The overwhelming majority of subject's combat occurrences take place on roads he knows — the industrial arteries of Boyle Heights, the freeway interchanges around the 5/10/60, the warehouse stretches east of the river. Home-field selection is not coincidence; it is the foundation of his tradecraft. He fights where he knows every alley, every chain-link gap, every overpass clearance.

**Engagement template:**
- *Acquire:* Subject tracks targets primarily by following criminal-economy nodes (drug pickups, gang gathering points, the chop-shop network he knows from civilian work). Surveillance is auditory and observational — he listens at the garage, in the neighborhood, at street races. He does not run electronic intercepts.
- *Approach:* In the Charger, headlights on, ordinary engine note. Acceleration profile pre-transformation is indistinguishable from any other tuned street car. This is intentional cover.
- *Initiate:* Transformation is held until the last available moment — often after the target has identified him as a teenager in a muscle car and underestimated. The reveal is itself a tactic; the psychological collapse it produces in adversaries is a force multiplier.
- *Engage:* Close-quarters, hellfire-augmented striking; the chain as flexible reach weapon; the car as ram, shield, and exit. He fights *with* the vehicle, not next to it.
- *Terminate:* Disable, do not kill. Subject's signature is breaking the engagement in a way that leaves the adversary alive but operationally finished — broken hands, burned faces, immobilizing wounds. The exceptions are when Eli wrests control; these episodes are followed by extended shame-cycles (see 6.7).
- *Exfiltrate:* Drive. Always drive. Subject does not walk away from a scene if the car is intact. The return drive doubles as decompression.

**Avoidances.** Subject does not engage in daylight when avoidable. Does not operate in unfamiliar terrain without reconnaissance. Does not engage adversaries in proximity to Gabe's location, school, or transit routes — he will let a target walk and reacquire later rather than fight on Gabe's block. Does not use firearms; the assessment is this is not tactical but biographical (he was killed by gunfire; the somatic aversion is total). Does not stage publicly when avoidable — refuses photo-op heroics, hates the spectator dynamic.

**Combat signature.** Hellfire output runs hot-blue under composure, deeper red and more ragged under Eli's pressure — a visible *tell* to anyone who has watched him twice. The chain whip pattern is right-handed, figure-eight, low-arc; he learned the mechanics by feel rather than instruction and has a consistent, identifiable rhythm. Punches are aimed at the structure of the adversary's body — joints, jaw hinge, sternum — not the face for show. Economy of motion is unusually high for a young combatant; the assessment infers garage-floor labor (compact, repetitive, force-efficient movement under hood-line constraints) as the kinesthetic source.

---

### 6.3 Tradecraft: Concealment and Operational Security

Subject's OPSEC is not learned from a tradecraft manual; it is learned from being a brown teenager in a gang neighborhood with an abusive parent. It is gang-survival OPSEC, transposed onto supernatural circumstances, and it is unusually effective.

**Concealment doctrine — "tell no one."**
- The Rider identity is concealed from Gabe (until forced), from Canelo (employer), from the school, from social services, from teammates for as long as possible. The default disclosure setting is *off*.
- Subject lies by *omission and silence* rather than confabulation. He does not invent cover stories; he simply does not answer. This is a stronger OPSEC posture than fabrication — there is no story to break.
- When pressed, he uses partial truths: "I was at work." "I was driving." These are technically accurate and emotionally flat enough to discourage follow-up.

**Physical concealment.**
- The hoodie. Operational uniform. Hood up obscures facial flame residue, scorch marks at the neck, and the unusual pupil dilation that lingers post-transformation. He owns multiple identical or near-identical hoodies — a quartermaster pattern, not a fashion choice.
- Long sleeves year-round, regardless of L.A. heat. Conceals minor burns, chain abrasions, knuckle damage.
- The car is the principal cover. A '69 Dodge Charger is loud and conspicuous *as a car*, which paradoxically functions as concealment: witnesses remember the car, not the driver. The Charger has no visible plates in most depictions, or plates that read as ordinary; subject does not customize visibly (no flames painted on, no skull decals — those would draw the wrong attention).
- Post-engagement, he washes scorch off the chassis at the garage after hours. Routine maintenance cover for what is essentially evidence cleanup.

**Communications discipline.**
- Subject's phone use is minimal. Calls Gabe. Texts Canelo about shifts. Does not maintain social media. Does not appear in selfies, group photos, or geotagged content — this is significant given his age cohort and is itself a tell of pre-existing operational caution.
- During Avengers tenure, he was consistently the slowest to respond on team comms and the first to drop off-channel. The assessment is that he treats team communications as surveillance exposure.
- No diary, no journal, no recorded confessional. Whatever processing occurs, occurs internally or at the workbench.

**Counter-surveillance behaviors.**
- Habitually checks reflections (shop windows, side mirrors, the Charger's polished chrome) for tails. Not paranoid; consistent.
- Varies route to school and to the garage in low-frequency rotation — typically two or three alternates, not random.
- Sits with back to wall in any room he enters. Selects parking with two egress paths.
- Identifies exits within ninety seconds of entering an unfamiliar space.

These behaviors predate the Rider. They are gang-neighborhood survival habits, and they ported directly into supernatural operations without modification.

---

### 6.4 Resources and Finances

Subject operates on what is effectively a poverty-line budget with one extraordinary asset (the Charger / the Rider) and one extraordinary liability (Gabe's medical and accessibility needs in a household with no insurance worth naming).

**Income streams (confirmed and inferred):**
- *Canelo's Auto and Body wages.* Hourly, almost certainly under-the-table or partial cash. Subject's hours are long; the wage is small. This is his only documented legal income.
- *Side mechanical work.* Tune-ups, transmission jobs, body work for neighborhood clients. Cash. Off-books.
- *Street race winnings (historical, pre-resurrection).* The originating incident was an attempt to win prize money. Post-Rider, the assessment is that he abandoned racing as an income strategy — too public, too witnessed.
- *No criminal income.* Subject does not steal, does not run product, does not extort. This is a hard line for him and has been tested.
- *No Avengers stipend taken,* per assessment of his withdrawal pattern; even if offered, his refusal-of-charity profile would predict declining or quietly not cashing it.

**Expenses (estimated structure):**
- Rent on the small Reyes-household apartment (East L.A., low-rent corridor).
- Gabe's care: wheelchair maintenance, accessibility adaptations, food, school transit, medications if any. This is the largest variable expense and the one that drives all the others.
- Vehicle: the Charger requires fuel, parts, fluids — though subject scavenges and barters most parts through the garage network, reducing cash cost.
- Food: minimal for self, prioritized for Gabe. Subject's own intake is observably erratic.
- No discretionary spending of note. No new clothes beyond replacement. No entertainment expenditure. No travel.

**Infrastructure assets:**
- *Canelo's Auto and Body.* Functions as workshop, intelligence hub, social cover, income source, and emotional containment site simultaneously. Canelo himself is one of the very few adults subject trusts on any axis.
- *The Charger.* Asset, weapon, prosthetic, partial alter, and crime-scene-cleanup-on-wheels.
- *The apartment.* Defensive position; sole sanctuary for Gabe.
- *Neighborhood network.* Mechanics, street racers, taqueria owners, neighborhood elders — a soft mesh of people who will not talk to outsiders. This is subject's most underrated tradecraft asset and the one he cannot replicate elsewhere. It is why he refuses to relocate.

**Resource posture.** Subject is *resource-poor and infrastructure-rich in one specific micro-geography.* This is the operational opposite of an Avengers-tier asset profile. Take him out of East L.A. and his effectiveness as a person (distinct from his effectiveness as the Rider) degrades sharply. His repeated insistence on going home after cosmic engagements is not sentimentality; it is *correct asset-management.*

---

### 6.5 Patterns of Action: The Weekly Operational Rhythm

The subject's life runs on a tight, repetitive weekday cycle that doubles as cover and as containment.

- **Pre-dawn (approx. 0500–0630):** Wakes early. Quiet movement so as not to rouse Gabe. Coffee, basic breakfast prep for Gabe. Often runs a hand over the Charger's hood in the alley before leaving — observable ritual, function unknown but consistent (assessment: spiritual check-in with Eli / the Rider, or simple proprioceptive grounding).
- **Morning (0700–1430):** School. Subject is academically functional but disengaged, low participation, often visibly fatigued. Sits near exits.
- **Afternoon (1430–1900):** Canelo's. Mechanical work. Most reliable mood-regulation window of his day. Affect is at its highest baseline during garage hours.
- **Early evening (1900–2100):** Home with Gabe. Dinner, homework help, conversation, occasional television, lifting/transfers as needed. *The only window in which his affective range fully opens.* If under-the-file profilers want to know who this subject is, watch this window.
- **Late evening (2100–0100):** Variable. Either continued garage work, or — increasingly — Rider operations. Patrol is not formal; it is opportunistic, triggered by what he heard during the day at school, on the street, or at the shop.
- **Sleep (0100–0500):** Short. Fragmented. Assessment: chronic sleep debt, never paid down.

**Weekend variation:** Saturdays are long garage days plus extended Gabe time (parks, library, the occasional outing). Sundays are quieter, with more Gabe-centered routine and more vehicular maintenance. Subject does not observe religious practice publicly, though his moral architecture has the residue of Catholic working-class East L.A. (the refusal to kill, the shame structure, the language of damnation when he speaks of Eli at all).

**Operational tempo signature.** Subject is *not* a constant patroller. He does not seek engagements. Operations are reactive, triggered by acquired intelligence about specific predators in his radius. The pattern is closer to a neighborhood watch with hellfire than to a Spider-style patrol grid. He will go weeks without transforming if the neighborhood is quiet. This restraint is itself a tell — most Spirits of Vengeance bearers transform far more often.

---

### 6.6 The Vehicle as Operational Platform

The Charger merits its own subsection because it is not equipment — it is *infrastructure, weapon, comms, sanctuary, and partial body.*

- *As mobility:* Range is theoretically unlimited (hellfire-augmented engine); practical range is whatever keeps him within Gabe-response distance, typically the L.A. basin.
- *As weapon:* Ramming platform. Hellfire-projection chassis. Can drive through structures and adversaries. Doors and frame function as shields when fighting dismounted.
- *As armor:* Subject re-enters the vehicle when wounded. Healing appears to accelerate inside the cabin. Whether this is occult or psychological is undetermined; both are operational.
- *As comms:* The radio. Subject talks to Eli, and Eli sometimes speaks through the radio rather than internally. The vehicle is the medium of the possession dialogue as well as the medium of transit.
- *As cover:* See 6.3. Conspicuous-car-as-witness-decoy.
- *As ritual object:* Subject's pre-departure hand-on-hood gesture; his post-engagement washdown; his decompression drive. The car is the locus of every transitional ritual he has.
- *As liability:* The car is identifiable. Lose the car, lose mobility and partial somatic integration. Any actor wanting to neutralize subject targets the Charger first.

Maintenance discipline on the vehicle is fanatical — daily walk-around, fluids checked weekly, regular detail work. He treats the car the way a sniper treats a rifle.

---

### 6.7 Post-Engagement Behavior and the Shame Cycle

Consistent across writers and arcs, subject exhibits a recognizable post-engagement sequence:

1. **De-transformation, typically in the car, typically while driving.** The flame recedes, the voice returns to its quieter register. He does not de-transform in front of witnesses if avoidable.
2. **Physical inventory.** He checks his hands, his face in the rearview, his clothes for blood or scorch. Quick, efficient, repeated.
3. **Vehicle inventory.** Damage assessment on the Charger. Mental triage list for the next garage session.
4. **Cover restoration.** Drives to the shop or to an alley; cleans the car, washes hands and face if water available, re-zips the hoodie, recomposes posture before approaching home.
5. **Re-entry to Gabe's environment.** Affect adjustment from operator to brother. This transition is observable in micro-expression and posture change.
6. **Shame interval, delayed.** Late at night, alone, after Gabe is asleep, subject sits quietly — often in the kitchen or on the apartment's small balcony/landing — and processes the engagement. If Eli broke the line (lethal or near-lethal force used non-volitionally), this interval extends and subject's affect degrades for days afterward. Sleep worsens. Garage hours increase.

This shame-cycle is itself an operational asset and liability. *Asset* because it keeps him calibrated, prevents drift toward Eli's preferences, and maintains the moral architecture that distinguishes him from the entities he carries. *Liability* because the cumulative load is unsustainable, and the assessment is that without intervention or relational support beyond Gabe, the cycle will eventually fracture — either through burnout-collapse or through a single engagement that breaks the refusal-to-kill line in a way he cannot recover from.

---

### 6.8 Signature Tells

A field observer with a week of coverage on subject would catalog the following:

- **Hood up indoors when stressed.** Comfort posture; also concealment.
- **Right hand to the back of the neck** when negotiating with Eli internally. Frequent, unconscious.
- **Jaw clench and held breath** in the half-second before transformation. The transformation is preceded by a microvolitional moment — he *allows* it. This is operationally important; it means transformation is not purely reflexive.
- **Eye drop when complimented.** Cannot receive praise. Looks at the floor, the engine, the workbench. Changes the subject.
- **Switches to Spanish under high emotion**, particularly with Gabe and with neighborhood elders. Operational language baseline is English-dominant code-switched; emotional baseline is Spanish-coded.
- **Touches the Charger before any significant decision.** Hand on the hood, the fender, the door. Consistent.
- **Will not sit with his back to a door.**
- **Eats standing up.** Almost never sits to a meal for himself; sits to a meal with Gabe.
- **Pockets a tool unconsciously** (a small wrench, a screwdriver) when leaving the garage. Carries it through the day. A talisman as much as a tool.
- **Goes quiet, not loud, when angry.** Volume drops, sentences shorten, eye contact intensifies. The escalation tell is *decreased* output, not increased.
- **Leaves rooms early.** Particularly social rooms. Average dwell time at any non-operational gathering is short.
- **Will not pose for photographs.** Drifts to the edge of frames, turns away, finds a reason to be elsewhere.
- **The chain coils left-over-right** when he stows it. Consistent. Identifying.
- **The Charger's engine note idles slightly higher than factory** — he keeps it tuned to instant-launch readiness. This is itself a posture: the car is always ready to go.

---

### 6.9 Operational Summary

Subject is a *micro-jurisdictional operator with macro-capability,* deliberately constraining his footprint to a geography he can hold, a dependent he can protect, and a moral line he can defend. His tradecraft is not professional in origin; it is the convergence of working-class labor discipline, gang-neighborhood survival behavior, mechanical craftsmanship, and improvised supernatural containment. It is unusually effective because every layer reinforces the others: the garage is cover and income and self-regulation; the car is weapon and concealment and ritual; the silence is OPSEC and trauma-defense and personality. Remove any one layer and the others compensate. Remove Gabe and the entire architecture collapses.

He should be modeled, by any party tracking him, as a subject whose operational ceiling is far above his operational ambition. He is capable of vastly more than he does. He chooses not to. The choice is the file's central operational fact.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Worldview & Operational Code

---

### 6.1 Preamble: The Shape of the Map

Robbie Reyes does not have a philosophy in the academic sense. He has never read Aurelius, never quoted scripture beyond what got recited at a relative's funeral, never sat in a classroom long enough to memorize a creed. What he has instead is an *operational code* — a working ruleset, assembled the way he assembles an engine: part by part, from things that worked, things that hurt, and things he watched fail other people. It is internally coherent, ruthlessly tested against reality, and almost entirely tacit. Asked to articulate it, he would shrug. Observed across the canonical record, it maps with uncommon consistency.

The dossier reads his worldview as **localist, particularist, materialist, fatalist-with-loopholes, and morally absolutist on a small number of axes** — with everything else triaged.

---

### 6.2 The World, As He Reads It

**The world is dangerous and indifferent.** This is the bedrock cognition, set before the supernatural ever touched him. East Los Angeles taught it; his father confirmed it; the men who shot him in the trunk-money exchange finalized it. Robbie does not believe in a benevolent order, nor in the special protection of the innocent. Bad things happen to children in wheelchairs. Bad things happen to mothers. Bad things happen to boys who steal a car for one good reason. The universe does not adjust its docket for merit.

**Most people are not coming to help.** Not because most people are evil — he does not believe that either — but because most people are scared, busy, or compromised, and the few who *would* help are usually outnumbered. He has watched neighbors close blinds during a beating. He has watched teachers see Gabe's bruise and write nothing down. His baseline expectation is that the cavalry is not en route and the institution is not your friend. This is not cynicism. It is fieldwork.

**Cruelty is the signature of weakness.** A genuine Robbie-conviction, derived in opposition to his father and reinforced by Eli. The cruel man is a man who needs to feel large. Robbie reads cruelty as confession — *this person is afraid, and is taking the fear out on a smaller target.* This is why he is contemptuous rather than impressed by neighborhood enforcers, by Hyde's lieutenants, by demons who monologue. The performance disgusts him before the violence does.

**The strong owe the weak.** Not as obligation imposed from outside — as the only thing strength is *for.* If you can lift, you lift. If you can stand between, you stand between. If you cannot, you find a way to. This is not articulated as ethics; it is articulated as common sense, the way a mechanic might say *if you have the wrench, use the wrench.* It is the closest thing in him to a religious commitment.

**The world is local.** Robbie's moral universe has a radius, and the radius is small. It contains Gabe, the garage, Canelo, a handful of named neighbors, a handful of named children on the block. Beyond that radius the world becomes abstract — *people*, not faces — and his concern attenuates. He is not callous to distant suffering; he is *unable to operationalize it.* When the Avengers ask him to care about the cosmos, the cosmos does not load into his moral imagination as actionable. The block does.

---

### 6.3 Conflict — Theory of

**Conflict is a tool failure.** Robbie's default reading of any conflict is that *something broke earlier* — a system, a family, a promise, a screw torqued wrong — and the conflict is the noise the broken thing is now making. This is the mechanic's epistemology applied to social life. Therefore his first instinct in a fight is rarely escalation; it is **diagnosis.** *Why is this person here? What do they actually need? What broke?* Once diagnosed, most conflicts can be de-escalated, redirected, or absorbed.

**Violence is a last-resort tool with a high cost-of-use.** Robbie does not believe violence solves things; he believes it *stops* things. Stopping is sometimes necessary. Solving requires the slower work afterward. He resents heroes (and adversaries) who treat violence as expressive — as catharsis, as theater, as identity. To him, violence is the wrench he picks up when no other wrench fits, and he resents needing it.

**Once committed, finish cleanly.** This is the operator's counterweight to the reluctance above. Robbie does not believe in half-measures inside a violent encounter. Hesitation gets dependents killed. Once the line is crossed — once de-escalation is off the table — the engagement is to be *concluded,* not extended. He will not posture, monologue, or showboat. He will end it and walk away. The Rider, left to its own preferences, would extend and savor; Robbie consistently truncates.

**Lethal force is the line.** Across writers, the load-bearing operational constraint. Robbie will maim, terrify, dismember property, sin-burn — but the conscious refusal to kill is the spine of his code. Two reasons, both derived: (1) killing is what his father / Eli / the gang are *for*; to do it is to confirm the inheritance; (2) Gabe's gaze, internalized, audits every act. A killer cannot be Gabe's brother in the way Robbie needs to be Gabe's brother. The constraint slips only under Eli's hijack, and the post-event shame is total.

**Civilian containment is non-negotiable.** Wherever possible, Robbie fights *away from* people. He moves engagements into industrial zones, alleys, his own garage, the road. This is partly tactical (the Charger needs road), partly moral (collateral haunts him). When he cannot move the fight, his priority order in the fight changes: civilian extraction first, threat reduction second, victory third.

---

### 6.4 Control — Theory of

**Control is a discipline, not a possession.** Robbie does not believe he *has* control; he believes he *practices* it, daily, and it is always provisional. The Eli problem makes this literal — he is a man whose interior is contested — but the conviction predates Eli. He learned in childhood that the man who believed he was in control (his father, drunk) was the man most out of it. From this: *the felt sense of control is a warning sign.* If he ever feels solidly in command, he is about to be ambushed by his own complacency.

**Self-control is the only kind that matters.** He does not try to control Gabe (notably — he protects without micromanaging Gabe's autonomy, even as Gabe grows). He does not try to control his teammates, his neighborhood, his future. He tries to control *himself,* moment by moment, and treats every other lever as illusory. This is partly trauma-shaped (the world has demonstrated itself uncontrollable) and partly mechanic-shaped (you cannot tune what you do not own).

**Routine is control's substrate.** Hence the rigidity of his daily structure (see Section 9). Wake at the same hour. Same breakfast for Gabe. Same route to school. Same shift at Canelo's. Same toolbox order. Same parking spot. Routine is not preference; routine is the *scaffolding* on which self-control is possible. Disruption of routine is felt as threat, not as inconvenience.

**Power is a liability until proven otherwise.** A defining inversion. Most superhumans in his cohort treat power as identity-positive. Robbie treats it as *exposure* — a thing that attracts attention, recruits enemies, invites mythic framing, and asks more of him than it gives. He uses the power; he does not enjoy it; he does not accumulate more of it. Offered a throne (King of Hell), he abdicates. Offered a team, he attends, performs, and leaves. The operational rule: *take only the power required by the immediate problem, and put it down afterward.*

**Refusal is a capability.** Robbie has discovered, through repeated tests, that *no* is itself a usable instrument. He has refused Eli, refused Hellstrom, refused various claimants to his service, refused Avengers recruitment-in-spirit even while showing up to missions. The refusal is rarely loud. It is usually a silence, a walk-away, a *no, I'm going home.* He treats refusal the way a strong negotiator treats walk-away power: as the thing that gives every other position its meaning.

---

### 6.5 Trust — Theory of

**Trust is earned in increments and revoked in lumps.** Robbie extends trust slowly, on small tests — *did you do what you said you would do; did you talk about me when I wasn't there; did you treat the cashier well.* He keeps mental ledgers. He revokes trust catastrophically and almost permanently on betrayal. This is consistent with his attachment profile: low base trust, high loyalty once established, minimal recoverability after rupture.

**Trust is granted to people, not roles.** He does not trust *the police*; he might trust a specific officer who proved themselves. He does not trust *the Avengers*; he trusts certain individual Avengers in narrow contexts. He does not trust *doctors*; he might trust a particular doctor who once treated Gabe without condescension. The grain of his trust map is individual, never institutional.

**The trustworthy are identified by what they do when no one is watching.** Robbie watches. He notices who is consistent across audiences, who alters tone for power, who is polite to Gabe when Gabe is the only one in the room. This is one of the most stable assessment heuristics in the file — and one of the reasons he can read room dynamics faster than his social impoverishment would suggest.

**He does not trust himself.** This is the load-bearing asymmetry. Robbie's trust in his own moral instrument is provisional at best. He believes his judgment can be hijacked (Eli has done it). He believes his anger can scale past his intention. He believes his love for Gabe can be weaponized against his ethics. Therefore he installs external constraints: routines, refusals, the avoidance of power. The self-distrust is functional — it is the source of his discipline — but it is also the source of his loneliness.

**Disclosure is the currency of trust, and he is poor.** Robbie does not give information away. To trust someone enough to *tell them something* is the highest tier, almost never reached. Even with Gabe — the person he loves most — he concealed the Rider for as long as he could. Concealment is, in his code, the *default* protective posture; disclosure is the rare exception requiring justification.

---

### 6.6 Risk — Theory of

**Risk is asymmetric and must be borne by the person best positioned to bear it.** Robbie's risk calculus is not utilitarian and not balanced; it is *load-bearing.* He believes risk should fall on whoever can survive it best, and in any room he is in, he assumes that is him. He has died once; he regenerates; he carries a hell-engine. The math, to him, is obvious. He takes the risk. He does not negotiate the distribution.

**Risk to self is acceptable to a near-suicidal degree.** This is the passive ideation surfacing as operational policy. Robbie will absorb damage, take the wound, accept the possession, walk into the trap, that others (especially Gabe) do not have to. He does not frame this as bravery. He frames it as *role.*

**Risk to dependents is intolerable.** Inverse and absolute. Any plan whose risk-tail includes Gabe is rejected, full stop, regardless of expected value. This is the one place where his rationality breaks cleanly. He will accept a worse expected outcome to remove Gabe from the variance.

**Risk to strangers requires conscious management.** Civilian collateral is a planning constraint, not a hope. He pre-positions encounters to minimize bystander exposure. When forced into populated theaters, his combat style narrows — shorter chains, tighter hellfire, more grappling than projection.

**Uncertainty is preferable to false certainty.** Robbie distrusts plans that require everything to go right. He builds in fallback positions, alternate exits, contingency cash, hidden tools. The mechanic's instinct: *assume the part will fail; have the replacement on the shelf.* He would rather operate under acknowledged uncertainty than execute a confident plan whose confidence he does not share.

**The Rider is, itself, an unmanaged risk.** The interior risk he cannot fully model. He treats it the way a man treats a fault in a load-bearing wall — daily inspection, no excess weight, evacuation route planned. The fact that he lives with the unmanaged risk does not mean he has accepted it; it means he has not yet figured out how to remove it.

---

### 6.7 Authority, Institutions, Hierarchy

**Authority is suspect until tested.** Robbie's prior with institutions is uniformly bad — Child Protective Services that did not protect, schools that did not see, police whose presence was net-negative on his block, hospitals that billed his mother into immobility. He does not start from a posture of compliance. He starts from a posture of *let me see what this actually does.*

**Hierarchy is a coordination tool, not a status reality.** Inside a mission, he will take direction from whoever has the relevant expertise or the better vantage. Outside a mission, he does not acknowledge that the person who outranked him an hour ago outranks him now. The Avengers' command structure registers to him as workplace-only — and even within work, he is the employee who arrives, performs, and leaves without lingering by the watercooler.

**He distrusts charisma.** A specific and consistent allergy. Charismatic figures — Blaze when grandstanding, Hellstrom when seductive, demons who monologue, politicians, recruiters of any kind — trigger his suspicion register hard. Charisma is, in his read, a tool for getting people to do things they would not do under quieter conditions. He prefers the company of the laconic, the technical, the bluntly competent.

**Money he understands; loyalty oaths he does not.** Transactional relationships are legible to him. He has worked for wages; he has owed and been owed; he respects a contract. The mystic compact, the team oath, the cosmic prophecy — none of these load. He will help because someone needs help, or because he was paid, or because a promise was made to a specific person. He will not help because he was *chosen.*

**Government and capital are forces of weather, not parties to negotiate with.** Robbie does not believe he can affect them; he believes he can route around them. His political imagination is small and tactical: *keep the apartment, keep the job, keep Gabe out of the system, keep the Charger off impound lists.* The macro-political stage does not exist as a venue for him. This is not depoliticization — it is the politics of those who have learned that voting did not stop the eviction.

---

### 6.8 Family, Blood, Inheritance

**Family is chosen by act, not by blood.** The defining ideological position. Robbie's blood family delivered him an abuser and a parasite (Eli is literal blood — the great-uncle whose violence now lives in him). His *real* family is the one he tends: Gabe primarily, Canelo functionally, the neighborhood at the edges. He believes — though he would not articulate it this way — that the genealogical claim is the weakest one, and the caretaking claim is the strongest.

**Inheritance is a trap to be refused, not a destiny to be fulfilled.** Eli is the literalization. Robbie's father is the rehearsal. Both offer him a script: *this is what the Reyes men do.* His entire moral identity is built around the refusal of that script. This is why mythic framings of the Rider lineage (you are a chosen Spirit of Vengeance; this was always your role) land so badly with him — they look like another version of the inheritance trap, dressed up in fire.

**Children are sacred and non-targets.** Inviolable. A combat axiom that is also a moral axiom. Threats to children collapse his de-escalation hierarchy instantly. This is the single most reliable trigger for full Rider expression. It is also the criterion by which he sorts adversaries — those who threaten children are categorized as the worst, and treated accordingly.

**The disabled and the dependent are sacred and non-targets.** Same axiom, extended. Gabe-shaped. Anyone who treats a wheelchair, a cognitive difference, an obvious vulnerability as an opportunity is, in Robbie's taxonomy, beneath consideration as a person and merits no de-escalation effort.

---

### 6.9 Self-Concept Inside the System

**He is a tool, not a hero.** A self-description he would offer if pressed. Robbie does not believe in the heroic identity. He believes there is a job, and someone has to do it, and the supernatural lottery picked him, and complaining about being picked is a waste of time better spent doing the job. He does not crave the recognition that other Riders have variously sought (Blaze's notoriety, Ketch's tragic register). He would prefer that no one knew his name.

**He is dangerous and must be supervised.** Self-supervised, since he does not trust others to do it. The contamination self-schema runs deep enough that he genuinely believes Gabe is safer when Robbie is *vigilant about Robbie.* The result is a quasi-monastic discipline: no drinking, no drugs, no fights he did not have to be in, no power he did not have to use, no relationships that could leverage him.

**He is replaceable in heroics, irreplaceable at home.** The asymmetry organizes his time. The Avengers can find another striker; Gabe cannot find another brother. Every cosmic mission is, in his head, a debit against the only account that matters. He does the missions because the missions arrive at his door and he cannot refuse them without consequence — but he treats them as time stolen.

**He is on borrowed time and behaves accordingly.** Having died once, Robbie operates with the affect of a man who knows the warranty is expired. This produces both the recklessness about self-risk and the urgency about Gabe — *if I have until the next bullet, then everything I build for Gabe has to be built now.* This is one of the under-examined drivers of his work ethic.

---

### 6.10 Time, Future, Hope

**The future is a place where Gabe is safe.** Not where Robbie is happy, married, retired. The horizon of his planning is Gabe-shaped: Gabe with stable housing, Gabe with continuity of care, Gabe with someone other than Robbie able to step in if Robbie does not survive. The dossier reads Robbie's future-imagination as almost entirely instrumental and almost entirely about contingencies for his own absence.

**Hope is rationed.** He does not allow himself extended optimism. He has learned that the times he hoped most (the prize-money race; the trunk full of who-knows-what that would *fix things*) were the times the world hit him hardest. His current setting is *cautious incrementalism* — small wins, banked quietly, no celebration.

**Atonement is daily, not climactic.** Robbie does not believe in a single act that would make him clean. He believes in showing up tomorrow, doing the work, refusing the bad option, taking the wound. He is suspicious of redemption arcs as narratives — they smell, to him, like the kind of story people tell themselves to skip the hard parts. The hard parts *are* the redemption, in his code, and they do not end.

**Death does not frighten him; failing Gabe does.** Operationally relevant. Any threat actor modeling him on fear-of-death will mis-predict. The fear that moves him is fear of *Gabe alone, Gabe unprotected, Gabe seeing what his brother became.* This is the only fear lever that reliably works on him, and it is the lever he most vigorously guards.

---

### 6.11 The Code, As He Would (Reluctantly) State It

Compressed from observation, in the register he might actually use if cornered into articulating it — short sentences, no theory:

- *Take care of your people. Start with the ones in the room.*
- *Don't be the man who hits.*
- *Don't be the man who kills.*
- *Fix what you can fix. Leave what you can't for later, and remember it.*
- *Don't take a job you can't put down.*
- *Don't take power you don't need.*
- *Show up on time. Do the work. Get paid. Go home.*
- *Watch who you tell.*
- *If something's coming for them, it goes through you first.*
- *If you have to do it, do it quick, do it once, and don't talk about it after.*
- *The car runs because someone takes care of the car. Same for everything.*

---

### 6.12 Synthesis

Robbie Reyes operates on a code built for a small radius, tested in a hard neighborhood, and now load-bearing for problems several orders of magnitude larger than the code was designed for. It holds — barely, daily — because its core axioms (protect the dependent, refuse the inheritance, use only the power required, finish what you start, go home) are unusually stable and unusually well-defended. It is the code of a parentified working-class adolescent who has died once, who carries a murderer in his skull, and who has decided, without ceremony, that the appropriate response to all of that is to keep the garage open, keep Gabe fed, and refuse, daily, to become the thing the world keeps offering him.

The Rider is the noise. The code is the signal. The code was set before the fire, and the fire has not yet rewritten it.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Moral & Ethical Framework

---

## 6.1 Preliminary Note: Enacted vs. Professed

Robbie Reyes does not articulate a moral philosophy. He has never delivered a creed, a manifesto, a speech to a teammate about what he believes, or a confession about what he will not do.
