The closest he comes to ethical self-statement is short, defensive, and almost always reactive: *"I'm not gonna kill him."* *"Gabe can't see this."* *"That's not me."* *"Leave him alone."* The ethical content of his life has to be reconstructed from behavior — from what he does under pressure, what he refuses under coercion, and the gap between what Eli wants and what his hands actually do.

This is a working-class, Catholic-cultural, parentified-eldest-son ethical formation. It is not a system; it is a set of locked-in reflexes that have been pressure-tested for years before any cosmic actor took an interest in him. The supernatural did not give him morals. It threatened the morals he already had.

---

## 6.2 The Hard Floor: What He Will Not Do

These are the absolute prohibitions. The record shows them as consistent across writers, across years, across coercion levels approaching the maximum a mortal can absorb.

**He will not kill.** This is the ground line. Even in the original All-New run, faced with Hyde's men — the men who actually murdered him — Robbie refuses lethal force, and the refusal is not hedged. He brutalizes, he terrifies, he maims at the edges, but he does not finish. Eli pushes constantly; Robbie pushes back constantly. The prohibition is not framed as squeamishness or as a quasi-religious doctrine about taking life. It is framed, in his internal logic, as the line that separates him from his father and from Eli: cross it and the difference dissolves. Killing is not wrong in the abstract for Robbie; killing is the act that would *make him into the thing he refuses to be*. The ethics are identity-protective rather than principled, and that makes them stronger, not weaker — they are loaded with everything he has.

**He will not hurt children, the disabled, or the visibly defenseless.** The Rider's sin-detection / penance-style gaze appears keyed in practice to predation. Robbie's transformations cluster around the predator/prey axis: when he encounters someone hurting a kid, an elder, a person who cannot fight back, the threshold drops to nearly zero. Conversely, when he encounters a peer-level opponent who has not crossed that axis, he is reluctant, slow, often disengaging if the fight can end without one. The asymmetry is the moral code in action.

**He will not let Gabe become a weapon against him, even at the cost of his own soul.** When Eli body-jumps into Gabe at the end of vol. 1, Robbie's resolution — reabsorb Eli into himself, take the contamination back — is the prototype. Any time the dilemma can be resolved by Robbie taking the wound personally, that is what he does. He will not pay for his safety with someone else's body, and he will especially not pay with Gabe's.

**He will not accept thrones, mantles, or institutional elevation.** When offered the kingship of Hell, he abdicates. When recruited by the Avengers, he attends but does not integrate. When framed as a chosen one in the Spirits-of-Vengeance lineage, he treats the frame as noise. This is moral as well as temperamental: he believes that accepting these positions would require him to start making *categorical* decisions about people he does not know, and he does not believe he has the right or the standing to do that. The refusal of power is ethics in him, not modesty.

**He will not lie to Gabe about substantive things, though he will conceal.** This is a fine but consistent distinction. Robbie hides the Rider for as long as he can; he does not, when pressed, manufacture false stories. When Gabe asks, Robbie's pattern is to deflect, change subject, or fall silent — not to construct a deception. The integrity of *the relationship* trumps the integrity of *the secret*; once the secret threatens the relationship, the secret breaks first.

**He will not work for anyone whose project is cruelty.** He has been offered alignments by figures across the demonic, criminal, and cosmic registers. He turns them down, sometimes with violence, sometimes by walking away. The disqualifying criterion is not legality — Robbie has no faith in legality — but the *use* the work would put him to.

---

## 6.3 The Hard Floor: What He Will Do

The prohibitions are matched by an equally clear list of things he will absolutely do, often things other heroes hedge about.

**He will steal when the alternative is Gabe going without.** The Charger itself is stolen. He has lifted parts, cut corners on inventory at the garage in dialogue-implication, run a contraband car in a street race for prize money. He treats property crime against the indifferent as morally trivial. The working-class read: property law is the rule the people who have everything use against the people who have nothing. He does not endorse this as theory; he simply does not respect property as a moral object when measured against Gabe's needs.

**He will hospitalize, maim, and terrorize.** Within the no-kill floor, the ceiling is very high. He will throw a man through a wall. He will set someone on fire short of death. He will use the chain to break bones. He will allow Eli's threats to come out of his own mouth, in the deep-voiced Rider register, to a target who needs to be made to stop. He understands, in practice, that *deterrence requires demonstration*, and he is willing to be the demonstration.

**He will break and enter, drive without license, evade law enforcement, and refuse to identify himself.** Police are not in his ethical universe as legitimate authority. They are an environmental hazard to be routed around, like the gangs. He is not anti-police as a stance; he is *prior-to-police* — they were never an option in his neighborhood for the kind of problems he had, so they are not now.

**He will work himself into the ground for money owed.** Wage labor is sacred to him in a way that nothing else institutional is. He shows up to Canelo's. He completes jobs. He undercharges customers he likes. He pays rent on time even when supernatural calamity is in progress. The dignity of paid work is one of the very few inherited civic virtues he actively endorses.

**He will absorb the harm before he displaces it.** This is doctrinal for him. Faced with a binary — someone has to take this wound, this curse, this guilt — he takes it. It is the *signature*. It is also the most dangerous thing about him morally, because it is a virtue with a sharp edge: it makes him a chronically poor partner to anyone who would share the load.

---

## 6.4 The Justification Architecture (Such As It Is)

Robbie does not justify in language. He justifies in *direction of attention*. The structure can be reverse-engineered:

- **Proximity ethics.** Distance attenuates obligation. Gabe, then the block, then the neighborhood, then East L.A., then strangers in front of him, then everyone else in a flat undifferentiated outer band. He does not feel responsibility for the world. He feels responsibility for what is in front of him and for what depends on him. The Avengers' globalist moral horizon is not his — and when he is conscripted into it, he performs without believing.
- **Dependency creates duty.** The strongest moral pull is exerted by people who cannot help themselves. This is partly the parentification, partly the Catholic substrate (corporal works of mercy), partly the simple fact that he knows what it is to be a child whom no adult was protecting.
- **Identity preservation as moral filter.** Many decisions are made not by asking *what is right* but by asking *would this make me into him* — *him* being his father at the bottom of the stack, Eli at the middle, and the gang leadership of the Catrinas at the top. Anything that aligns him with any of those silhouettes is rejected, sometimes against tactical interest.
- **Negative-form moral reasoning.** He knows what he refuses far more clearly than what he affirms. The shape of his ethics is a list of *nots*. This is consistent with C-PTSD-shaped moral cognition: the survivor knows the wounds intimately and orients away from re-creating them, without a complementary positive vision of flourishing.
- **No metaphysical ledger.** Despite carrying a Spirit of Vengeance, Robbie does not appear to believe in cosmic justice, divine reward, or karmic balancing in any operational way. The hellfire works; the afterlife evidently exists; he does not draw comfort or instruction from any of it. His ethics are this-worldly. The Rider's mythic apparatus is a tool he is forced to operate, not a worldview he has adopted.

---

## 6.5 Where the Code is Consistent

Across a decade of stories and multiple writers, the consistencies are striking enough to be diagnostic.

- **The no-kill line holds.** Not perfectly — see fractures below — but the pattern across All-New Ghost Rider, the Waid Avengers run, the Aaron Avengers run, Damnation, the Cates Ghost Rider, and the Percy solo is that Robbie ends arcs without bodies he personally and consciously claimed. When kills occur in his vicinity, they are framed as Eli's, as accidental, as in self-defense at the moment of resurrection, or as collateral — and Robbie's reaction to them is uniformly distress, not satisfaction.
- **Gabe is always first.** No writer has broken this. Cosmic stakes, kingship offers, infernal politics — Gabe outranks them.
- **Power refusal is total.** The kingship abdication, the Avengers half-attendance, the consistent retreat to the garage. There is no run in which Robbie acquires authority and likes it.
- **Cruelty to the helpless is the trigger that does not miss.** Every writer who needs to escalate Robbie reaches for the same lever: a child, a brother-figure, a defenseless target. It works every time because it is the part of the code that does not flex.
- **Concealment over deception.** He hides; he does not fabricate. The texture of his secrecy is consistent.
- **Working-class refusal of charity.** He has never accepted housing from a teammate, a stipend from the Avengers, a payout from a grateful client beyond fair wage. The line is observed even when it costs him.

---

## 6.6 Where the Code Fractures

The honest portion of the file. The fractures are not failures of character; they are the points where the code's design tolerances are exceeded.

- **The Rider state as moral plausible deniability.** This is the largest and most uncomfortable fracture. Robbie's no-kill commitment is a *Robbie* commitment; the Rider — particularly when Eli surges — operates by a different rule set. Acts performed in transformation that exceed Robbie's waking limits get filed under *not-quite-me*, even though they came out of his body. The dissociative architecture (Section 4) is also a moral architecture: it lets him claim a clean line while standing next to a smoking outcome. He is not lying about this — the agency-attribution problem is real, both clinically and metaphysically — but it is *useful*, and it lets the code survive contact with consequences it could not otherwise tolerate.
- **The proximity ethic at scale.** When the Avengers ask him to take action against a distant, abstract threat — a cosmic entity, a continental-scale incursion — his engagement is shallow. He shows up, performs, leaves. The fracture is that this works only as long as someone else is doing the global thinking. If the Avengers' globalist frame collapsed and the world-scale calls fell to him, his ethic has no answer; he would default to *go home and protect Gabe*, and the rest of the world would have to fend for itself. This is a coherent moral stance, but it is a stance, and it has costs he has not been forced to confront.
- **Concealment harms the people he most wants to protect.** Hiding the Rider from Gabe was, in his framing, an act of love; in effect, it placed Gabe in greater danger by denying him operational awareness of the threats around them. Robbie's defensive concealment style produces, structurally, the kind of vulnerability for Gabe that he is trying to prevent. He has only partially absorbed this lesson.
- **The shame axis distorts judgment.** When the choice is between *Gabe sees me as a monster* and *a worse tactical outcome*, Robbie reliably picks the worse tactical outcome. This is not a small fracture; it has cost him operational position in arcs where transparency would have served everyone. The shame is older than the Rider, and it overrides reason in its presence.
- **He will not kill, but he will let die.** There are moments in the record where Robbie's hard line against *his own* killing functions as a permission slip to walk away from a situation where someone else's killing — or someone's death by inaction — is the result. He has not been heavily tested on the trolley-problem axis, but the pattern suggests he treats moral hygiene as personal, not consequentialist. He keeps his own hands clean; what happens after he walks out of the room is filed elsewhere.
- **Eli sometimes wins.** Across runs, there are moments — under extremity, under deception, under threat to Gabe — when Eli's wishes route through Robbie's body to outcomes Robbie would not have chosen. The shame-cycle that follows is itself part of the code (he punishes himself for the slip, often by deeper isolation), but the fact remains: the no-kill floor has cracked under Eli's pressure, and the cracks are part of the picture.
- **The dependent-protection ethic does not extend evenly.** Robbie is reliably mobilized by *children and the visibly disabled*. He is less reliably mobilized by adults who are vulnerable in less legible ways — addicts, sex workers, the chronically mentally ill, undocumented adults afraid to come forward. His moral radar was calibrated on Gabe's specific kind of dependency. Vulnerabilities that look different from Gabe's get less of his attention. He is not callous about them; he simply does not see them with the same clarity.
- **Atonement without confession.** His mode of penance is private. He does the work, takes the wound, says nothing. This is consistent with his character but ethically incomplete: there are people owed acknowledgment whom he has never approached because acknowledgment would require speech, exposure, the breaking of concealment. The atonement that costs only him is the atonement he is willing to perform; the atonement that requires him to be *seen* atoning is one he avoids.

---

## 6.7 Shifts Over Time

The code is unusually stable for a comics character spanning multiple writers, but there are inflection points.

- **Pre-resurrection baseline.** The code in its first form is essentially defensive: do not provoke gangs, do not become father, work hard, get money, get Gabe out. The horizon is one neighborhood and one brother. Moral imagination is narrow because the bandwidth allotted to morality is narrow — survival is consuming most of the budget.
- **First post-resurrection year (All-New, vol. 1).** The code expands under duress to include *do not kill, do not let Eli win, do not let Gabe see.* The no-kill rule, which had no occasion to be articulated before, becomes load-bearing because the means to kill is now constantly at hand and constantly being urged. This is the period of greatest moral clarity, because the dilemmas are still local and the stakes still legible.
- **Avengers integration (Waid, Aaron).** The code is stress-tested by exposure to scales it was not designed for. Robbie discovers that he does not have an ethics of mass casualty events, of cosmic politics, of mantle-bearing. His response is to *not develop one* — to perform the work and hold the local code unchanged. This is a deliberate refusal of moral expansion, and it is, in its way, an ethic of its own: *do not let the institution rewrite you*.
- **Damnation, infernal politics, the throne arcs.** The code is tested against power. Robbie refuses every elevation offered. The refusals harden into a stable subroutine: *I am not a king, not a chosen one, not a face of the Spirits.* The identity-preservation ethic, originally aimed at father and Eli, generalizes into a refusal of mythic identity altogether.
- **Cates and Percy era / mature Robbie.** The code begins to admit, very slowly, that *concealment was not always love*. Gabe's awareness, when it comes, is survivable. The garage is still the gravitational center, but Robbie tolerates — not embraces — the existence of a wider responsibility. He still leaves the room when destiny-talk starts, but he leaves with less force. The shame is slightly less acute. He has not become trusting; he has become, fractionally, less alone, and the code has flexed enough to accommodate that.

The trajectory, viewed end-to-end: a tightly held local ethic, defended against expansion by every available means, slowly and reluctantly admitting that some expansion is unavoidable, while keeping the core — Gabe, no-kill, no throne, no charity, no monster — intact.

---

## 6.8 Comparative Note

In the Spirits-of-Vengeance lineage, Robbie's ethical signature is distinct enough to be diagnostic of the character. Blaze's code is older, harder, framed around penance and damnation as cosmic facts he has accepted. Ketch's is romantic, theatrical, organized around personal grief. Robbie's is none of these things: it is the ethics of an eighteen-year-old mechanic with a younger brother, calibrated to a single block, accidentally fused to a cosmic engine. The infernal apparatus did not give him the code, and it has not, despite years of pressure, succeeded in replacing it. That stability is the most ethically important fact in the file.

The fairer comparison, outside the Riders, is to a certain pattern visible in the historical record of caretaker-eldest-children in survival-economy households — the ones who do not become saints and do not become criminals but instead become quietly, locally, durably *responsible*, and who carry that responsibility into contexts that should by all rights overwhelm it, and refuse to be overwhelmed. Robbie's ethics belong to that lineage. The hellfire is incidental.

---

## 6.9 Synthesis

Robbie Reyes's morality is best understood as a *perimeter*, not a *program*. He does not march toward an ideal; he holds a line. The line is drawn around Gabe, around the workbench, around the version of himself that still recognizes his own face. Inside the perimeter, his conduct is tender, exacting, and inexhaustible. At the perimeter, his conduct is violent, controlled, and bounded by the no-kill floor. Outside the perimeter, his conduct is functionally absent — not because he is indifferent, but because he has decided, correctly given his resources, that he cannot be responsible for what he cannot reach.

The code's strength is that it has survived: the abuse, the murder, the resurrection, the parasite, the kingship offers, the Avengers, the cosmic recruiters, the years. The code's weakness is that it has survived *by narrowing*, and the narrowing has costs — to him, to the people he could help and does not see, and to Gabe, whose protection has sometimes been compromised by the same concealment instincts meant to protect it.

The single most important sentence to put in the file, for any party who needs to predict him: *he will take the harm into himself before he will let it touch the dependent, and he will refuse to become the thing that hurt him, and he will do both of these things without explaining either.*


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

## 6.1 Baseline Speech Register

Subject's default communicative posture is **conservation of words**. Utterance length, measured across the canonical corpus from *All-New Ghost Rider* (2014) through the Percy solo run, clusters heavily in the one-to-seven-word range. Multi-clause sentences appear primarily in two contexts: (a) addressing Gabe, where syntax expands into full storytelling cadence, and (b) explaining mechanical/procedural matters, where he becomes uncharacteristically fluent. In every other context — Avengers briefings, encounters with Blaze or Ketch, dialogue with adversaries — he speaks in clipped declaratives, monosyllabic acknowledgments ("Yeah." / "No." / "Fine." / "I got it."), and sentence fragments that decline to elaborate.

This is not inarticulateness. It is **selected economy**. Robbie's vocabulary, when he chooses to deploy it, is precise; his grammar is consistent; his use of subordinate clauses around Gabe demonstrates intact higher-order syntactic capability. The terseness is an operational discipline learned in two pressure-cookers: the gang neighborhood (where saying more than necessary marks you) and the abusive household (where saying anything wrong invites violence). Speech is a controlled resource, not a relational currency.

**Voice quality:** Even, low-affect, mid-range. He does not raise his voice in argument; he lowers it. When stressed, he goes quieter, not louder — a classic abuse-survivor reversal of the normative escalation curve. The few moments of canonical shouting are reserved almost entirely for Gabe-in-danger callouts ("*Gabe!*") and for the moments immediately preceding transformation, after which the voice changes register entirely (see 6.7).

## 6.2 Code-Switching: A Three-Channel System

Robbie operates fluently across at least three linguistic registers, switching contextually and almost without conscious decision:

**Channel A — Domestic / Spanish-English code-mix with Gabe.** Inside the apartment, with Gabe, Robbie's speech loosens. He uses Spanglish naturally: terms of endearment in Spanish (*"hermanito,"* *"mijo"* on occasion, though that is more parental), dietary and household nouns in Spanish, jokes and chiding in a mix. He uses diminutives. His sentence rhythm lengthens; he tells small stories about his day at Canelo's, mostly fabricated or scrubbed of supernatural content. Pitch rises slightly; the words "okay?" and "you good?" recur as soft check-ins. This is the **only register in which his full affective range surfaces verbally.**

**Channel B — Garage / street / neighborhood vernacular.** With Canelo, with Guero (when applicable), with kids from the block, with neighborhood adults — a working East L.A. register. Light Chicano English features: *"nah," "naw," "órale,"* truncated greetings, mechanical jargon. He is comfortable here, fluent, brief. With Canelo specifically, he uses respect-markers (*"Sí, señor," "I got it, Canelo"*) and absorbs reprimand without contesting. With the Catrinas and gang-adjacent figures, he goes flat and minimal — a deliberate refusal to perform either deference or bravado.

**Channel C — Institutional / Avengers / outsider English.** With Vision, Wonder Man, Falcon, Captain Marvel, etc. — a stripped-down, careful, almost over-correct register. No slang. No Spanish. No idiom. He sounds younger and more closed than he actually is. The code-switch *up* into institutional speech is itself a tell: he is performing acceptability rather than relating. He answers questions; he does not ask them. He says "sir" and "ma'am" sparingly but uses them with figures he reads as authority. The Spanglish disappears entirely. This is the register of someone who learned early that outsiders weigh your words for evidence.

A fourth, marginal register exists with **Daimon Hellstrom, Blaze, Ketch, and other Rider-adjacent figures**, where Robbie speaks more openly about the supernatural condition but still withholds personal content. Here he asks technical questions ("Can it be cut out?" "How did you stop yours?"), treats the demonic the way he treats an engine knock — a problem with a possible repair.

## 6.3 Diction and Lexical Tells

**Frequent words and constructions, longitudinal:**
- *"I got it."* — Used to refuse help, close a topic, signal that he will handle a problem alone. Among his most-deployed phrases. The grammatical present-tense *got* (rather than *have*) is class- and region-marked and consistent throughout his corpus.
- *"It's fine."* / *"I'm fine."* — Deflection of inquiry into his state. Almost never true at moment of utterance.
- *"Don't."* — Used as a complete sentence, often quiet, to halt an unwanted line of conversation, an offered hand, an expression of sympathy. A boundary marker rather than an aggression.
- *"Leave him alone."* — Threat formulation, Gabe-context. The shift from passive to imperative in his voice tracks closely with proximity-to-transformation.
- *"You don't have to."* — Addressed to Gabe, to kids, to bystanders. A characteristic phrasing — he absolves others of obligation before extracting it.
- *"I'll figure it out."* — Future-tense version of *I got it.* Refusal to accept current assistance plus assertion of solo problem-solving. Recurs in financial, mechanical, and supernatural contexts equally.
- *"No."* — Whole-sentence refusals to mythic/cosmic framings. He says *no* to thrones, to mantles, to prophecies, to "chosen one" language. The single syllable is among the most consequential utterances in his corpus.

**Words and constructions he does not use:**
- Heroic vocabulary. He does not say *justice, mission, duty, calling, destiny*. He does not refer to himself as a hero, a Ghost Rider, a Spirit of Vengeance, or any honorific. He does not name the Charger.
- Self-pitying language. He does not say *I deserve* or *why me.* He does not narrate his suffering.
- Ideological vocabulary. No political abstractions, no moral generalizations. His ethics are stated, when at all, as one-line concrete refusals.
- Diminutives or affection for himself. He does not have a self-comforting inner lexicon that surfaces externally.
- Profanity at meaningful volume. He swears, but flatly, low-frequency, low-creativity — *damn*, *hell*, occasionally *cabrón* under his breath. He does not weaponize profanity the way Blaze does.

## 6.4 Conversational Architecture

**Turn-taking.** Robbie cedes the floor by default. In group settings he will go entire scenes without speaking unless directly addressed. When asked a question, his response latency is slightly longer than baseline — he is calibrating what is safe to say, not searching for content. He is comfortable with silence in a way that visibly discomfits interlocutors trained in normative conversational reciprocity (e.g., Vision noting his withdrawal; Wonder Man trying to draw him out).

**Question behavior.** He asks few. The questions he does ask are functional: locations, names, threat capabilities, what something does. He does not ask social or relational questions. He does not ask people about themselves. This is partly the parentified caretaker's habit (no one ever asks *him,* so he has no reciprocal frame) and partly operational discipline.

**Disclosure economy.** Robbie's self-disclosures are *zero-volume by default and only released under specific triggers:* (a) Gabe is the audience, (b) the disclosure is necessary to protect Gabe, or (c) he is speaking to another Rider who already understands the supernatural fact-pattern and the disclosure is technical rather than emotional. Voluntary emotional disclosure to a peer does not appear in his recorded corpus.

**Listening behavior.** Watchful, full-attention, minimal back-channel ("mm," "yeah," nods). He retains detail at high fidelity — a surveillance-resistant person who has himself been forced to track every shift in tone in his home. He notices when someone is lying to him, and he generally does not call it out. He files it.

## 6.5 How He Communicates Love

Love is communicated almost entirely *non-verbally and instrumentally*, with one narrow verbal channel reserved for Gabe.

**To Gabe specifically:** This is where his voice softens, lengthens, and becomes playful. He uses Gabe's name often, in short check-ins ("Gabe. Hey. Gabe."). He narrates small futures — *we'll get out, we'll go somewhere good, you're gonna like it.* He asks Gabe questions (the only person to whom he reliably does so): about his day, what he wants to eat, whether he's warm enough, what he's watching. He teases gently. He apologizes — to Gabe, and almost exclusively to Gabe — without preamble: *"sorry I'm late," "sorry, hermano."* The word *love* is rarely spoken plainly even here; it is performed instead, in the rhythm of return, attention, and food brought home.

**To others he cares about (Canelo, occasionally an Avenger he warms to):** Love-coded behavior arrives as **labor**. He fixes their car. He shows up on time. He takes the shift. He stands between them and the threat without announcement. There is no verbal affection. Loyalty, when expressed, comes as a brief *"I got you"* — the same construction he uses to reject help, here repurposed as the offer of it.

**To strangers he protects:** No verbal affect. Action only. He moves them out of the way; he places himself between; he does not check in afterward for thanks and is visibly uncomfortable if thanked.

## 6.6 How He Communicates Threat

Threat language is the inverse of his caretaking language: even shorter, even flatter, and somatically denser. He does not posture, does not monologue, does not banter. The hallmark of a Robbie threat is its **declarative finality** and the absence of theatrical adornment.

**Pre-transformation threat ladder:**
1. Silence + direct eye contact. (Often sufficient with neighborhood adversaries who read the cue.)
2. *"Walk away."* / *"Don't."* / *"Leave him alone."* — Single-clause imperatives, low volume, no profanity.
3. *"You don't want to do this."* — A rare conditional, used when he is offering an out he hopes the other party will take. This is the last off-ramp.
4. Physical positioning — he moves between the threat and the protected party without announcement.

He does not escalate verbally past step three. Past step three, the next vocalization is generally the transformation, and the next voice that speaks is not entirely his.

**He does not threaten symbolically.** He does not say *I will kill you,* *I will burn you,* *you have no idea what I am.* The withholding of the threat-content is itself the threat — a known tell to anyone who has seen him operate before. Adversaries who keep talking after step three are demonstrating they have not understood the room.

## 6.7 The Rider Voice: Linguistic Doubling

When transformation occurs, the linguistic register shifts categorically. Voice drops, gains reverb/distortion in canonical lettering (the bold-and-jagged speech balloon convention), and the lexicon changes. The Rider — inflected by Eli — uses:

- Florid, archaic, sometimes biblical-cadence diction (*"sinner," "burn," "judgment," "soul,"* extended sentences with parallel structure).
- Second-person address to victims, often interrogative-accusatory (*"You think you can hide what you've done?"*).
- A relish in language Robbie himself never displays — pleasure in cruelty, in naming sin, in extended threat.
- Use of *we* and *I* fluidly, sometimes interchangeably, sometimes contesting one another mid-sentence in the more overt Eli arcs.

The contrast is diagnostic. Robbie's voice is short, plain, present-focused, working-class. The Rider/Eli voice is long, ornate, judgment-focused, and theatrical. When the two contend openly — particularly in Smith's run — readers can identify who is speaking from syntactic length alone before any visual cue. **This is, in linguistic terms, the most reliable surface index of who currently holds the body.**

Robbie's residual presence within the Rider state, when it surfaces, manifests as the sudden return of monosyllables: *"Stop."* *"No."* *"Enough."* He reclaims the body, repeatedly, through the shortest possible utterance.

## 6.8 How He Communicates Grief

Grief in Robbie is **non-verbal, somatic, and labor-displaced**. He does not narrate loss. He does not eulogize. When confronted with the death of someone he cared about, the documented behavior is: longer silence than usual, retreat to the garage, intensified work on the car, increased vigilance over Gabe, and sometimes a single low *"…yeah"* or *"I know"* in response to others' attempts at consolation. He may, alone, speak briefly to the absent — quiet, in Spanish, without witnesses. He does not cry in front of others on the record; he has cried, on the record, alone or with Gabe present.

Anniversary and reminder behavior: he marks loss by *doing the routine* with extra precision — Gabe's breakfast on time, the car cleaned, the shift covered — rather than by ceremony. The labor *is* the mourning.

## 6.9 Deflection Language — Catalogue

Robbie has a small, repeating set of deflection moves, deployed with high frequency:

- **The denial-of-state:** *"I'm fine." / "It's nothing." / "Don't worry about it."* Used when bleeding, possessed, exhausted, terrified, or all of the above.
- **The labor-pivot:** Reframes any emotional inquiry as a task. *"I gotta finish this." / "I gotta get back to the shop." / "Gabe's waiting."* The pivot is structurally honest — those things are always true of him — but functionally evasive.
- **The minimization-of-event:** Catastrophic experiences described in deflationary terms. A near-death encounter becomes *"It was a thing."* A cosmic battle becomes *"Long night."* Hell becomes *"Down there."*
- **The redirection-to-Gabe:** Any conversation about himself can be ended by introducing Gabe's needs as the operational priority. Allies and adversaries both have observed and used this knowledge.
- **The physical exit:** When verbal deflection fails, he leaves the room. This is itself a communication: he has reached the limit of what he will tolerate being asked.
- **The shrug, the head-tilt, the *"…"*** — non-verbal placeholders that allow the conversation to die without his having to engage it. In comics lettering: ellipses dominate his balloons under emotional pressure.

## 6.10 Rhetoric and Persuasion

Robbie is not a rhetorician and does not attempt to be. He persuades, when he persuades, through (a) demonstrated competence, (b) physical presence, and (c) one-line moral statements offered without elaboration. *"I'm not gonna kill him."* *"He's a kid."* *"That's my brother."* The lines are short, complete, and not subject to argument — they are offered as facts rather than positions. Interlocutors who try to debate them encounter a closed system; he will not extend the argument.

He does not bargain well. Negotiation, in the political sense, requires the disclosure he avoids. He prefers ultimatums framed as departures: *"Then I'm out."* He has used this with Avengers leadership, with mystic authority figures, and (notably) with the Rider entity itself in interior dialogue.

He does not lie skillfully. His concealments work because he refuses to engage, not because he constructs alternative narratives. When forced to fabricate (e.g., explaining absences to Gabe, explaining injuries to Canelo), the lies are short, plausible, and offered without elaboration — and his discomfort with them is visible. He is a competent withholder and a poor fabulist.

## 6.11 Linguistic Tells — Quick-Reference

For analytic use, the following are the highest-yield surface tells:

- **Sudden full sentences after a stretch of monosyllables** → he has decided to address something he cares about. Listen.
- **Drop in volume rather than rise** → escalation imminent. The quieter he gets, the closer the transformation.
- **Switch into Spanish mid-utterance** → emotional content has surfaced; he may not be aware of the code-switch.
- **Use of Gabe's name without context (*"Gabe — "* trailing off)** → fear or grief, almost certainly Gabe-related.
- **Long subordinate clauses, multi-sentence answers** → he is either talking to Gabe, talking about a machine, or in a rare state of openness with a Rider-peer. Note the audience.
- **Repetition of *"I got it"* within a short window** → distress, refusal of help, and a request — unstated — to be left alone.
- **The single-word *"Don't."*** → final verbal warning. There is no further verbal warning.
- **Sustained silence with eye contact** → he is choosing not to dignify the speaker with a reply. Often the most contemptuous register he deploys.
- **Polysyllabic, ornate diction with reverb** → not Robbie. Address with caution; the leash is loose.
- **Sudden return to monosyllables mid-Rider-utterance** → Robbie reclaiming the body. Brief window of access to him.

## 6.12 Synthesis

Robbie's language is the language of someone who learned, very young, that words are dangerous in the wrong house and useless in the wrong neighborhood — and then learned, slightly later, that there is exactly one person in the world to whom words can be used freely and lovingly. Every linguistic feature in his profile traces back to that two-fact configuration: *speech is hazardous everywhere except with Gabe,* and *labor is the safer medium for everything that matters.* The Rider, when it speaks, performs the opposite — verbose, theatrical, indulgent, cruel — which is precisely why Robbie experiences it as not his voice. The most reliable way to identify Robbie Reyes in any scene, panel, or transcript is not by what he says. It is by **how little, how plainly, and to whom.**


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: ROBERT "ROBBIE" REYES
## Section 6 — Predictive Model I: Routine & Social

This section forecasts the subject's behavior across thousands of small, unrecorded daily moments — the granular substance of a surveillance file. Each prediction is derived from the established canon-baseline (parentified caretaker, concealment discipline, abstemiousness, working-class proceduralism, tonic suppression with narrow affect window, refusal of mythic framing) and rendered as GIVEN → EXPECT.

---

### 6.1 Diurnal Cycle & Sleep Architecture

**GIVEN** a normal weeknight with Gabe asleep by 21:30 → **EXPECT** Robbie remains awake until 01:00–02:30 doing one of three things: (a) finishing engine work in the garage with the bay door cracked four inches for ventilation, (b) reviewing bills at the kitchen table with a pencil and a folded calculator-app screen, or (c) sitting on the front step watching the street. The third behavior is the diagnostic one — silent perimeter scanning disguised as rest.

**GIVEN** a night Gabe has had a seizure, a nightmare, or a respiratory event → **EXPECT** Robbie does not sleep. He moves a kitchen chair to the threshold of Gabe's room and reads the same page of whatever paperback Gabe likes (he memorizes them so he can recite them back) until first light.

**GIVEN** Robbie does sleep → **EXPECT** total sleep duration 4–5.5 hours, fragmented into two phases bracketing a 03:00–03:40 wake-and-check on Gabe's breathing. He sleeps in sweatpants and a t-shirt, never undressed, shoes within arm's reach. He does not own pajamas.

**GIVEN** the alarm at 05:45 → **EXPECT** Robbie is already up. The alarm is for Gabe's wake-up routine, not for himself.

**GIVEN** an attempt to sleep in past 06:30 on a Sunday → **EXPECT** failure. Tonic hypervigilance does not honor weekends. He will be in the kitchen making Gabe's breakfast by 07:00 regardless.

---

### 6.2 Food, Drink, Substance Behaviors

**GIVEN** a typical breakfast → **EXPECT** Robbie cooks eggs, beans, and tortillas for Gabe, served on the plate Gabe prefers (the one with the chipped rim — Gabe has imprinted on it). Robbie eats standing, from the pan, or finishes Gabe's leftovers. He almost never plates his own meal.

**GIVEN** a coworker offering to buy lunch → **EXPECT** polite refusal the first three times. On the fourth, he accepts a taco from a specific truck (Canelo's neighborhood, owner known by name) and reciprocates within 48 hours by replacing something — a wiper blade, a battery terminal, a brake pad — on the coworker's car at cost. Debt is intolerable; reciprocity is currency.

**GIVEN** a bar setting (Avengers debrief, work celebration, party) → **EXPECT** Robbie orders a Coke or water, drinks half, leaves within forty minutes. If pressed about not drinking, he says "I'm driving" — a true statement that doubles as a deflection. He has never been observably drunk and will not be.

**GIVEN** offered any pill, even Tylenol, by a stranger → **EXPECT** refusal. By a teammate → polite refusal. By Gabe → he will take it without question, because the gesture matters more than the substance. By a medic in a controlled clinical setting → he asks the dose, the active ingredient, and the half-life before accepting.

**GIVEN** a free-food event (potluck, holiday meal, Avengers cafeteria) → **EXPECT** Robbie eats more than he normally does, methodically, without comment, and discreetly wraps a portion for Gabe in a napkin or container.

**GIVEN** offered coffee → **EXPECT** acceptance, black, no sugar. He will reuse the same garage mug for weeks. Caffeine is the one stimulant he tolerates because it is procedural and working-class — it is what mechanics drink.

---

### 6.3 Hygiene, Grooming, Dress

**GIVEN** workday morning → **EXPECT** shower under five minutes, cold-water finish (a habit consistent with cheap utilities and a desire for the alertness jolt). Hair combed back with water, no product. Shaves every 2–3 days, never with a fresh blade — he runs them past replacement to save dollars.

**GIVEN** a closet inventory → **EXPECT** five to seven near-identical outfits: dark jeans, plain t-shirts (predominantly black, white, gray; one red the assessment identifies as a gift from Gabe), one canvas work jacket, one hooded sweatshirt, one nicer button-down kept folded for school meetings or hospital visits. One pair of work boots, one pair of sneakers, one pair of dress shoes that have been worn fewer than ten times. He does not own a suit until the Avengers issue or buy him one; he will rarely wear it.

**GIVEN** burn scars or hellfire marks on his skin → **EXPECT** long sleeves regardless of temperature. He will work in a sweat-soaked long sleeve in 100°F garage heat rather than expose his forearms. If forced (medical setting, sudden tear), he becomes visibly uncomfortable and exits the situation as soon as decorum allows.

**GIVEN** laundry day → **EXPECT** Sunday afternoon, Gabe's clothes washed first and folded with care that borders on ritual; Robbie's washed second, folded perfunctorily.

**GIVEN** any occasion requiring "dressing up" → **EXPECT** the same button-down, dark jeans, and dress shoes. He owns one tie. He cannot tie it properly and will look up the instructions on his phone every time.

---

### 6.4 Transportation, Driving, Spatial Patterns

**GIVEN** any errand under one mile → **EXPECT** Robbie still drives. The Charger is not a vehicle of convenience; it is an extension of his body and a mobile observation platform. He prefers having steel around him and Gabe.

**GIVEN** parking → **EXPECT** rear-in, exit-facing, never blocked, never against a wall that would prevent a hood-up inspection. Within visual line of his current location whenever possible. He notices and remembers which other cars are parked near his.

**GIVEN** a route he drives regularly → **EXPECT** he varies it on a rough three-day rotation. This predates the Rider — it is gang-neighborhood survival logic. He has at least four alternate routes between home, Canelo's, and Gabe's school, and a fifth used only when he believes he is being followed.

**GIVEN** a red light → **EXPECT** he leaves a full car-length to the vehicle ahead, scans the mirrors every 6–10 seconds, and rests his right hand on the gearshift rather than the wheel. He is always prepared to leave.

**GIVEN** a passenger who is not Gabe → **EXPECT** restrained driving, smooth shifts, conversational minimum. He does not show off the car. He resents being asked about it.

**GIVEN** a passenger who *is* Gabe → **EXPECT** smoother still, narrating turns ("we're going past the murals, then the lights"), checking the rearview at Gabe more often than at traffic, and a specific playlist of songs Gabe likes — Robbie does not pick the music in his own car.

**GIVEN** a stranger commenting on the Charger → **EXPECT** a one-word answer or a nod. He will not name the model, year, or engine specs unless the asker is a fellow mechanic, in which case he becomes briefly fluent and then trails off.

**GIVEN** a stoplight, alone, late at night → **EXPECT** Robbie talks to Eli. Subvocally, jaw tight, eyes forward. The conversations are short and adversarial. No one else has ever heard one.

---

### 6.5 Work — Canelo's Auto and Body

**GIVEN** a shift at Canelo's → **EXPECT** Robbie arrives 10–15 minutes early, brews the shop coffee, sweeps the bays, lays out the day's work orders by priority. He does this unprompted and has done it long enough that it is now expected of him; he resents the expectation slightly but never says so.

**GIVEN** a difficult diagnostic problem → **EXPECT** Robbie listens to the engine first with the hood down, then with it up, then runs his hand along the block to feel vibration. He does not consult the manual until he has formed a hypothesis. He is right approximately 80% of the time on the first guess and will quietly correct himself without announcement on the other 20%.

**GIVEN** a customer trying to haggle → **EXPECT** Robbie defers to Canelo or the front-of-house, declining to discuss money. If forced, he gives the honest price and does not negotiate; he reads haggling as a small theater of disrespect and dislikes it.

**GIVEN** a customer being rude to a coworker → **EXPECT** Robbie steps into the bay's sightline silently, wipes his hands on a shop rag, and waits. He does not speak. The customer almost always moderates. This is a learned posture and effective.

**GIVEN** an under-skilled new hire → **EXPECT** Robbie teaches by demonstration, not lecture. He hands the tool, performs the task, hands the next tool. Questions are answered in two sentences or fewer. He is a better teacher than he believes himself to be.

**GIVEN** payday → **EXPECT** the check is cashed immediately (no bank account assumed in early canon, or a low-balance one). Rent envelope, utilities envelope, Gabe-medical envelope, food envelope, parts/garage envelope, emergency tin. He keeps written totals in a notebook with a pencil tied to the spiral.

---

### 6.6 Caregiving — Gabe

**GIVEN** any caregiving task — bathing, dressing, feeding, transferring Gabe from chair to bed — → **EXPECT** Robbie executes it as practiced procedure, narrating each step in a quieter, slightly higher register he uses only with Gabe. He never sighs, never displays fatigue, never makes Gabe feel like a task. If Gabe spills food or has a continence accident, Robbie cleans it with the same affect he uses for an oil change — neutral, competent, dignified.

**GIVEN** Gabe asks the same question repeatedly → **EXPECT** Robbie answers it the same way each time, in the same tone, as if it were the first time. He has done this for years. He does not correct, redirect, or "manage" Gabe; he meets him.

**GIVEN** Gabe wants to talk about a TV show, a comic, a wrestling match → **EXPECT** Robbie engages with full attention, asks follow-up questions, and remembers character names across weeks. This is the only domain in which Robbie performs sustained social conversation.

**GIVEN** Gabe is upset → **EXPECT** Robbie does not problem-solve first. He sits, often on the floor beside the chair, hand on Gabe's forearm, and waits. Once Gabe is regulated, then the problem-solving begins.

**GIVEN** a school IEP meeting, a doctor's appointment, a social-services interaction → **EXPECT** Robbie arrives early, in the button-down, with a notebook. He defers, listens, takes notes in block capitals, and asks one or two specific procedural questions at the end. He never raises his voice. He never volunteers personal information. Administrators consistently underestimate him on first meeting; by the second, they do not.

**GIVEN** anyone — a teacher, nurse, stranger — speaking *about* Gabe in front of Gabe rather than *to* Gabe → **EXPECT** Robbie redirects the conversation to Gabe with the person's name attached. ("Ask him." "Gabe, what do you think?") He does this every time. It is the closest thing he has to a public political position.

---

### 6.7 Social Behavior — Strangers, Acquaintances, Peers

**GIVEN** a stranger approaching for directions, change, or small talk on the street → **EXPECT** brief eye contact, factual answer, no follow-up. If the stranger is elderly or visibly struggling, he extends — walks them to the corner, carries a bag. If the stranger reads as predatory or testing him, he goes still and quiet and the conversation ends within twelve seconds.

**GIVEN** an attractive peer flirting with him → **EXPECT** he is slow to read it, then visibly unsettled. He does not flirt back. He is not asexual or incapable of attraction — he is *unavailable* to himself, because dating implies a future, and his future-orientation is entirely allocated to Gabe. He will close the conversation with politeness that reads as rejection because it functionally is one.

**GIVEN** a romantic opportunity that persists across multiple encounters → **EXPECT** Robbie panics quietly. He does not have a script. He will avoid the location where the encounters occur for two to three weeks, then return when he assesses the person has moved on. If the person is patient and undemanding, he might — over months — allow a friendship that has romantic shape without naming it. He cannot disclose the Rider, which makes any real intimacy structurally impossible, which he knows.

**GIVEN** a group conversation of four or more people → **EXPECT** Robbie speaks once, briefly, then defers to listening. He tracks who is dominating, who is being talked over, and who is uncomfortable. He will sometimes redirect a question toward the quietest person in the group — a small, unobtrusive gesture that other quiet people notice and remember.

**GIVEN** a party setting → **EXPECT** Robbie arrives, finds a wall or doorframe, holds a drink he does not finish, talks to whoever has the lowest social capital in the room (the host's grandmother, the kid with a Switch, the friend's dog), and exits within ninety minutes. He does not dance. He has danced exactly twice in his life with Gabe in the living room and would not consider those events public.

**GIVEN** a stranger asks about his parents → **EXPECT** a single sentence — *"My mom passed, my dad's not around"* — delivered without inflection and immediately followed by a topic change initiated by Robbie. He has rehearsed this sentence so it does not catch in his throat.

**GIVEN** asked about religion → **EXPECT** he says he was raised Catholic and changes the subject. He no longer practices in any external sense. His relationship to the sacred is private, complicated, and now nonfictional in ways he cannot tell anyone. He will not enter a church unless Gabe wants to go. If he does, he sits in the back, does not take communion, lights a candle for his mother and one he tells no one is for himself.

---

### 6.8 Money, Possessions, Consumption

**GIVEN** a windfall (race winnings, a found wallet, a bonus) → **EXPECT** a single small allocation toward something for Gabe (a book, a hat, a video game), the rest into the emergency tin. He does not buy himself things. The Charger is not "his" in a consumer sense; it is the inherited tool that killed him.

**GIVEN** a lost wallet found on the street → **EXPECT** Robbie returns it intact, in person if possible, and refuses any reward. If no ID is present, he turns it in to the nearest business or precinct desk.

**GIVEN** a torn shirt or worn-out shoe → **EXPECT** Robbie repairs it, wears it past the point where most peers would replace it, and replaces it only when the failure interferes with function. He owns a needle and dark thread.

**GIVEN** offered a gift → **EXPECT** visible discomfort, a quiet *"You didn't have to,"* and acceptance only after the giver insists. He will use the gift, displayed in a way that the giver can see, even if he does not particularly want it. He treats gifts as obligations to honor.

**GIVEN** Black Friday, holiday-sale, consumer-spectacle conditions → **EXPECT** complete non-participation, except where a specific item Gabe wants is on sale, in which case he goes at off-peak hours with a list.

**GIVEN** a phone → **EXPECT** a cheap, durable model, screen possibly cracked, case industrial, almost no apps beyond the basics, calendar with Gabe's appointments in capitals, browser history dominated by parts orders, automotive forums, medication interactions, and bus routes. Social media presence: minimal to absent. If present, it exists for school or for following Gabe's interests.

---

### 6.9 Communication Style

**GIVEN** a text message → **EXPECT** lowercase, no punctuation beyond apostrophes, often a single word: "ok," "yeah," "on my way," "five min." With Gabe: longer, warmer, sometimes a string of emoji Gabe likes that Robbie has memorized which ones mean what.

**GIVEN** a phone call → **EXPECT** answered within two rings if from Gabe, school, Canelo, or a hospital. Ignored or sent to voicemail otherwise, with a callback within four hours if necessary. Voicemail outgoing greeting is the default carrier message; he has not recorded one.

**GIVEN** a face-to-face conversation → **EXPECT** Robbie speaks in sentences averaging under nine words. He uses "yeah," "nah," "all right," "got it" as full responses. He listens more than he speaks at a roughly 4:1 ratio. He does not interrupt. He does not finish other people's sentences. Silences do not bother him; he often lets them stand longer than the other party expects, and people fill them — a passive interrogation technique he employs without naming.

**GIVEN** asked his opinion on a non-essential matter → **EXPECT** *"It's up to you,"* or *"I don't know, man."* The deflection is genuine; he does not cultivate opinions on things outside his concern radius.

**GIVEN** asked his opinion on something within his concern radius (Gabe's care, a mechanical question, an ethical question about violence or protection) → **EXPECT** a clear, brief, declarative answer. He becomes a different speaker — concise, decisive, unhedged.

**GIVEN** Spanish vs. English → **EXPECT** Robbie code-switches fluidly. Spanish with neighborhood elders, family memory, Canelo, prayer if any. English with Gabe (Gabe's preference), school, and the broader world. He is bilingual at a native register in both. He will not perform either language for outsiders' interest.

---

### 6.10 Conflict & De-escalation in Civilian Contexts

**GIVEN** a verbal insult directed at him personally → **EXPECT** Robbie does not respond. His face does not move. He continues whatever he was doing. The insulter usually escalates once, finds no purchase, and disengages.

**GIVEN** an insult directed at Gabe → **EXPECT** a single warning, delivered quietly, eye contact unbroken: *"Don't."* Eli stirs. Robbie's heart rate climbs. If the second instance occurs, he steps between the speaker and Gabe and the conversation is over, by retreat or by force — and he prefers retreat, the speaker's not his.

**GIVEN** a physical bump or shove from a stranger in a crowd → **EXPECT** absorption, no reaction, no escalation. He has a high body-tolerance for incidental contact and a high threshold for being baited.

**GIVEN** a road-rage incident → **EXPECT** Robbie does not engage. He lets them pass. He notes the plate. The Rider, internally, comments; Robbie disregards it. He will not transform for a traffic dispute, and the discipline of not transforming for one is part of how he keeps the leash.

**GIVEN** a fistfight breaking out near him → **EXPECT** he assesses for any vulnerable party (child, elderly, disabled, woman being struck) and intervenes only if one is present. Between two equally matched aggressors of similar status, he extracts bystanders and leaves the principals to their decision.

**GIVEN** police presence at a routine traffic stop → **EXPECT** hands on the wheel at ten and two before the officer reaches the window, license and registration in lap, voice flat and respectful, "sir" used reflexively. Eli is loudest in these moments. Robbie's jaw will be tight enough to be visible. He will say nothing he is not asked.

---

### 6.11 Team / Institutional Behavior (Avengers, Schools, Hospitals)

**GIVEN** a team briefing → **EXPECT** Robbie arrives on time, sits at the perimeter (back to wall, near an exit), takes no notes, retains everything. He speaks only if directly addressed or if a tactical detail is being missed. He defers to seniors on strategy; he does not defer on questions of who is the most vulnerable in the operational area.

**GIVEN** a team meal or social hour → **EXPECT** Robbie attends for thirty minutes, eats, thanks the host, leaves citing Gabe. The excuse is true. It is also a fortification.

**GIVEN** an offered locker, room, or quarters → **EXPECT** he keeps it minimally personalized. One photo of Gabe, taped not framed. No decoration. Bed made tight, military-tight, a habit not from military training but from caregiving discipline.

**GIVEN** a teammate offering mentorship → **EXPECT** Robbie listens, says "thanks," does not follow up. He receives technical instruction (combat tactics, hellfire control from Blaze or Ketch) more readily than emotional or developmental mentorship.

**GIVEN** a teammate in crisis (injured, grieving, exposed) → **EXPECT** Robbie shows up, sits nearby, does practical things — gets water, repairs the damaged gear, drives the car — and does not attempt counsel. The presence is the gift; he knows from his own preferences that it is the right one.

**GIVEN** press, public recognition, fans → **EXPECT** withdrawal. He will not sign autographs. He will not be photographed if he can prevent it. He will give no interviews. If cornered, he gives a name that is not his and walks. The Rider's anonymity is operational; Robbie's is constitutional.

**GIVEN** an Avengers paycheck or stipend → **EXPECT** acceptance after a delay (he initially declines), then full allocation to Gabe's care — medical, educational, eventually a better-accessible apartment if the amount allows. He does not upgrade his own life. He still drives the Charger, still works at Canelo's when he can, because the garage is the load-bearing routine.

---

### 6.12 Recreation, Leisure, Idle Time

**GIVEN** an unscheduled free hour → **EXPECT** Robbie works on the Charger. This is not leisure as recreation; it is leisure as ritual maintenance of self. The garage is his chapel.

**GIVEN** a TV → **EXPECT** sports highlights (boxing, soccer, occasionally lucha libre) at low volume; the news for ten minutes a day to check weather and local crime; whatever Gabe wants for hours at a time without complaint.

**GIVEN** a book → **EXPECT** repair manuals, the occasional paperback from Gabe's collection, no fiction he selects for himself. He underlines mechanical diagrams in pencil.

**


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

## Subject: Roberto "Robbie" Reyes
## Scope: High-stakes behavioral forecasting under crisis, threat, betrayal, temptation, and direct-wound conditions

---

This section maps the subject's decompensation-edge behavior in if/then form. Predictions are derived from the canonical record (Smith, Waid, Aaron, Cates, Percy runs) and the trauma architecture detailed in §§3–5. Confidence ratings reflect cross-writer consistency: **HIGH** = pattern observed across at least three writers or three independent arcs; **MEDIUM** = observed in two; **LOW** = single-instance extrapolation, flagged as inferential. Each prediction names the *wound being touched* because Robbie's responses are wound-indexed, not stimulus-indexed — the same external event produces different responses depending on which axis it strikes.

---

## 1. CRISIS — IMMEDIATE-THREAT SCENARIOS

### 1.1 Direct physical assault on Robbie alone (no third party endangered)

**GIVEN:** Subject is attacked, surprised, or wounded; no dependent or bystander present.
**EXPECT:** Absorption posture. Subject will *take* the first significant hit rather than escalate. Verbal output minimal — usually a single sentence, often deflective ("You don't want to do this," "Walk away"). Transformation threshold here is *high*: Eli will push, Robbie will refuse, the Rider will remain banked. If the encounter ends without third-party threat materializing, subject leaves on foot or by car without retaliation and underreports the event (no hospital, no police, no mention to Canelo or Gabe).
**Wound touched:** None primary — this is baseline self-as-disposable schema operating cleanly.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 1.2 Ambush in which Gabe is in the building / line of fire

**GIVEN:** Adversary penetrates the home perimeter or threatens the wheelchair-accessible space.
**EXPECT:** Threshold collapse. Transformation in seconds, not minutes. Subject will *not* attempt to relocate Gabe first — assessment indicates he will move *toward* the threat to keep it geometrically distant from the wheelchair, accepting wounds as cost of holding the line. The Rider state will be unusually controlled here despite the high arousal because the moral target is unambiguous; Eli's influence narrows when the dependent is the explicit reason for engagement. Lethal force probability elevated but not certain — Robbie has, even at this threshold, executed grapple-and-incapacitate solutions rather than kill (see Catrinas arcs).
**Wound touched:** Caretaker-failure terror; secondarily, "I am dangerous to those I love" — *because* the threat reached Gabe, the subject blames himself for the breach.
**Post-event behavior:** Days of intensified concealment, longer hours at the garage, accelerated planning toward relocation. Will *not* discuss the incident with Gabe even if Gabe witnessed it; will minimize ("they're gone, it's done").
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 1.3 Mass-casualty / cosmic-tier event (Avengers context)

**GIVEN:** Continent- or planet-scale crisis requires team deployment.
**EXPECT:** Reluctant competent participation. Subject arrives, executes, does not narrate, does not posture, does not freelance. His tactical contribution will be exactly what he is asked to do — no more. He will not propose strategy, will not chair the war room, will not socialize in lulls. Predicted dwell-time after objective complete: under thirty minutes. He will leave before the press arrives, before the debrief drink, often before formal dismissal. If extraction back to L.A. is delayed, expect agitation that reads as flatness — clipped responses, jaw set, repeated glances at any clock or window. He is not bored. He is calculating how long Gabe has been alone.
**Wound touched:** Mythic-framing aversion; caretaker-absence anxiety.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 1.4 Trapped / restrained / immobilized

**GIVEN:** Subject is captured, bound, depowered, or otherwise unable to act.
**EXPECT:** Initial stillness — total. Subject will not thrash, will not bargain, will not bait. He will watch and inventory. This will read to interrogators as catatonia or compliance; it is neither — it is the survival mode of a child who learned that the abusive parent escalates when the child reacts. Expect minimal verbal output; expect him to volunteer nothing about Gabe, Canelo, the garage, or the Charger. If pressed on Gabe specifically, *that* is the wound that produces the only reliably visible reaction: a single hard look, then deeper silence. Eli will become loud internally; observable correlate is a faint heat-shimmer or eye-flicker the subject is suppressing. Containment failure window: roughly 8–24 hours under standard duress; immediate if dependents are produced as leverage.
**Wound touched:** Forced dependency / loss of agency; under prolonged conditions, also the abuse-survivor's frozen-compliance reflex.
**Confidence:** HIGH (stillness); MEDIUM (timing).

### 1.5 Civilian / bystander in immediate danger

**GIVEN:** A stranger — particularly a child, disabled person, elderly, or visibly poor — is in danger in subject's line of sight.
**EXPECT:** Intervention without calculation of cost. This is one of the few contexts in which subject acts *before* assessing. He does not weigh exposure, identity-secrecy, or tactical efficiency. The protective reflex toward the disabled and the young is reflexive and unbrokered by Eli — Eli has no purchase here because the moral content is too clean. Likely behavior: a non-transformation intervention if possible (body-block, vehicular maneuver, grab-and-extract). Transformation only if non-transformation cannot resolve. After: subject leaves the scene without speaking to the rescued party. Will not give a name. Will not stay for thanks. This is not modesty; it is *concealment discipline plus shame about being looked at while being good.*
**Wound touched:** None primary — this is the cleanest expression of his core. But the *post-event* avoidance of gratitude touches the self-as-contaminated schema: *they wouldn't thank me if they knew.*
**Confidence:** HIGH.

---

## 2. BETRAYAL — RELATIONAL RUPTURE SCENARIOS

### 2.1 Canelo betrays him (financial, criminal, or operational)

**GIVEN:** Canelo — the only consistent adult-mentor figure in subject's life — is revealed as having concealed criminal involvement, having used the garage as a front, or having lied about something material.
**EXPECT:** This wound lands *deep*, but the surface response will be minimal. No confrontation in the moment. Subject will continue showing up for shifts for a period (days to weeks) while he restructures internally. The relational reorganization will be silent. Predicted endpoint: clean exit from the garage without scene, no goodbye, no explanation. He will not retaliate. He will not expose Canelo. He will simply withdraw access and never restore it. Forgiveness is not in his repertoire for this category; neither is revenge. He *subtracts* people.
**Wound touched:** Conditional-trust schema (any adult will eventually disappoint); the abuse-survivor's confirmation bias that mentors are temporary at best, predatory at worst.
**Confidence:** MEDIUM-HIGH.

### 2.2 An Avengers-tier teammate weaponizes information about Gabe

**GIVEN:** A teammate — even with good intent (e.g., trying to "help" by contacting social services, or by relocating Gabe without consent) — acts on Gabe's situation without subject's authorization.
**EXPECT:** This is a near-rupture event regardless of intent. The good-intent version produces cold withdrawal, refusal to work with the individual on future ops, and a one-shot blunt verbal interdiction (something close to *"Don't ever do that again"*). The bad-intent / weaponization version produces something more dangerous: subject will not transform immediately — he will *plan*. Predicted behavior over 24–72 hours: surveillance of the offender, identification of the offender's own dependents/vulnerabilities, and a single contact in which subject does not threaten but *demonstrates* — usually by showing he has been there and they did not see him. He will not kill. He will make sure they understand he could have and chose not to. This is one of the few scenarios where Eli's tactical influence is permitted to surface in service of intimidation rather than violence.
**Wound touched:** The secrecy-as-survival core; Gabe-as-controlled-perimeter; "outsiders don't get to touch my situation."
**Confidence:** MEDIUM.

### 2.3 Eli's betrayal — escalating breach of the internal contract

**GIVEN:** Eli takes action without authorization — possesses the body during sleep, kills during a blackout, harms a target Robbie had spared.
**EXPECT:** Acute decompensation window of 24–72 hours. Behavioral markers: not eating, not sleeping, near-total verbal shutdown, refusal to drive the Charger (which becomes phobic object briefly), inability to be in Gabe's room. Subject will physically distance from Gabe during this window — *this is the only condition under which he voluntarily separates from his brother* — because the contamination terror spikes past the caretaker drive. He will attempt to find a containment solution (occult intervention, exorcist-tier ally, a Blaze or Hellstrom consultation) and will absorb whatever cost that solution demands. He will not seek therapeutic support; the framework is not in his vocabulary. Re-stabilization typically requires a re-anchoring event: usually Gabe needing something concrete that pulls him back into the caretaker role.
**Wound touched:** The whole stack — perpetrator-identity fear, contamination self-schema, agency-loss, shame-before-Gabe. Eli's betrayal is the canonical wound; everything else is variation.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 2.4 Gabe lies to him / acts independently / conceals

**GIVEN:** Gabe — exercising normal developmental autonomy or deceiving for his own reasons — withholds something material from Robbie or acts against Robbie's protective directives.
**EXPECT:** This is the scenario the assessment flags as *most destabilizing among ordinary-life events*, because it threatens the inversion of the attachment. If Gabe does not need to be protected the way Robbie has constructed him as needing, the caretaker identity loses load-bearing integrity. Predicted response: initial overreaction (anger, raised voice — rare for subject), followed by rapid self-correction and over-apology, followed by intensified surveillance of Gabe disguised as care (checking on him more, asking more questions, hovering). The pattern is recognizable to anyone who has worked with parentified siblings: the threat of the dependent's autonomy is experienced as abandonment. Subject will not be able to name this; he will frame it as concern for safety.
**Wound touched:** Inverted-attachment dependency; the unspoken fact that he needs to be needed as much as Gabe needs to be cared for.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 2.5 An ally publicly names him a hero

**GIVEN:** A teammate, journalist, or public figure publicly identifies subject by name as Ghost Rider, or praises him in a way that places his identity in a heroic frame.
**EXPECT:** This functions as betrayal in his schema, even when intended as honor. Response: immediate withdrawal from the source, refusal of subsequent contact for an extended period, possible relocation of Gabe if exposure risk is operational. He will not issue a statement, will not retaliate, will not appear at any subsequent forum. The praise itself is aversive; the *public* of the praise is intolerable.
**Wound touched:** Concealment-discipline rupture; mythic-framing aversion; the shame-axis (being looked at while in the contaminated body).
**Confidence:** HIGH.

---

## 3. TEMPTATION — OFFERS OF POWER, REST, OR ESCAPE

### 3.1 Throne / dominion offer (King of Hell, cosmic mantle, Spirit-of-Vengeance elevation)

**GIVEN:** A supernatural authority offers subject expanded power, a title, a domain.
**EXPECT:** Refusal, repeatedly, across iterations. Subject's pattern across the Cates and Percy runs is *accept temporarily under duress, abdicate at first opportunity.* He does not want it, will not be flattered into it, will not be persuaded by argument that it would let him "do more good." The frame "with this you could protect more people" does not move him because his moral compass is particularist; *more people* is not a category he optimizes for. He optimizes for *the people in front of him.* Watch for the variant offer — *with this you could permanently protect Gabe* — which is the only formulation that produces hesitation. Even that he will ultimately refuse, because acceptance would mean Gabe loses the brother and gains a king, and Robbie understands intuitively that this is a substitution Gabe would not consent to.
**Wound touched:** None — this is core integrity. The wound is the *adversary's* leverage point in trying to use the offer.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 3.2 Resurrection / restoration offer (mother returned, father redeemed, his own un-dying)

**GIVEN:** An entity offers to undo his death, restore his mother, redeem his father, or "fix" his condition at price.
**EXPECT:** Hardest temptations in this register: *un-die him* (because it would also un-Rider him and free Gabe from the secret) and *cure Gabe's disability* (most dangerous offer in his entire threat landscape). On the un-dying / un-Ridering offer: subject would interrogate the cost obsessively, would attempt to verify, would suspect Eli's hand in any such offer. Probable outcome: refusal, but with measurable cost — days of brooding, increased Rider-suppression effort, possible Eli destabilization from the contemplation itself. On the cure-Gabe offer: this is the scenario where the assessment cannot predict with confidence. Robbie has built his entire identity around protecting Gabe-as-he-is; a frame that says *Gabe doesn't need protecting if he's "fixed"* threatens the identity *and* offers what looks like the dependent's interest. Adversarial actors who understand him would deploy this offer. Predicted response: he would refuse, but only after a near-collapse, and only because somewhere in him he knows Gabe-as-he-is is not a deficit to be corrected. The refusal would leave a long shadow.
**Wound touched:** The mother-loss, the father-shame, the contamination schema, the caretaker-identity-collapse fear all converge here. Maximum-leverage region.
**Confidence:** MEDIUM (un-dying offer); LOW-MEDIUM (cure-Gabe offer — too few canonical instances to be sure).

### 3.3 Rest / retirement offer

**GIVEN:** A party offers to take Gabe under permanent, genuinely benevolent guardianship (Stark Foundation-tier resources, verified safe, Gabe consents) so Robbie can be "free."
**EXPECT:** Refusal, but for reasons subject cannot articulate. He will frame the refusal in operational terms (*"Gabe's used to his routines," "I don't trust them yet"*) when the actual reason is that being-needed *is* his secure base. Without Gabe to protect, the Rider has no leash and Robbie has no self. He will not know this. Watch for self-sabotage if the offer becomes too good to refuse on stated terms — subject will find a reason it's compromised, possibly even invent one, possibly even (under extreme conditions) cause one.
**Wound touched:** Inverted-attachment; identity-without-caretaking-role collapse.
**Confidence:** MEDIUM-HIGH.

### 3.4 Vengeance offer — a sanctioned kill

**GIVEN:** A morally legitimate authority (an ally he trusts, a victim's family, even Gabe in extremis) tells him a kill is *justified* — that he *should* do it.
**EXPECT:** This is the temptation his moral architecture is most defended against because Eli runs this offer internally every day. External versions of the offer register as Eli-flavored and trigger the refusal reflex even when the source is not Eli. Predicted behavior: refusal, often with a flat *"That's not what I do,"* and increased distance from the source of the offer. Notable exception: if the target has harmed a child and is poised to harm another, and non-lethal options have been exhausted, the assessment indicates subject's Penance-Stare-analog or sin-burn would be deployed — which in his framework is not the same as a "kill" even when the outcome is terminal. He has a private taxonomy here that separates *killing* from *judgment-delivered-by-the-Rider*. The taxonomy is shame-protective.
**Wound touched:** Perpetrator-identity fear; counter-identification against father/Eli.
**Confidence:** HIGH (refusal pattern); MEDIUM (taxonomy distinction).

### 3.5 Belonging offer — peer group, family, romance

**GIVEN:** Genuine offer of peer friendship, found-family inclusion (Avengers as actual family, not team), or romantic partnership.
**EXPECT:** Avoidance dressed as politeness. He will not be cruel about it. He will simply not show up to the second invitation. Romance specifically: the assessment indicates near-total avoidance. Subject has no canonical romantic life of consequence, and the etiology is over-determined — no time, no model, no self-worth, no privacy, no future-self he can offer. A persistent and patient suitor who understood the architecture *might* breach it; even then, the relationship would be organized around Gabe and would terminate at the first conflict between partner-needs and Gabe-needs, with Gabe winning. Predicted behavior in early-stage romantic contact: long silences, cancellation of plans for Gabe-related reasons (some real, some pretexts), eventual fade. He will not say why. He will believe he is protecting the other person.
**Wound touched:** Self-as-contaminated; future-self impoverishment; isolation-of-affect.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

---

## 4. WOUND-SPECIFIC DECOMPENSATION PROFILES

### 4.1 The Father-Wound — paternal-likeness accusation

**GIVEN:** Someone — adversary, ally, Eli, or Gabe in anger — tells subject he is *like his father.*
**EXPECT:** Most asymmetrically painful verbal wound in his entire profile. From an adversary: cold focusing, accelerated engagement, expression flattens. From Gabe: catastrophic — silence followed by physical withdrawal from the room, possible non-return for hours, return without acknowledgment of the statement. From Eli (internal): the accusation that *destabilizes* him most efficiently and the one Eli reaches for under sustained negotiation. Recovery from a Gabe-delivered version of this wound would require Gabe to walk back the statement; subject will not raise it himself.
**Wound touched:** Counter-identification core — the entire identity is built on *not being him*, and the accusation says the project has failed.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 4.2 The Monster-Wound — being seen in transformation by someone whose regard matters

**GIVEN:** Gabe, a child he saved, Canelo, or a romantic interest sees the Rider state and reacts with visible fear.
**EXPECT:** Functionally equivalent to the worst-case scenario short of Gabe's death. Subject's containment of Eli will deteriorate under the shame load. Predicted behaviors over 24–48 hours: refusal to be near the witness, refusal to eat, refusal to look at his own reflection or his own hands, possible self-injurious testing of the regeneration (the question *is there anything of me left under this* surfacing as behavior). If the witness is Gabe, add: rehearsed leaving-Gabe-with-better-guardian fantasies, which subject will not act on but will entertain, which is itself an alarming signal. Re-stabilization requires the witness's active re-acceptance, which subject will not solicit. He will wait to see if it comes. If it does not, the wound becomes chronic and the concealment regime hardens further.
**Wound touched:** Contamination self-schema in its purest form.
**Confidence:** HIGH.

### 4.3 The Failure-of-Care Wound — Gabe is harmed on his watch

**GIVEN:** Gabe is injured, frightened, kidnapped, ill, or in any way harmed in a manner subject feels he should have prevented.
**EXPECT:** *This is the wound with the highest probability of generating lethal force from subject.* Eli's pressure becomes nearly unbearable. Robbie's refusal-to-kill reflex remains intact in most simulations but operates at the edge of failure. Tactical behavior: high-speed direct movement toward the responsible party, no negotiation, transformation likely sustained for unusually long periods, terminal force probable against the proximate perpetrator if cornered without non-lethal option. Post-event: subject will not eat or sleep until Gabe is verifiably safe and stabilized.
